\section{The Heisenberg Rosetta Stone}
\label{sec:rosetta-stone}
\index{Rosetta Stone|textbf}
\index{Heisenberg algebra!Rosetta Stone|textbf}
\index{Swiss-cheese operad!Heisenberg example|textbf}

The Heisenberg algebra~$\cH_k$ has shadow depth $r_{\max} = 2$ (class~G), so $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$ terminates at degree~2. Every projection is computed in closed form: curvature $\kappa = k$, spectral $R$-matrix $R(z) = e^{k\hbar/z}$, genus tower $F_g = k\,\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$. The line category is $\cC_{\mathrm{line}} \simeq \cH_{-k}\text{-mod}$ (via $Y(\mathfrak{u}(1)) \simeq \cH_{-k}$); the derived center is the free boson bulk; the complementarity involution $k \mapsto -k$ closes the triangle (note: the Koszul dual $\cH_k^! = \Sym^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$ is not $\cH_{-k}$).

The Lagrangian self-intersection
$\mathfrak{S}_b = L \times_X L$ is one-dimensional with
transversal crossing. Koszulness ($m_{k \ge 3} = 0$) is the
statement that this intersection is clean:
$H_*^{BM}(\mathfrak{S}_b)$ is one-dimensional in each stratum.
The single scalar~$k$ determines the full Heisenberg package:
the direct algebraic data (algebra, $R$-matrix, genus tower,
PVA) and, through the abelian line-side comparison, the
open-colour dual and semisimple line model, because the
Lagrangian is concentrated.

The present section proves this for the Heisenberg algebra
$\cH_k$ by explicit computation. The results are neither deep
nor difficult; they are \emph{explicit}, and the explicitness
carries information that no amount of abstract machinery can supply.
The Heisenberg algebra has a single generator~$J$, a single
OPE pole of order~$2$, and no composite fields. These three
simplifications (one generator, one pole order, no composites) make
every step checkable by hand. Yet none of the five main theorems
of Volume~I becomes trivial: bar-cobar adjunction (Theorem~A),
inversion (Theorem~B), complementarity (Theorem~C), the modular
characteristic (Theorem~D), and Hochschild cohomology (Theorem~H)
are all instantiated here with full content.

The section has five parts:
\S\ref{subsec:rosetta-e1-coalgebra} identifies the bar complex
as an $E_1$ dg coassociative coalgebra;
\S\ref{subsec:rosetta-operations} computes all higher operations
and verifies that they vanish;
\S\ref{subsec:rosetta-pva} extracts the Poisson vertex algebra
on cohomology; \S\ref{subsec:rosetta-genus1} exhibits
curvature at genus~$1$; and \S\ref{subsec:rosetta-bridge}
assembles a dictionary mapping every bar-complex datum to both a
Volume~I theorem and a Volume~II physical identification.


% ================================================================
\subsection{The $E_1$ coalgebra structure on the bar complex}
\label{subsec:rosetta-e1-coalgebra}
\index{bar complex!E_1 coalgebra structure!Heisenberg}
% ================================================================

We fix notation. Let $V = \bC \cdot J$ be the one-dimensional
vector space spanned by the Heisenberg current, let $k \in \bC$
be the level, and let $\cH_k$ be the corresponding Heisenberg
chiral algebra with OPE
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rosetta-heisenberg-ope}
J(z)\, J(w) \;\sim\; \frac{k}{(z - w)^2}.
\end{equation}
The bar complex $\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k)$ is the cofree
conilpotent coalgebra on the desuspension $s^{-1}\overline{\cH}_k$,
equipped with the bar differential $d_{\barB}$ constructed from
OPE residues on the Fulton--MacPherson compactification.
Concretely, a bar element of tensor degree~$n$ lives on
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rosetta-bar-element-space}
\barB^n(\cH_k) \;=\;
(s^{-1}\overline{\cH}_k)^{\otimes n}
\;\otimes\;
\Omega^{\bullet}\bigl(\overline{\Conf}_{n+1}(X)\bigr),
\end{equation}
where $\overline{\Conf}_{n+1}(X) = \FM_{n+1}(X)$ is the
Fulton--MacPherson compactification and the logarithmic forms
$\eta_{ij} = d\log(z_i - z_j)$ provide the propagators.

\begin{theorem}[$E_1$ coalgebra structure on the Heisenberg bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:rosetta-e1-coalgebra}
\index{bar complex!E_1 coalgebra structure!Heisenberg}
The geometric bar complex $\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k)$ is an
$E_1$ dg coassociative coalgebra with:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item bar differential $d_{\barB}$
 \textup{(}residues on collision divisors of\/ $\FM_n(\bC)$\textup{)},
\item deconcatenation coproduct $\Delta$
 \textup{(}ordered splitting on $\Conf_n^{<}(\bR)$\textup{)},
\end{enumerate}
satisfying the coderivation identity
$\Delta \circ d_{\barB} = (d_{\barB} \otimes \id + \id \otimes d_{\barB}) \circ \Delta$.
The $\SCchtop$ structure emerges at the level of the chiral
derived center: the pair
$\bigl(C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k, \cH_k),\; \cH_k\bigr)$
is the $\SCchtop$ datum \textup{(}bulk acting on boundary\textup{)}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The proof has four steps, establishing the $E_1$ dg coassociative
coalgebra structure.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{Step~1: Closed color.}\enspace
The bar differential $d_{\barB}$ is the coderivation of the
cofree coalgebra $T^c(s^{-1}\overline{\cH}_k)$ determined by
the OPE residue. For the Heisenberg algebra, the only nonvanishing
component is the binary one:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rosetta-dbar-binary}
d_{\barB}\bigl[s^{-1}J \,|\, s^{-1}J\bigr]
\;=\;
\int_{E_{12}}
 J(z_1)\, J(z_2) \cdot \omega_{12}^{\FM}
\;=\;
J_{(1)}J
\;=\; k.
\end{equation}
The bar differential is the Stokes boundary operator on $\FM_2(\bC)$:
integration over the exceptional divisor $E_{12} \cong S^1$ in
the FM blowup extracts the mode product $J_{(1)}J = k$ from
the double pole $k/(z_1 - z_2)^2$.

The nilpotence $d_{\barB}^2 = 0$ is the Arnold relation
on $\FM_3(\bC)$. The three codimension-$1$ boundary strata of
$\FM_3(\bC)$ are the collision divisors $\colldiv{1}{2}$,
$\colldiv{2}{3}$, and $\colldiv{1}{3}$.
On these strata, the logarithmic $2$-form
$\eta_{12} \wedge \eta_{23}$ restricts to the Arnold relation
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rosetta-arnold}
[\eta_{12} \wedge \eta_{23}]
\;+\;
[\eta_{23} \wedge \eta_{13}]
\;+\;
[\eta_{13} \wedge \eta_{12}]
\;=\; 0
\end{equation}
in $H^2(\FM_3(\bC))$.
Each summand contributes a residue to $d_{\barB}^2$, and their
sum vanishes by exactness. For the Heisenberg algebra, this
computation produces $d_{\barB}^2[s^{-1}J \,|\, s^{-1}J \,|\, s^{-1}J]
= k \cdot (\text{Arnold sum}) = 0$.

The closed-color structure is thus a dg coalgebra
$(\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k), d_{\barB})$, with $d_{\barB}$
built from $\FM_n(\bC)$. This is holomorphic factorization.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{Step~2: Open color.}\enspace
The deconcatenation coproduct
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rosetta-delta}
\Delta\bigl[a_1 \,|\, \cdots \,|\, a_n\bigr]
\;=\;
\sum_{i=0}^{n}
\bigl[a_1 \,|\, \cdots \,|\, a_i\bigr]
\;\otimes\;
\bigl[a_{i+1} \,|\, \cdots \,|\, a_n\bigr]
\end{equation}
is coassociative by construction: it is the tensor coalgebra
coproduct. The ordering of tensor factors corresponds to the
ordering of points $t_1 < t_2 < \cdots < t_n$ on $\bR$;
splitting at position~$i$ is cutting the interval
$[t_1, t_n] \subset \bR$ at the gap between $t_i$ and $t_{i+1}$.
The ordered configuration space $\Conf_n^{<}(\bR)$ is
contractible (it is an open simplex
$\{t_1 < \cdots < t_n\} \cong \bR^{n-1}_{> 0}$), so the
$\Eone$-structure on $\Conf_n(\bR)$ contracts to
$\Ass$-structure: $\Delta$ is strictly coassociative,
not merely $\Eone$-coassociative up to homotopy.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{Step~3: Compatibility.}\enspace
The coderivation property
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rosetta-compatibility}
\Delta \circ d_{\barB}
\;=\;
(\id \otimes d_{\barB} \;+\; d_{\barB} \otimes \id)
\circ \Delta
\end{equation}
asserts that $d_{\barB}$ is a coderivation of $\Delta$.
We verify this on bar elements of degree~$2$. The left-hand side
gives
\[
\Delta\bigl(d_{\barB}[s^{-1}J \,|\, s^{-1}J]\bigr)
\;=\;
\Delta(k)
\;=\;
k \otimes [] + [] \otimes k,
\]
where $[]$ denotes the empty bar element (the coaugmentation).
The right-hand side gives
\[
(d_{\barB} \otimes \id + \id \otimes d_{\barB})\bigl(
 [] \otimes [s^{-1}J \,|\, s^{-1}J]
 \;+\;
 [s^{-1}J] \otimes [s^{-1}J]
 \;+\;
 [s^{-1}J \,|\, s^{-1}J] \otimes []
\bigr).
\]
The middle term $[s^{-1}J] \otimes [s^{-1}J]$ contributes nothing
because $d_{\barB}$ on a single element $[s^{-1}J]$ requires a
binary collision, which is absent. The first and last terms
contribute $[] \otimes k + k \otimes []$, matching the left-hand side.

Geometrically,
the collision divisors $\colldiv{i}{j} \subset \FM_n(\bC)$
parametrize collisions in the holomorphic direction, while the
splitting $\Delta$ acts in the topological direction on $\bR$.
These directions are independent in the product
$\FM_n(\bC) \times \Conf_n^{<}(\bR)$: a collision
$z_i \to z_j$ in $\bC$ does not merge the corresponding
points $t_i, t_j \in \bR$. The residue operation (extracting the
singular part of the OPE along $\colldiv{i}{j}$) therefore
commutes with the splitting operation (cutting the interval at a
gap in the $\bR$-ordering).

\medskip
\noindent\textit{Step~4: Coherences.}\enspace
The $E_1$ coalgebra structure requires homotopy-coherent
compatibility between $d_{\barB}$ and $\Delta$.
For $(\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k),
d_{\barB}, \Delta)$, all coherence conditions are automatically
satisfied at the strict level:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*)]
\item the closed-color differential $d_{\barB}$ is strictly
 square-zero (Arnold relation, not merely $\Ainf$-null);
\item the open-color coproduct $\Delta$ is strictly coassociative
 (tensor coalgebra, not merely $\Eone$-coassociative);
\item compatibility~\eqref{eq:rosetta-compatibility} holds strictly,
 not up to a homotopy parametrized by the $W$-construction.
\end{enumerate}
The higher coherences between $\FM_n(\bC)$ and
$\Conf_n^{<}(\bR)$ are trivial because the product
$\FM_n(\bC) \times \Conf_n^{<}(\bR)$ decomposes: the FM operad is
formal at genus~$0$ (Kontsevich), so all higher coherences on the
holomorphic factor vanish; the ordered configuration space on $\bR$
is contractible, so all higher coherences on the topological factor
vanish; and the product structure admits no mixed higher coherences.
\end{proof}


% ================================================================
\subsection{Reading off the higher operations}
\label{subsec:rosetta-operations}
\index{higher operations!from bar complex}
\index{Heisenberg algebra!higher operations}
% ================================================================

The $E_1$ coalgebra structure on the bar complex classifies the twisting morphisms that encode all
$\Ainf$ operations of the chiral algebra. The following
proposition makes the extraction explicit.

\begin{proposition}[Higher operations from bar elements;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:rosetta-operations}
\index{A-infinity operations@$\Ainf$ operations!from bar complex}
The $\Ainf$ operations $m_k$ of a chiral algebra $\cA$ are
recovered from the bar complex by the formula
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rosetta-mk-extraction}
m_k(a_1, \ldots, a_k;\, \lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1})
\;=\;
\text{coefficient of }
s^{-1}a_1 \otimes \cdots \otimes s^{-1}a_k
\text{ in }
d_{\barB}^{(k)},
\end{equation}
where $d_{\barB}^{(k)}$ denotes the component of the bar
differential that maps $\barB^k \to \barB^{k-1}$ and the
spectral parameters $\lambda_j$ arise from the regularization
of the collision integral on $\FM_k(\bC) \times \Conf_k^{<}(\bR)$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
This is the defining property of the bar construction as a
coderivation: $d_{\barB}$ is the unique coderivation of
$T^c(s^{-1}\overline{\cA})$ whose composition with the
projection $T^c(s^{-1}\overline{\cA}) \twoheadrightarrow
s^{-1}\overline{\cA}$ recovers the sequence of operations
$(m_1, m_2, m_3, \ldots)$. The spectral parameter
$\lambda_j$ arises from the regularized integral
$\int_{\Conf_k^{<}(\bR)} dt_1 \cdots dt_{k-1}$
along the topological direction, with $\lambda_j = t_{j+1} - t_j$
recording the separation between consecutive points.
\end{proof}

The computation of all $m_k$ for $\cH_k$.

\begin{proposition}[Heisenberg higher operations;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:rosetta-heisenberg-mk}
\index{Heisenberg algebra!$m_k$ operations}
For the Heisenberg algebra $\cH_k$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $m_1 = 0$ \textup{(}no internal differential\textup{)}.
\item $m_2(J, J;\, \lambda) = k\lambda$
 \textup{(}the OPE residue\textup{)}.
\item $m_k = 0$ for all $k \geq 3$
 \textup{(}no ternary or higher operations\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
In particular, $\cH_k$ is \emph{formal}: its $\Ainf$ structure is
concentrated in $m_2$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
(i) The internal differential of $\cH_k$ is zero: there is no
$Q$-operator, and the algebra has trivial cohomological grading
concentrated in degree~$0$.

\smallskip
(ii) The binary operation extracts the double-pole mode. From
equation~\eqref{eq:rosetta-dbar-binary}, the bar differential
on a degree-$2$ element is
\[
d_{\barB}[s^{-1}J \,|\, s^{-1}J]
\;=\;
J_{(1)}J
\;=\; k.
\]
In the spectral (Fourier) parametrization, the meromorphic function
$k/(z_1 - z_2)^2$ corresponds to the spectral expression
$m_2(J, J;\, \lambda) = k\lambda$. The spectral parameter
$\lambda$ records the weight of the residue: a pole of order~$2$
at $z_1 = z_2$ produces a first-order polynomial in~$\lambda$
via the substitution $(z_1 - z_2)^{-n-1} \leftrightarrow
\lambda^{(n)}/n!$.

\smallskip
(iii) The vanishing of $m_k$ for $k \geq 3$ is the decisive
computation. Consider the degree-$3$ bar element
\[
\xi_3
\;=\;
s^{-1}J \otimes s^{-1}J \otimes s^{-1}J
\;\otimes\;
\eta_{12} \wedge \eta_{23}
\;\in\;
\barB^3(\cH_k).
\]
To compute $d_{\barB}^{(3)}$, one must extract a residue
from the iterated OPE of three Heisenberg currents along a
codimension-$2$ stratum of $\FM_3(\bC)$. The iterated OPE is
\begin{align}\label{eq:rosetta-iterated-ope}
J(z_1)\, J(z_2)\, J(z_3)
&\;\sim\;
\frac{k}{(z_1 - z_2)^2}\, J(z_3)
\;+\;
\frac{k}{(z_1 - z_3)^2}\, J(z_2)
\;+\;
\frac{k}{(z_2 - z_3)^2}\, J(z_1).
\end{align}
Each term has a double pole in one pair of variables and is
regular in the third. The ternary operation $m_3$ would arise
from a \emph{simultaneous} triple collision $z_1 \to z_2 \to z_3$.
On $\FM_3(\bC)$, the triple collision stratum is a point
(the maximal boundary stratum). The residue at this point requires
a pole of order $\geq 3$ in the combined variables. But the
iterated OPE~\eqref{eq:rosetta-iterated-ope} has at most
double poles in each pair; there is no pole of the required
order in the ternary collision limit.

More precisely: in the coordinates $u = z_1 - z_2$,
$v = z_2 - z_3$ on $\FM_3(\bC)$, the triple collision
$u, v \to 0$ has codimension~$2$. The form
$\eta_{12} \wedge \eta_{23} = d\log u \wedge d\log v$
contributes a factor $u^{-1}v^{-1}\, du \wedge dv$. The
OPE contributes at most $u^{-2}$ or $v^{-2}$ (never both
simultaneously, because there is no term with $u^{-2}v^{-2}$
in~\eqref{eq:rosetta-iterated-ope}). The combined integrand
is therefore at most $u^{-3}v^{-1}$ or $u^{-1}v^{-3}$ in
the worst case: the residue in the \emph{other} variable
vanishes because the pole order is insufficient. Hence
$m_3 = 0$.

The same argument applies at all higher degrees: $m_k = 0$
for $k \geq 3$ because the Heisenberg OPE has only a double
pole, and the $k$-fold collision on $\FM_k(\bC)$ requires
poles of total order $\geq k$ to produce a nonvanishing
residue against the logarithmic $k$-form
$\eta_{12} \wedge \eta_{23} \wedge \cdots \wedge \eta_{k-1,k}$.
The double-pole OPE can produce at most order~$2$ in each pairwise
variable, but the factorization of the iterated OPE ensures that
no more than one pair is singular at a time.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Formality and Koszulness]
\label{rem:rosetta-formality-koszulness}
\index{formality!Heisenberg}
\index{Koszulness!Heisenberg}
The vanishing of $m_k$ for $k \geq 3$ is \emph{formality}: the
$\Ainf$ structure on $\cH_k$ is quasi-isomorphic to a strict
(non-homotopy) chiral algebra. This is a consequence of the
general one-loop criterion (Theorem~\ref{thm:one-loop-koszul}:
one-loop exact algebras without DS reduction are Koszul), and
for the Heisenberg algebra it is exactly the bar-side manifestation
of chiral Koszulness computed in Volume~I: the PBW spectral
sequence degenerates at~$E_1$, and there are no higher Massey
products. For non-abelian algebras (affine Kac--Moody, Virasoro,
$\mathcal{W}$-algebras), the simple-pole OPE terms produce
nonvanishing $m_3$ and the theory ceases to be formal,
but all standard families remain \emph{Koszul}
(PBW spectral sequence degenerate, bar cohomology concentrated).
The non-formality is detected by the Chevalley--Eilenberg
differential on the bar complex, which is the $d_1$ page of
the PBW spectral sequence.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Lagrangian content of the perturbative/non-perturbative divide]
\label{rem:rosetta-lagrangian-perturbative}
\index{perturbative!Heisenberg as clean intersection}
\index{non-perturbative!Virasoro as excess intersection}
The Heisenberg is perturbatively exact because its Lagrangian
self-intersection is clean: the double-pole OPE produces a
transversal crossing with one-dimensional strata, $m_k = 0$
for $k \ge 3$, and the genus tower is controlled by a single
scalar $\kappa(\cH_k) = k$. The Virasoro, by contrast, is
non-perturbative: its fourth-order pole $c/(z-w)^4$ creates
excess intersection dimension, forcing nonvanishing higher
$\Ainf$ operations that proliferate like instanton corrections
through the genus tower. This is not a coincidence; it is the
Lagrangian content of the perturbative/non-perturbative divide
(Remark~\ref{rem:koszul-perturbative-watershed}).
\end{remark}

% ================================================================
\subsection{The Poisson vertex algebra on cohomology}
\label{subsec:rosetta-pva}
\index{Poisson vertex algebra!Heisenberg}
\index{Heisenberg algebra!PVA structure}
% ================================================================

The binary operation $m_2$ decomposes into a regular part (the
commutative product) and a singular part (the $\lambda$-bracket).
For the Heisenberg algebra, this decomposition reveals the
simplest nontrivial Poisson vertex algebra.

\begin{proposition}[Heisenberg PVA; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:rosetta-pva}
\index{lambda-bracket@$\lambda$-bracket!Heisenberg}
The cohomology $H^{\bullet}(\cH_k, Q) = \bC[J]$ carries the
structure of a Poisson vertex algebra with:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item\label{item:rosetta-pva-product}
 commutative product: the differential polynomial algebra
 $\bC[J, \partial J, \partial^2 J, \ldots]$, with the
 ordinary polynomial product\textup{;}%
 \footnote{In particular $J \cdot J = J^2 \neq 0$ as an
 element of the polynomial ring. The zeroth product
 $J_{(0)}J = 0$ (the simple-pole coefficient of the
 Heisenberg self-OPE vanishes), but this is the
 \emph{zeroth $\lambda$-bracket mode}, not the
 commutative product $\mu$. The normally ordered product
 $:\!JJ\!:\, = J_{(-1)}J$ corresponds to $J^2$ in the
 PVA polynomial ring.}
\item\label{item:rosetta-pva-bracket}
 $\lambda$-bracket: $\{J_\lambda J\} = k\lambda$
 \textup{(}the singular part of $m_2$\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
This is the free boson PVA: the Poisson vertex algebra of a free
scalar field with propagator $k/(z - w)^2$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The binary operation $m_2(J, J;\, \lambda) = k\lambda$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:rosetta-heisenberg-mk}(ii)) decomposes
according to the pole order:
\begin{align}
m_2(J, J;\, \lambda)
&\;=\;
\underbrace{0}_{\text{regular part}}
\;+\;
\underbrace{k\lambda}_{\text{singular part}}.
\end{align}
The regular part (the $\lambda^0$ coefficient) vanishes:
this is the zeroth product $J_{(0)}J = 0$, reflecting the
absence of a simple pole in $J(z)J(w) \sim k/(z-w)^2$.
The commutative PVA product $\mu$ is the polynomial ring
product on $\bC[J, \partial J, \ldots]$, with
$J \cdot J = J^2$ as an ordinary polynomial (corresponding
to the normally ordered product $:\!JJ\!:\, = J_{(-1)}J$
in the vertex algebra).

The singular part is the $\lambda$-bracket
$\{J_\lambda J\} = k\lambda$, encoding the double-pole OPE
$J(z)J(w) \sim k/(z-w)^2$.

The PVA axioms are verified as follows.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{Sesquilinearity.}\enspace
$\{\partial J_\lambda J\} = -\lambda \{J_\lambda J\} = -k\lambda^2$
and $\{J_\lambda \partial J\} = (\partial + \lambda)\{J_\lambda J\}
= (\partial + \lambda)(k\lambda) = k\lambda^2$
(where $\partial$ acts on the vacuum, giving zero).

\medskip
\noindent\textit{Skew-symmetry.}\enspace
The PVA skew-symmetry axiom reads
$\{a_\lambda b\} = -\{b_{-\lambda - \partial} a\}$.
With $a = b = J$:
$-\{J_{-\lambda - \partial} J\} = -k(-\lambda - \partial) = k\lambda + k\partial$.
Acting on the vacuum ($\partial \cdot \mathbf{1} = 0$), this reduces to $k\lambda = \{J_\lambda J\}$.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{Jacobi identity.}\enspace
With a single generator $J$, the Jacobi identity
\[
\{J_\lambda \{J_\mu J\}\}
\;-\;
\{J_\mu \{J_\lambda J\}\}
\;=\;
\{\{J_\lambda J\}_{\lambda + \mu} J\}
\]
reduces to $\{J_\lambda\, k\mu\} - \{J_\mu\, k\lambda\} = \{(k\lambda)_{\lambda+\mu}\, J\}$.
Since $k\mu$ and $k\lambda$ are scalars (not elements of the algebra), all three brackets vanish.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{Leibniz rule.}\enspace
The Leibniz rule $\{a_\lambda (b \cdot c)\} = \{a_\lambda b\} \cdot c
+ b \cdot \{a_\lambda c\}$ must be verified on generators of the
polynomial ring $\bC[J]$.
The nontrivial instance is $a = b = c = J$:
\begin{align*}
\text{RHS}
&= \{J_\lambda J\} \cdot J \;+\; J \cdot \{J_\lambda J\}
= (k\lambda)\, J \;+\; J\, (k\lambda)
= 2k\lambda\, J.
\end{align*}
For the left-hand side, the $\lambda$-bracket acts on
$J \cdot J = J^2 \in \bC[J]$ as a derivation of the
commutative product (item~\ref{item:rosetta-pva-product}):
$\{J_\lambda\, J^2\} = 2J \cdot \{J_\lambda J\} = 2k\lambda\, J$.
Both sides equal $2k\lambda\, J$: Leibniz is satisfied.%
\footnote{The zeroth product $J_{(0)}J = 0$ (the simple-pole
 coefficient of the Heisenberg self-OPE vanishes) plays no role
 here. It means $J$ is \emph{primary of conformal weight~$1$}
 with respect to itself, not that $J \cdot J = 0$ in the PVA
 commutative product. The commutative product is the polynomial
 ring product, corresponding to the normally ordered product
 $:\!JJ\!:\, = J_{(-1)}J \neq 0$ in the vertex algebra.}
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Connection to the coisson structure]
\label{rem:rosetta-coisson}
\index{coisson algebra!Heisenberg}
The PVA of Proposition~\ref{prop:rosetta-pva} is the classical
limit of the chiral algebra $\cH_k$: it is the Beilinson--Drinfeld
coisson structure on the commutative $\mathcal{D}_X$-algebra
underlying $\cH_k$. The $\lambda$-bracket $\{J_\lambda J\} = k\lambda$
encodes the symplectic pairing on $V = \bC \cdot J$: the coefficient
$k$ of $\lambda$ is the level. This is the simplest
instance of the general principle that the chiral Koszul dual
$\cA^!_{\mathrm{ch}}$ of a chiral algebra $\cA$ is controlled by the
$\lambda$-bracket of its Beilinson--Drinfeld coisson structure,
as proved in Volume~I.
\end{remark}


% ================================================================
\subsection{Genus 1: curvature appears}
\label{subsec:rosetta-genus1}
\index{curvature!genus 1!Heisenberg}
\index{Heisenberg algebra!genus 1 curvature}
\index{Swiss-cheese operad!curved}
% ================================================================

At genus~$0$, the bar complex $(\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k),
d_{\barB})$ is an honest chain complex: $d_{\barB}^2 = 0$,
and the $E_1$ coalgebra structure is flat. At genus~$1$, the
situation changes qualitatively. The propagator on an elliptic
curve $E_\tau = \bC / (\Z + \Z\tau)$ is no longer single-valued:
the Weierstrass zeta function
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rosetta-elliptic-propagator}
G_\tau(z)
\;=\;
\zeta_\tau(z) \;-\; \frac{\pi^2}{3}\, E_2(\tau) \cdot z
\end{equation}
has $B$-cycle monodromy $G_\tau(z + \tau) - G_\tau(z) = -2\pi i$.
This monodromy, absent at genus~$0$, is the source of curvature.

\begin{theorem}[Curved $E_1$ coalgebra at genus~$1$;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:rosetta-curved}
\index{curved $E_1$ coalgebra!genus 1}
At genus $g = 1$, the bar complex $\barB^{(1)}(\cH_k)$ with:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item fiberwise differential $\dfib$ \textup{(}residues using
 the elliptic propagator $d\log E_\tau(z, w)$\textup{)},
\item coproduct $\Delta$ \textup{(}unchanged from genus~$0$\textup{)},
\end{enumerate}
satisfies:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item\label{item:rosetta-curved-delta}
 $\Delta$ is coassociative \textup{(}same proof as genus~$0$:
 the deconcatenation coproduct is purely combinatorial and
 does not depend on the propagator or the genus\textup{)};
\item\label{item:rosetta-curved-dsquared}
 $\dfib^{\,2} = k \cdot \omega_1$, where
 $\omega_1 = c_1(\mathbb{E}) \in H^2(\overline{\cM}_1)$
 is the first Chern class of the Hodge bundle;
\item\label{item:rosetta-curved-coder}
 $\dfib$ is \emph{not} a coderivation of $\Delta$: the
 curvature $\dfib^{\,2} = k\cdot\omega_1$ produces a
 factor-$2$ discrepancy at every interior splitting because
 $\omega_1$ contracts the closed-colour collision class
 against the same $\bR$-interval on both branches
 (Volume~I,
 Remark~\ref{V1-rem:sc-higher-genus}\textup{(ii)});
\item\label{item:rosetta-curved-corrected}
 the period-corrected differential
 $\Dg{1} = \dfib + \delta_{\mathrm{per}}$, where
 $\delta_{\mathrm{per}}$ is built from the Fay trisecant
 identity, satisfies $\Dg{1}^{\,2} = 0$ \emph{and} is a
 coderivation of $\Delta$ (Volume~I,
 Remark~\ref{V1-rem:sc-higher-genus}\textup{(iii)}).
\end{enumerate}
The $E_1$ dg coalgebra structure at genus~$1$ is therefore
carried by the period-corrected triple
$(\barB^{(1)}(\cH_k), \Dg{1}, \Delta)$, not by
$(\barB^{(1)}(\cH_k), \dfib, \Delta)$. The fibrewise
differential $\dfib$ records only the Hodge curvature class on
$\overline{\cM}_1$; the period correction restores both flatness
and the coderivation property simultaneously.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\ref{item:rosetta-curved-delta}:
The coproduct $\Delta$ is the tensor coalgebra structure,
defined by the ordering of tensor factors. It depends only on
the combinatorial data of the bar complex, not on the
propagator or the genus of the curve. The proof of
coassociativity is identical to the genus-$0$ case (Step~2 of
Theorem~\ref{thm:rosetta-swiss-cheese}).

\medskip
\ref{item:rosetta-curved-dsquared}:
We compute $\dfib^{\,2}$.
On $\FM_3(E_\tau)$, the differential $\dfib$ acts twice via
the elliptic propagator. The first application produces a
function $G_\tau(z_1 - z_2)$; the second transports this
function around the $B$-cycle of $E_\tau$. The
$B$-cycle monodromy of $G_\tau$ contributes a constant shift:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rosetta-monodromy}
G_\tau(z + \tau) - G_\tau(z) = -2\pi i.
\end{equation}
When $\dfib$ acts a second time, the monodromy of the first
propagator interacts with the second propagator. The
double-pole OPE $J(z_1)\, J(z_2) \sim k/(z_1 - z_2)^2$
contributes a factor of~$k$. The combined effect is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rosetta-dsquared-computation}
\dfib^{\,2}\bigl[s^{-1}J \,|\, s^{-1}J \,|\, s^{-1}J\bigr]
\;=\;
k \cdot (-2\pi i)^2 \cdot
\left(
 \text{period integral over } E_\tau
\right)
\;=\;
k \cdot \omega_1,
\end{equation}
where the period integral, after pushforward to
$\overline{\cM}_1$, produces the Hodge class
$\omega_1 = c_1(\mathbb{E})$. The coefficient $k$ records
the Heisenberg level; the curvature class lives in
$H^2(\overline{\cM}_1)$, not in the coalgebra of bar elements.

\medskip
\ref{item:rosetta-curved-coder}:
We show that $\dfib$ fails the Leibniz rule for $\Delta$ at
interior splittings. Apply $\Delta\circ\dfib^{\,2}$ to the
length-three element
$[s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J]$ and split between the
second and third factor:
\[
\Delta_{2{,}3}\bigl(\dfib^{\,2}[s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J]\bigr)
\;=\;
k\cdot\omega_1\otimes [s^{-1}J]
\;+\;
[s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J]\otimes(k\cdot\omega_1).
\]
The Leibniz rule for $\dfib$ acting on the same element via
$\dfib\otimes\id + \id\otimes\dfib$ produces, at the same
splitting, the sum
\[
\bigl(\dfib\otimes\id + \id\otimes\dfib\bigr)^{2}\Delta_{2{,}3}
[s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J]
\;=\;
2\,k\cdot\omega_1\otimes [s^{-1}J]
\;+\;
2\,[s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J]\otimes(k\cdot\omega_1),
\]
because the Hodge class $\omega_1$ contracts the closed-colour
collision against the same $\bR$-interval on \emph{both}
branches of the splitting. The two sides differ by a factor
of two; $\dfib$ is therefore not a coderivation of~$\Delta$.
This is the genus-$1$ Heisenberg specialization of
Remark~\ref{V1-rem:sc-higher-genus}\textup{(ii)} of Volume~I.
The genus-$0$ argument fails because $\omega_0 = 0$, so the
discrepancy is invisible at the cusp.

\medskip
\ref{item:rosetta-curved-corrected}:
The corrected differential $\Dg{1} = \dfib + \delta_{\mathrm{per}}$
incorporates a period correction $\delta_{\mathrm{per}}$ that
compensates for the $B$-cycle monodromy. The period correction
is determined by the requirement $\Dg{1}^{\,2} = 0$: it must
satisfy
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rosetta-period-correction}
\delta_{\mathrm{per}}^{\,2}
\;+\;
\dfib \circ \delta_{\mathrm{per}}
\;+\;
\delta_{\mathrm{per}} \circ \dfib
\;=\;
-k \cdot \omega_1.
\end{equation}
The existence and uniqueness of $\delta_{\mathrm{per}}$ is the
Heisenberg specialization of the period-corrected differential
constructed in Volume~I; the Fay trisecant identity yields
both the square-zero relation
\eqref{eq:rosetta-period-correction} and the cancellation of
the factor-$2$ discrepancy from~(c) at every interior
splitting. After this cancellation $\Dg{1}$ is a genuine
coderivation of $\Delta$, and the curved $E_1$ dg
coalgebra structure persists at genus~$1$ as
$(\barB^{(1)}(\cH_k), \Dg{1}, \Delta)$. The period correction
couples the topological direction ($\bR$-ordering) to the Hodge
bundle $\mathbb{E}$ over $\overline{\cM}_1$: it is the
first place where the holomorphic and topological directions of the
$E_1$ coalgebra interact nontrivially.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Physical meaning of curvature]
\label{rem:rosetta-curvature-physics}
\index{conformal anomaly!Heisenberg}
The curvature $\dfib^{\,2} = k \cdot \omega_1$ is the conformal
anomaly of the Heisenberg theory. At genus~$0$, the theory is
conformally invariant: $d_{\barB}^2 = 0$ and the partition function
is a constant. At genus~$1$, the torus $E_\tau$ has a modulus
$\tau \in \mathfrak{H}$, and the theory acquires a conformal anomaly
proportional to the level~$k$.

The anomaly lives in the holomorphic (closed-color) direction
and is invisible to the topological (open-color) direction:
$\Delta$ is coassociative at every genus. This is the
$E_1$ coalgebra incarnation of the principle that the conformal
anomaly is a \emph{holomorphic} obstruction. The central
charge $c = 1$ of the Heisenberg algebra (one free boson)
enters through the modular characteristic $\kappa(\cH_k) = k$
computed in Volume~I: the curvature
coefficient is the level, and the level is the basic scalar
invariant of the Koszul pair $(\cH_k, \cH_k^!)$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Genus~$0$ as the flat limit]
\label{rem:rosetta-flat-limit}
The genus-$0$ theory is the \emph{flat} limit of the genus-$1$
theory: as $\tau \to i\infty$ (the cusp of the modular curve),
the elliptic curve $E_\tau$ degenerates to a nodal rational curve,
the propagator $G_\tau(z) \to (z - w)^{-1}$ loses its monodromy,
and the curvature $\dfib^{\,2} = k \cdot \omega_1 \to 0$. The
$E_1$ coalgebra structure specializes from curved to flat. This
degeneration is the bar-complex avatar of the $q$-expansion:
the genus-$1$ bar complex is a deformation of the genus-$0$ bar
complex by the nome $q = e^{2\pi i \tau}$, and the curvature
is the leading obstruction to extending the genus-$0$ theory to
genus~$1$.
\end{remark}


% ================================================================
\subsection{The bridge: one object, two readings}
\label{subsec:rosetta-bridge}
\index{Rosetta Stone!dictionary}
% ================================================================

The Heisenberg bar complex is a single mathematical object (an
$E_1$ curved dg coassociative coalgebra) but it admits
two simultaneous readings: one algebraic (Volume~I), one physical
(Volume~II). The following table records the correspondence.

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.25}
\begin{tabular}{@{}l@{\;\;}l@{\;\;}l@{}}
\textbf{Bar complex} & \textbf{Vol.\@ I reading} &
 \textbf{Vol.\@ II reading} \\
\hline
$d_{\barB}$
 & bar differential
 & closed-color (holomorphic) \\[2pt]
$\Delta$
 & coalgebra coproduct
 & open-color (topological) \\[2pt]
$d_{\barB}^{\,2} = 0$
 & Arnold relations
 & $\Ainf$ identity ($n = 2$) \\[2pt]
$\Delta$ coassociative
 & cofree coalgebra
 & $\Eone$-coalgebra \\[2pt]
$d_{\barB}$ coderivation of $\Delta$
 & bar is dg coalgebra
 & color compatibility \\[2pt]
$m_2$ from bar
 & Koszul dual OPE
 & $\lambda$-bracket / PVA \\[2pt]
$m_k = 0$ for $k \geq 3$
 & bar $A_\infty$-formality (Koszulness)
 & SC-formality \\[2pt]
$\dfib^{\,2} = k \cdot \omega_1$
 & curvature (Thm.\@ C)
 & curved $E_1$ coalgebra \\[2pt]
$\kappa(\cH_k) = k$
 & modular characteristic (Thm.\@ D)
 & conformal anomaly \\[2pt]
$H^{\bullet}(\barB) = \bC \oplus \bC c_k$
 & bar cohomology (Thm.\@ A)
 & Hochschild (Thm.\@ H) \\[2pt]
$\rho_n^{\mathrm{HT}} = \rho_n^{\mathrm{KZ}}$
 & monodromy identification
 & $\cC_{\mathrm{line}}^{\mathrm{red}} \simeq \mathrm{Rep}_q$
 (Thm~\ref{thm:affine-monodromy-identification})
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Each row is a theorem on the left and a physical identification on
the right.

\begin{proposition}[Complementarity for the Heisenberg algebra;
\ClaimStatusProvedElsewhere]
\label{prop:rosetta-complementarity}
\index{complementarity!Heisenberg}
The Heisenberg algebra and its Koszul dual
$\cH_k^! = \mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$,
as computed in Volume~I,
satisfy:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $\kappa(\cH_k) + \kappa(\cH_k^!) = 0$:
 the modular characteristics are opposite;
\item $\mathbf{Q}_1(\cH_k) \oplus \mathbf{Q}_1(\cH_k^!)
 = H^{\bullet}(\overline{\cM}_1,\, \mathcal{Z}_{\cH_k})$:
 the quantum corrections are complementary Lagrangians.
\end{enumerate}
This is Theorem~C
\textup{(}the quantum complementarity theorem of Volume~I\textup{)}
specialized to the Heisenberg case. The curvature coefficient
$\kappa(\cH_k) = k$ has opposite sign in the dual:
$\kappa(\cH_k^!) = -k$, reflecting the opposite $B$-cycle
monodromy of the dual propagator.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[$bc$--$\beta\gamma$ Koszul duality and the statistics exchange]
\label{rem:rosetta-bc-betagamma-koszul}
\index{Koszul duality!bc-betagamma@$bc$--$\beta\gamma$}%
\index{complementarity!free fields}%
The Heisenberg complementarity $K(\cH_k) = 0$ is the first
instance of a universal pattern for all free-field chiral
algebras. The $bc$ ghost system of conformal weights
$(\lambda, 1-\lambda)$ and the $\beta\gamma$ system of the same
weights are Koszul dual to each other:
\[
bc_\lambda^! \;=\; \beta\gamma_\lambda,
\qquad
\beta\gamma_\lambda^! \;=\; bc_\lambda.
\]
The mechanism is the chiral incarnation of classical
$\mathrm{Ext}/\mathrm{Sym}$ duality: $bc_\lambda$ is the
chiral exterior algebra $\bigwedge^{\mathrm{ch}}(V)$ on
$V = \bC b \oplus \bC c$ (fermionic), and its Koszul dual is the
chiral symmetric algebra $\mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$
(bosonic), which is precisely the $\beta\gamma$ system. The bar
complex has $m_2$ only (simple-pole OPE), confirming that both
systems are Koszul. Koszul duality exchanges statistics while
preserving conformal weights; it does \emph{not} exchange spins
$\lambda \mapsto 1 - \lambda$ (that is a relabelling, not a
dualisation).

The complementarity constant vanishes:
$K(bc_\lambda) = c_{bc}(\lambda) + c_{\beta\gamma}(\lambda)
= -2(6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1) + 2(6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1)
= 0$
for all $\lambda$. This extends to tensor products: for mutually
regular Koszul algebras,
$(\cA \otimes \cB)^! \simeq \cA^! \otimes \cB^!$,
so $K = 0$ for any tensor product of Heisenberg, $bc$, and
$\beta\gamma$ systems.

At the string-theory point $\lambda = 2$, $\mu = 3/2$: the Koszul
dual of the reparametrisation ghost $bc_2$ ($c = -26$) is the
bosonic spin-$2$ system $\beta\gamma_2$ ($c = +26$). A spin-$2$
boson is a symmetric tensor field, a graviton. The Koszul dual of
the ghost is, morally, a graviton: the
$\bigwedge \leftrightarrow \mathrm{Sym}$ exchange relates forms
(antisymmetric, diffeomorphism ghosts) to jets (symmetric, metric
fluctuations). This is the free-field shadow of the phenomenon that
Koszul duality of the Virasoro algebra encodes three-dimensional
quantum gravity. The crucial difference: for Virasoro,
$K = 13 \neq 0$, because the DS reduction that produces
Virasoro from affine KM is nonlinear in the level. The free-field
case $K = 0$ is the unique setting where Koszul complementarity is
a strict sign flip.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The modular characteristic is the level]
\label{rem:rosetta-kappa-is-k}
\index{modular characteristic!Heisenberg}
For the Heisenberg algebra, the modular characteristic
$\kappa(\cH_k) = k$ \emph{is} the level. This is the simplest
instance of the general relation: $\kappa$ measures the scalar
component of the genus-$1$ curvature
(as computed in Volume~I), and for a single
free boson with propagator $k/(z - w)^2$, the curvature is
$k \cdot \omega_1$ with no further structure. The $\hat{A}$-genus
generating function for the Heisenberg genus tower is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rosetta-ahat}
\hat{A}_{\cH_k}(q)
\;=\;
\prod_{n=1}^{\infty}\,
\frac{n\, q^{n/2}}{e^{n k q^n / 2} - e^{-n k q^n / 2}}
\end{equation}
which, at $k = 1$, specializes to the standard $\hat{A}$-series.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Bar cohomology and Hochschild cohomology;
\ClaimStatusProvedElsewhere]
\label{prop:rosetta-bar-hochschild}
\index{bar cohomology!Heisenberg}
\index{Hochschild cohomology!Heisenberg}
The bar cohomology of $\cH_k$ at genus~$0$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rosetta-bar-cohomology}
H^n(\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k))
\;=\;
\begin{cases}
\bC & n = 0, \\
0 & n = 1, \\
\bC \cdot c_k & n = 2, \\
0 & n \geq 3,
\end{cases}
\end{equation}
recovering the central extension class $c_k \in H^2$
computed on the Heisenberg bar complex in Volume~I.
This is the chiral Hochschild cohomology of Volume~II:
$\mathrm{CH}^{\bullet}(\cH_k, \cH_k) \simeq
H^{\bullet}(\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k))$, identifying the
central charge as a Hochschild class.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[The Rosetta Stone principle]
\label{rem:rosetta-principle}
\index{Rosetta Stone!principle}
The Heisenberg algebra is the simplest chiral algebra, but it is
not trivial: it carries curvature ($\dfib^{\,2} = k \cdot \omega_1$),
complementarity ($\kappa(\cH_k) + \kappa(\cH_k^!) = 0$),
the $\hat{A}$-genus, and the full modular structure.
Every feature of the general theory is already present.

The Rosetta Stone is the principle that these features have two
simultaneous readings, algebraic (Volume~I) and physical
(Volume~II), unified by the Swiss-cheese structure of a single
dg coalgebra. The bar differential~$d_{\barB}$ is the
holomorphic side; the coproduct~$\Delta$ is the topological
side; their interaction
$\Delta \circ d_{\barB} = (d_{\barB} \otimes \id
+ \id \otimes d_{\barB}) \circ \Delta$
is the content of the 3d theory on $\bC \times \bR$. At genus~$0$,
both readings are equivalent and either suffices. At genus~$1$
and beyond, the curvature couples the two readings, and the full
Swiss-cheese structure becomes necessary.

The Heisenberg bar complex is a single coalgebra that unifies
Koszul duality with holomorphic--topological factorization
(Theorem~\ref{thm:steinberg-presentation}).
The Rosetta Stone is the dictionary that makes this analogy precise.
\end{remark}

% ================================================================
\subsection{The Heisenberg 3d MC element}
\label{subsec:rosetta-3d-mc}
\index{universal MC element!3d!Heisenberg}
\index{Heisenberg algebra!3d MC element}
% ================================================================

The Swiss-cheese convolution $L_\infty$-algebra
$\gSC_T$ (Definition~\ref{def:sc-convolution}) and its canonical
MC element $\alpha_T$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:3d-universal-mc}) specialise
to the Heisenberg as follows.

\begin{theorem}[Heisenberg 3d MC element; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:rosetta-3d-mc}
For the Heisenberg theory $T = (\cH_k, \cH_{-k}\text{-mod})$ on
$\C \times \R_{\ge 0}$, the Swiss-cheese convolution algebra
$\gSC_T$ is abelian: $[\alpha,\beta] = 0$ for all
$\alpha, \beta \in \gSC_T$. The MC element is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:alpha-heisenberg}
\alpha_{\cH_k}
\;=\;
\alpha_{\mathrm{cl}}
\;+\;
\hbar\,\alpha_{\mathrm{loop}},
\end{equation}
where the two components are:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Closed-colour, genus-$0$ component:}
 $\alpha_{\mathrm{cl}}$ is the binary operation
 $m_2(J,J;\lambda) = k\lambda$ on $\FM_2(\C)$, encoding the
 double-pole OPE\@. No higher closed vertices contribute
 ($m_k = 0$ for $k \ge 3$, by
 Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:rosetta-heisenberg-mk}}).
\item \emph{Closed-colour, genus-$1$ component:}
 $\alpha_{\mathrm{loop}} = k \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$ is the
 genus-$1$ self-loop correction from the unique graph
 $\Gamma_{\mathrm{irr}}$ \textup{(}one vertex of genus~$0$ with
 one self-edge\textup{)}. The BV operator $\Delta$ traces the
 level $\langle J, J \rangle = k$; the boundary class
 $[\delta_{\mathrm{irr}}]$ gives
 $\lambda_1 = \tfrac{1}{12}\delta_{\mathrm{irr}}$.
\end{enumerate}
There is no mixed-colour or open-colour MC contribution: the
abelian structure forces all mixed and open graph sums to vanish.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Abelianity.}\enspace
The Lie bracket on $\gSC_T$ is the operadic composition bracket,
which requires at least one nontrivial vertex operation. For the
Heisenberg, $m_k = 0$ for $k \ge 3$ and the simple-pole OPE
residue $J_{(0)}J = 0$ vanishes. Every composition of two graph
contributions involves at least one operation $m_k$ with $k \ge 3$
or a simple-pole insertion, hence vanishes. The bracket is
identically zero.

\emph{Closed-colour component.}\enspace
The only contributing two-coloured trees with all vertices closed
are those with each vertex labelled by $m_2$ (the binary OPE).
Stability $2g(v) - 2 + \mathrm{val}(v) > 0$ with
$\mathrm{val}(v) = 2$ and $g(v) = 0$ fails ($2 \cdot 0 - 2 + 2 = 0
\not> 0$), so at genus~$0$ no nontrivial tree contributes
beyond the binary operation itself.
The element $\alpha_{\mathrm{cl}}$ is the identity
\[
\alpha_{\mathrm{cl}}
\;=\;
m_2 \;\in\;
\Hom\bigl(\mathbf{B}^{(0,2)}(\SCop),\;
\End_{\cH_k}\bigr),
\]
encoding the double-pole OPE at the unique two-point closed
vertex. Its MC equation $D\alpha_{\mathrm{cl}} +
\tfrac{1}{2}[\alpha_{\mathrm{cl}}, \alpha_{\mathrm{cl}}] = 0$
reduces to $d_{\barB}^2 = 0$ (the Arnold relation, verified in
Theorem~\ref{thm:rosetta-swiss-cheese}, Step~1).

\emph{Genus-$1$ component.}\enspace
At genus~$1$, the unique graph is $\Gamma_{\mathrm{irr}}$: one
vertex of genus~$0$ with one self-edge and one half-edge. The
graph contribution is $\hbar \cdot \Delta$, where
$\Delta(sJ) = \langle J, J \rangle \cdot s\mathbf{1} = k \cdot
s\mathbf{1}$. The chain $W_{\Gamma_{\mathrm{irr}}} =
[\delta_{\mathrm{irr}}]$ gives the Hodge class
$\lambda_1 = \tfrac{1}{12}\delta_{\mathrm{irr}}$. Therefore
$\alpha_{\mathrm{loop}} = k \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$, and the
total MC element is $\alpha_{\cH_k} = \alpha_{\mathrm{cl}} +
\hbar\,k \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$.

\emph{Mixed and open colours.}\enspace
A mixed-colour graph has at least one open vertex (labelled by an
$E_1$-operation on line modules) and at least one closed vertex.
For the Heisenberg, line modules are modules over
$Y(\mathfrak{u}(1)) \simeq \cH_{-k}$, the abelian open-colour
Koszul dual. The
Heisenberg module category is semisimple: every module is a direct
sum of Fock spaces $\mathcal{F}_\mu$, and the $E_1$-operations on
Fock modules are scalar (the vertex operators are abelian). Every
mixed graph contribution is therefore proportional to a product of
scalars, and the structure maps of $\gSC_T$ annihilate them by the
coderivation property applied to the trivial $m_k = 0$ ($k \ge 3$)
at the closed vertices. The open-colour contribution vanishes
for the same reason.
\end{proof}

The six projections of Proposition~\ref{prop:alpha-projections}
specialise as follows.

\begin{corollary}[Heisenberg projections; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:rosetta-heisenberg-projections}
For the Heisenberg theory:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Closed face} $=$ the boundary $\Ainf$ algebra $\cH_k$
 with $m_2(J,J;\lambda) = k\lambda$ and $m_{k \ge 3} = 0$.
\item \emph{Open face} $=$ the semisimple Fock category with
 trivial open-colour line-sector operations.
\item \emph{Spectral $R$-matrix}: $R(z) = e^{k\hbar/z}$, the
 abelian braiding. The Yang--Baxter equation is satisfied
 trivially \textup{(}$R$ is scalar\textup{)}.
\item \emph{Bulk-to-boundary}: $\Abulk = \Zder(\cH_k) = \cH_k$
 \textup{(}abelian algebras are their own derived centers\textup{)}.
\item \emph{Genus face}: $\Theta_{\cH_k} = k \cdot \eta \otimes
 \Lambda$, recovering Vol~I\@.
\item \emph{PVA}: $\{J_\lambda J\} = k\lambda$, the rank-$1$ PVA
 bracket.
\end{enumerate}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
(i)--(ii): Propositions~\ref{prop:rosetta-heisenberg-mk}
and~\ref{prop:rosetta-operations}.
(iii): The spectral braiding of two Fock modules $\mathcal{F}_{\mu_1}$,
$\mathcal{F}_{\mu_2}$ at spectral separation~$z$ is
$R_{\mu_1,\mu_2}(z) = e^{k\mu_1\mu_2\hbar/z}$. For the fundamental
module ($\mu = 1$): $R(z) = e^{k\hbar/z}$.
(iv): $\cH_k$ is commutative ($J_{(0)}J = 0$), so
$\HH^0(\cH_k) = \cH_k$ and the derived center is the algebra
itself.
(v): Restriction of $\alpha_{\cH_k}$ to the closed genus-expanded
sector gives $\alpha_{\mathrm{cl}} + \hbar\,\alpha_{\mathrm{loop}}
= m_2 + \hbar\,k\cdot\eta\otimes\Lambda = \Theta_{\cH_k}$.
(vi): $m_2(J,J;\lambda) = k\lambda$ descends to the PVA bracket
by the descent theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:cohomology_PVA}).
\end{proof}

\begin{computation}[The Heisenberg hydrogen atom; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:heisenberg-hydrogen-atom}%
\index{Heisenberg algebra!hydrogen atom|textbf}%
\index{hydrogen atom!Heisenberg bar complex}%
The Heisenberg algebra is the hydrogen atom of the bar-complex
programme: all data reduce to a single scalar~$k$ and all
higher complexity vanishes. We collect the complete
package in one place.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Operations.}
The single nonvanishing operation is
$m_2(J,J;\lambda) = k\lambda$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:rosetta-heisenberg-mk}).
All $m_k = 0$ for $k \ge 3$.
The depth spectrum is $\{1\}$: the bar
cogenerators live in degree~$2$ only, and
$\barBch(\cH_k)$ is cogenerated in degree~$1$
with the single relation $d_{\barB}[s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J] = k$.
The weight-depth identity $w + d = n - 1$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)) is trivially satisfied: the unique monomial has $w = 0$, $d = 1$, $n = 2$.
The Swiss-cheese structure is SC-formal: the higher
coherences of $W(\SCchtop)$ are trivially satisfied.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{$R$-matrix.}
The collision residue is $r^{\mathrm{coll}}(z) = k/z$
(the $d\log$ kernel absorbs one power from the
double-pole OPE: $k/(z-w)^2 \cdot d\log(z-w)
\leadsto k/z$).
The connection on $\Conf_2^{\mathrm{ord}}(\C)$ is
$\nabla = d - k \cdot d\log(z)$,
and the monodromy is $\exp(-2\pi i k)$.
The spectral $R$-matrix on modules is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:heisenberg-hydrogen-R}
R(z) \;=\; e^{k\hbar/z},
\end{equation}
confirming
Corollary~\ref{cor:rosetta-heisenberg-projections}(iii).
The Yang--Baxter equation is trivially satisfied
($R$ is scalar). The braiding is nontrivial
but derived from the local OPE: tier~(ii) of the
three-tier picture
(Section~\ref{subsec:ordered-three-tier}).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Genus-$1$ $r$-matrix.}
On $E_\tau$, the rational propagator $1/z$ is replaced by
$\zeta(z|\tau)$. Since $c_0 = J_{(0)}J = 0$
(no simple pole), the quasi-periodic part of
$\zeta(z|\tau)$ drops out of the $r$-matrix:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:heisenberg-hydrogen-genus1-r}
r^{(1)}_{\cH_k}(z)
\;=\;
k \cdot \wp(z|\tau)
\;=\;
k\biggl(\frac{1}{z^2}
 - \sum_{n=1}^{\infty}(2n+1)\, G_{2n+2}(\tau)\, z^{2n}
\biggr).
\end{equation}
The genus-$1$ correction is the Eisenstein-weighted series
$-k\bigl(3G_4(\tau)\,z^2 + 5G_6(\tau)\,z^4 + \cdots\bigr)$.
The $r$-matrix is doubly periodic on $E_\tau$: no
$B$-cycle monodromy. Curvature and braiding are
decoupled.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Complete MC element.}
The total MC element (Theorem~\ref{thm:rosetta-3d-mc}) is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:heisenberg-hydrogen-theta}
\Theta_{\cH_k}
\;=\;
k\lambda
\;+\;
k \sum_{g \ge 1} \hbar^{2g}\, \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}} \cdot \omega_g,
\end{equation}
purely curvature-driven: the genus tower contains
no shadow corrections because $m_n = 0$ for all $n \ge 3$. The free energy is $F^{\mathrm{tot}} = k \cdot (\hbar/2)/\sin(\hbar/2)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:ahat-lagrangian}).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Euler characteristic.}
The genus-$1$ partition function
$Z_1(\cH_k) = \eta(\tau)^{-k}$
(Computation~\ref{comp:heisenberg-line-bundle})
recovers the Dedekind eta function. The $q$-expansion
$\eta(q)^{-1} = q^{-1/24}\prod_{n=1}^{\infty}(1-q^n)^{-1}$
is the generating function for partitions (the
pentagonal theorem). The Heisenberg bar complex,
through the genus tower, knows the combinatorics of
integer partitions.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Koszul dual.}
$\cH_k^! = \mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$, the
chiral symmetric algebra on the dual.
The Poincar\'{e} series of the bar complex is
$P(t) = 1 + t$ (one cogenerator in degree~$1$).
\end{computation}

\begin{computation}[Complete $E_1$ ordered shadow for $\cH_k$;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:heisenberg-e1-ordered-shadow}%
\index{Heisenberg algebra!E1 ordered shadow@$E_1$ ordered shadow|textbf}%
\index{ordered shadow!Heisenberg|textbf}%
\index{hydrogen atom!E1 ordered shadow@$E_1$ ordered shadow}%
The Heisenberg algebra is the hydrogen atom of the $E_1$ ordered
shadow programme: all data reduce to a single scalar~$k$, the shadow
tower terminates at degree~$2$, and the entire ordered structure is
computed in closed form at every genus. We assemble the complete
package.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(1) The ordered shadow polynomial.}
The single nonvanishing operation is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:e1-shadow-m2}
m_2(J,J;\lambda) \;=\; k\lambda,
\end{equation}
valid for all $k \in \bC$. The spectral parameter $\lambda$ is the
Fourier dual of the collision coordinate $z_1 - z_2$ on
$\FM_2(\bC)$, and records the weight of the residue: the double pole
$k/(z_1 - z_2)^2$ produces $k\lambda$ via the substitution
$(z_1 - z_2)^{-n-1} \leftrightarrow \lambda^{(n)}/n!$. The shadow
tower terminates: $m_k = 0$ for all $k \ge 3$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:rosetta-heisenberg-mk}). The depth spectrum is
$\{1\}$: the shadow depth is $r_{\max} = 2$ (class~G, Gaussian),
bar cogenerators live in degree~$2$ only, and the weight-depth
identity $w + d = n - 1$ is satisfied trivially ($w = 0$, $d = 1$,
$n = 2$).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(2) The $E_1$ content: spectral ordering.}
The spectral parameter $\lambda$ in $m_2(J,J;\lambda) = k\lambda$
carries the ordering information of the $E_1$-structure. On the
ordered bar complex $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(\cH_k)$, the
differential at tensor degree~$2$ is
\[
d_{\mathrm{res}}[s^{-1}J \,|\, s^{-1}J]
\;=\; k,
\]
with the ordering $z_1 < z_2$ on $\bR$ recorded in the tensor
sequence $s^{-1}J \otimes s^{-1}J$ (the first factor corresponds to
the earlier point). The parameter $\lambda$ is the \emph{directed}
spectral flow: under the transposition $\sigma_{12}$ that exchanges
the two points, $\lambda \mapsto -\lambda$, and
$m_2(J,J;-\lambda) = -k\lambda = -m_2(J,J;\lambda)$. The
antisymmetry in $\lambda$ reflects the Koszul sign of the
desuspension: $s^{-1}J$ has odd cohomological degree.

The ordered bar complex has generating function
(Computation~\ref{comp:heisenberg-dim-table}):
\[
\sum_{n,w \ge 1}
\dim\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}_{n,w}\; t^n q^w
\;=\;
\frac{tq(1-q)}{1-q-tq},
\]
with $\dim\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}_{n,w} = \binom{w-1}{n-1}$
(compositions of $w$ into $n$ positive parts).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(3) The $R$-matrix: Taylor expansion to order~$50$.}
The collision residue is $r^{\mathrm{coll}}(z) = k/z$ (the
$d\log$ kernel absorbs one power from the double-pole OPE:
$k/(z-w)^2 \cdot d\log(z-w) \leadsto k/z$). The
connection on $\Conf_2^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bC)$ is
$\nabla = d - k\, d\log(z)$, and the monodromy around
the generator $\gamma$ is $\exp(-2\pi i k)$. The spectral
$R$-matrix on modules is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:e1-shadow-R}
R(z) \;=\; e^{k\hbar/z}
\;=\;
\sum_{n=0}^{\infty} \frac{(k\hbar)^n}{n!\, z^n}.
\end{equation}
This is the abelian braiding: the Yang--Baxter equation
$R_{12}R_{13}R_{23} = R_{23}R_{13}R_{12}$ is trivially satisfied
because $R$ is a scalar (all factors commute). The Taylor
expansion to order~$50$ in $u = 1/z$:
\begin{align}\label{eq:e1-R-expansion-50}
R(z) \;&=\;
1 + k\hbar\, u + \tfrac{k^2\hbar^2}{2}\, u^2
+ \tfrac{k^3\hbar^3}{6}\, u^3
+ \tfrac{k^4\hbar^4}{24}\, u^4
+ \tfrac{k^5\hbar^5}{120}\, u^5
\notag\\
&\quad
+ \tfrac{k^6\hbar^6}{720}\, u^6
+ \tfrac{k^7\hbar^7}{5040}\, u^7
+ \tfrac{k^8\hbar^8}{40320}\, u^8
+ \tfrac{k^9\hbar^9}{362880}\, u^9
+ \tfrac{k^{10}\hbar^{10}}{3628800}\, u^{10}
\notag\\
&\quad + \cdots
+ \tfrac{(k\hbar)^n}{n!}\, u^n + \cdots
+ \tfrac{(k\hbar)^{50}}{50!}\, u^{50}
+ O(u^{51}),
\end{align}
with $u = 1/z$ and the general coefficient
$(k\hbar)^n/n!$. At $k = 1$, $\hbar = 1$:
\[
R(z)\big|_{k=\hbar=1}
\;=\;
e^{1/z}
\;=\;
1 + \frac{1}{z} + \frac{1}{2z^2}
+ \frac{1}{6z^3} + \frac{1}{24z^4}
+ \frac{1}{120z^5} + \cdots.
\]
The $50$th coefficient is $1/50! \approx 3.29 \times 10^{-65}$:
the series converges faster than any power, confirming that
the Heisenberg $R$-matrix is an entire function of $1/z$.

The three-tier placement
(Section~\ref{subsec:ordered-three-tier}): $\cH_k$ is
tier~(ii): the $R$-matrix is nontrivial but \emph{derived}
from the local OPE $J(z)J(w) \sim k/(z-w)^2$ via the
monodromy of the flat connection on $\Conf_2^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bC)$.
The descent $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}} \to \barBch$ is
$R$-matrix twisted
(Proposition~\ref{prop:r-matrix-descent}), but since
$R$ is scalar, the twist amounts to a phase and the two
complexes carry the same cohomological information.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(4) Genus-$1$ $E_1$ shadow.}
At genus~$1$, the rational propagator $1/z$ is replaced by the
elliptic propagator $G_\tau(z) = \zeta(z|\tau) - \tfrac{\pi^2}{3}
E_2(\tau)\cdot z$ on $E_\tau = \bC/(\Z + \Z\tau)$.
The genus-$1$ binary operation acquires an Eisenstein correction:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:e1-shadow-genus1-m2}
m_2^{(1)}(J,J;\lambda;\tau)
\;=\;
k\lambda
\;-\;
\frac{\pi^2 k}{3}\, E_2(\tau)\, \lambda.
\end{equation}
The correction $-(\pi^2 k/3)\, E_2(\tau)\, \lambda$ arises from
the regularization of the elliptic propagator: the Weierstrass
$\zeta$-function $\zeta(z|\tau)$ has quasi-periodicity
$\zeta(z+\tau|\tau) - \zeta(z|\tau) = -2\pi i + 2\eta_\tau$,
and the subtraction $-(\pi^2/3)\, E_2(\tau)\cdot z$ renders $G_\tau$
with monodromy $-2\pi i$
(equation~\eqref{eq:rosetta-monodromy}). The Eisenstein series
\begin{equation}\label{eq:e2-expansion}
E_2(\tau)
\;=\;
1 - 24\sum_{n=1}^{\infty} \sigma_1(n)\, q^n
\;=\;
1 - 24q - 72q^2 - 96q^3 - 168q^4 - 144q^5 - \cdots
\end{equation}
(with $q = e^{2\pi i \tau}$ and $\sigma_1(n) = \sum_{d|n} d$)
encodes the genus-$1$ deformation of the Heisenberg shadow.

The genus-$1$ $r$-matrix, from
equation~\eqref{eq:heisenberg-hydrogen-genus1-r}, is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:e1-genus1-r}
r^{(1)}_{\cH_k}(z)
\;=\;
k\cdot\wp(z|\tau)
\;=\;
k\biggl(
\frac{1}{z^2}
- \sum_{n=1}^{\infty}(2n+1)\, G_{2n+2}(\tau)\, z^{2n}
\biggr),
\end{equation}
where $\wp$ is the Weierstrass elliptic function and
$G_{2n+2}(\tau) = \sum_{\substack{(m,n) \neq (0,0)}}
(m + n\tau)^{-(2n+2)}$ are the Eisenstein series. The
key structural fact: since $c_0 = J_{(0)}J = 0$ (no simple pole),
the $r$-matrix is the Weierstrass $\wp$-function, which is
\emph{doubly periodic} on $E_\tau$, with no $B$-cycle monodromy.
Curvature and braiding decouple
(Theorem~\ref{thm:higher-genus-spectral-dichotomy}\ref{item:genus-g-decoupling}).
This is the simplest instance of the decoupling
regime: the Heisenberg is the unique standard family with $c_0 = 0$.

The genus-$1$ $R$-matrix is therefore
\begin{equation}\label{eq:e1-genus1-R}
R^{(1)}(z;\tau)
\;=\;
\exp\bigl(k\hbar\cdot\wp(z|\tau)\bigr)
\;=\;
\exp\biggl(
k\hbar\Bigl(
\frac{1}{z^2}
- 3G_4(\tau)\, z^2
- 5G_6(\tau)\, z^4
- \cdots
\Bigr)
\biggr),
\end{equation}
a doubly periodic meromorphic function on $E_\tau$ (with
an essential singularity at $z = 0$).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(5) Genus-$2$ $E_1$ shadow: the Bergman kernel replacement.}
At genus~$g \ge 2$, the propagator on $\Sigma_g$ is the abelian
differential of the third kind $f(z,w) = \partial_z \log E(z,w)$,
where $E(z,w)$ is the Szeg\H{o} prime form. The genus-$g$
collision residue for $\cH_k$ is
(Theorem~\ref{thm:higher-genus-spectral-dichotomy}):
\begin{equation}\label{eq:e1-genus-g-r}
r^{(\Sigma_g)}_{\cH_k}(z,w)
\;=\;
k \cdot B(z,w),
\end{equation}
where $B(z,w) = \partial_z \partial_w \log E(z,w)$ is the
Bergman kernel, the unique symmetric bidifferential on
$\Sigma_g \times \Sigma_g$ with a double pole on the diagonal
and no other singularities. Since $c_0 = 0$, the zeroth-pole
term $c_0 \cdot f(z,w)$ in the general formula
\eqref{eq:genus-g-r-matrix} vanishes, and only the Bergman
kernel term survives. The $B$-cycle monodromy vanishes
(equation~\eqref{eq:genus-g-r-monodromy} with $c_0 = 0$):
the genus-$g$ $r$-matrix for $\cH_k$ is a globally meromorphic
bidifferential on $\Sigma_g \times \Sigma_g$ at every genus.

At genus~$2$ specifically, the Bergman kernel on a genus-$2$ curve
$\Sigma_2$ with period matrix $\Omega = \bigl(\begin{smallmatrix}
\tau_1 & \tau_{12} \\ \tau_{12} & \tau_2
\end{smallmatrix}\bigr)$ is
\[
B(z,w)
\;=\;
\frac{1}{(z-w)^2}
\;+\;
\sum_{i,j=1}^{2}
\bigl(\mathrm{Im}\,\Omega\bigr)^{-1}_{ij}\;
\omega_i(z)\,\omega_j(w)
\;+\;
(\text{higher-order diagonal corrections}),
\]
and the genus-$2$ Heisenberg $r$-matrix is $r^{(2)} = k \cdot B$.
The genus-$2$ $R$-matrix is $R^{(2)}(z,w) = \exp(k\hbar\cdot B(z,w))$,
again globally meromorphic (no $B$-cycle monodromy). The genus tower
is $F_g = k \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ at all genera (Theorem~\ref{thm:ahat-lagrangian}), with the free energy
$F^{\mathrm{tot}} = k \cdot (\hbar/2)/\sin(\hbar/2)$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(6) The Euler-eta and pentagonal verification.}
The genus-$1$ partition function
$Z_1(\cH_k) = \eta(\tau)^{-k}$
(Computation~\ref{comp:heisenberg-line-bundle}) gives, at $k = 1$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:e1-euler-eta}
\eta(q)
\;=\;
q^{1/24}\prod_{n=1}^{\infty}(1 - q^n)
\;=\;
q^{1/24}\sum_{n=-\infty}^{\infty}(-1)^n\, q^{n(3n-1)/2},
\end{equation}
where the last equality is Euler's pentagonal theorem. The
pentagonal numbers $\omega(n) = n(3n-1)/2$ for $n \in \Z$ are
\begin{align}\label{eq:pentagonal-numbers}
&n = 0:\; 0, \quad
n = 1:\; 1, \quad
n = -1:\; 2, \quad
n = 2:\; 5, \quad
n = -2:\; 7,
\notag\\
&n = 3:\; 12, \quad
n = -3:\; 15, \quad
n = 4:\; 22, \quad
n = -4:\; 26, \quad
n = 5:\; 35,
\notag\\
&n = -5:\; 40, \quad
n = 6:\; 51, \quad
n = -6:\; 57, \quad
n = 7:\; 70, \quad
n = -7:\; 77,
\notag\\
&n = 8:\; 92, \quad
n = -8:\; 100, \quad
n = 9:\; 117, \quad
n = -9:\; 126, \quad
n = 10:\; 145.
\end{align}
The expansion of $\eta(q)/q^{1/24} = \prod_{n=1}^{\infty}(1-q^n)$
to $100$ terms, writing $P(q) = \prod_{n \ge 1}(1-q^n)$:
\begin{align}\label{eq:eta-100-terms}
P(q) \;&=\;
1 - q - q^2 + q^5 + q^7
- q^{12} - q^{15} + q^{22} + q^{26}
- q^{35}
\notag\\
&\quad
- q^{40} + q^{51} + q^{57}
- q^{70} - q^{77} + q^{92} + q^{100}
- q^{117} - q^{126}
\notag\\
&\quad
+ q^{145} + q^{155}
- q^{176} - q^{187}
+ q^{210} + q^{222}
- q^{247} - q^{260}
\notag\\
&\quad
+ q^{287} + q^{301}
- q^{330} - q^{345}
+ q^{376} + q^{392}
- q^{425} - q^{442}
\notag\\
&\quad
+ q^{477} + q^{495}
- q^{532} - q^{551}
+ q^{590} + q^{610}
- q^{651} - q^{672}
\notag\\
&\quad
+ q^{715} + q^{737}
+ O(q^{782}).
\end{align}
Each nonzero exponent is a pentagonal number $n(3n-1)/2$, and
each coefficient is $(-1)^n$; there are no other terms. This
is the content of Euler's identity:
\[
\prod_{n=1}^{\infty}(1 - q^n)
\;=\;
\sum_{n=-\infty}^{\infty}(-1)^n\, q^{n(3n-1)/2}
\;=\;
1 + \sum_{n=1}^{\infty}(-1)^n\bigl(q^{n(3n-1)/2} + q^{n(3n+1)/2}\bigr).
\]
Verification: the exponents
$\{0, 1, 2, 5, 7, 12, 15, 22, 26, 35, 40, 51, 57, 70, 77,
92, 100, 117, 126, 145, 155, 176, 187, 210, 222, 247, 260,
287, 301, 330, 345, 376, 392, 425, 442, 477, 495, 532, 551,
590, 610, 651, 672, 715, 737, \ldots\}$
are precisely the generalised pentagonal numbers
$\omega(n) = n(3n-1)/2$ for $n = 0, \pm 1, \pm 2, \ldots$,
listed in order. The signs alternate: $+$ for even $|n|$, $-$
for odd $|n|$.

The inverse $P(q)^{-1} = \sum_{n=0}^{\infty} p(n)\, q^n$ is the
partition generating function, with
\[
p(0) = 1,\;
p(1) = 1,\;
p(2) = 2,\;
p(3) = 3,\;
p(4) = 5,\;
p(5) = 7,\;
p(6) = 11,\;
p(7) = 15,\;
\ldots
\]
the partition numbers. The Heisenberg bar complex, through the genus
tower and the $E_1$ ordered shadow, \emph{knows} the combinatorics
of integer partitions: the ordered bar complex counts compositions
(Computation~\ref{comp:heisenberg-dim-table}), the $\Sigma_n$-descent
quotients them to partitions, and the Euler characteristic of the
alternating sum recovers the pentagonal identity.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Summary of the $E_1$ ordered dictionary.}
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.25}
\begin{tabular}{@{}l@{\;\;}l@{}}
\textbf{$E_1$ ordered datum} & \textbf{Value for $\cH_k$} \\
\hline
Shadow polynomial $m_2(J,J;\lambda)$
 & $k\lambda$ \\[2pt]
Shadow depth $r_{\max}$
 & $2$ (class~G) \\[2pt]
Higher operations $m_{k \ge 3}$
 & $0$ (Koszul and SC-formal) \\[2pt]
$R$-matrix $R(z)$
 & $e^{k\hbar/z}$ (scalar, abelian) \\[2pt]
Three-tier placement
 & tier~(ii): $\Einf$ with OPE poles \\[2pt]
Genus-$1$ $r$-matrix
 & $k\cdot\wp(z|\tau)$ (doubly periodic) \\[2pt]
Genus-$1$ correction to $m_2$
 & $-(\pi^2 k/3)\, E_2(\tau)\, \lambda$ \\[2pt]
Genus-$g$ $r$-matrix
 & $k \cdot B(z,w)$ (Bergman kernel) \\[2pt]
$B$-cycle monodromy
 & $0$ at all genera ($c_0 = 0$) \\[2pt]
Euler characteristic
 & $\eta(q)^{-k}$ (pentagonal numbers) \\[2pt]
Partition function
 & compositions $\to$ partitions via $\Sigma_n$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The single scalar~$k$ determines the entire $E_1$ ordered shadow.
\end{computation}

\begin{computation}[Heisenberg classifying space; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{comp:heisenberg-classifying-space}
We verify the representability theorem (Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-representability}) for $\cA = \cH_k$. The bar construction $\barB(\cH_k) = T^c(s^{-1}\C \cdot J)$ is the cofree conilpotent coalgebra on a single desuspended generator. For any conilpotent test coalgebra $\cC$, the space of twisting morphisms is:
\[
\mathrm{Tw}(\cC, \cH_k) \;=\; \bigl\{\tau \in \Hom^{-1}(\cC, \cH_k) \;\bigm|\; d\tau + \tau \star \tau = 0\bigr\}.
\]
Since $\cH_k$ has $m_{k \geq 3} = 0$, the MC equation reduces to $d\tau + m_2(\tau, \tau) = 0$, where $m_2(\tau,\tau)(c) = k \cdot \langle \tau(c'), \tau(c'') \rangle \cdot \lambda$ for the reduced coproduct $\bar\Delta(c) = \sum c' \otimes c''$. The terminality map $f_\tau \colon \cC \to \barB(\cH_k)$ is:
\[
f_\tau(c) \;=\; \sum_{n \geq 1} \tau^{\otimes n} \circ \Delta^{(n-1)}(c) \;\in\; T^c(s^{-1}\C \cdot J),
\]
converging because $\cC$ is conilpotent. For $\cC = \barB(\cH_k)$ itself, the identity twisting morphism gives $f_{\tau_{\mathrm{univ}}} = \id$, recovering the algebra from its own bar complex.
\end{computation}

\subsection{The doubling construction for Heisenberg}

The general half-space BV theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:general-half-space-bv}) is proved by the doubling
construction (Theorem~\ref{thm:doubling-rwi}): embed the half-space
into the doubled whole-space and apply Stokes. For the Heisenberg
algebra, this construction is completely explicit.

The free propagator on $\C\times\R$ is
$K(z,t;\,z',t')=\Theta(t-t')/(2\pi(z-z'))$. The reflected
propagator on the half-space $\C\times\R_{\ge 0}$ is
\[
K^{\mathrm{refl}}(z,t;\,z',t')
=\frac{\Theta(t-t')}{2\pi(z-z')}
+\frac{\Theta(t+t')}{2\pi(z-\bar z')}.
\]
The reflection $\sigma(z,t)=(\bar z,-t)$ maps
$\C\times\R\to\C\times\R$, and $K^{\mathrm{refl}}=K+K\circ\sigma$ is
the standard propagator on the doubled space restricted to the
$\sigma$-invariant sector.

The method-of-images embedding $\iota\colon\Conf_n(\C\times\R_{\ge 0})
\hookrightarrow\Conf_{2n}(\C\times\R)^{\sigma}$ sends each point
$(z_i,t_i)$ to the pair $\{(z_i,t_i),(\bar z_i,-t_i)\}$. The
propagator form $\omega_{ij}^{\mathrm{refl}}=\iota^*(\omega_{ij}+
\omega_{i,\sigma(j)})$ extends to a logarithmic form on the
Fulton--MacPherson compactification of $\Conf_{2n}(\C\times\R)$, with
log poles along the collision divisor $z_i=z_j$ (standard) and the
reflection divisor $z_i=\bar z_j$ (from the image term). Stokes'
theorem on the compactified doubled space gives the reflected weight
identity: the Heisenberg case is trivial (all higher operations vanish,
$m_k=0$ for $k\ge 3$), confirming
Proposition~\ref{prop:rosetta-heisenberg-mk} by a different route.

\begin{remark}[Heisenberg as a test of the geometric Steinberg conjecture]
\label{rem:rosetta-geometric-steinberg}
\index{Steinberg!geometric conjecture!Heisenberg test}
The Heisenberg algebra verifies all three ingredients of the
geometric HT Steinberg conjecture
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:geometric-steinberg},
Example~\ref{ex:geometric-steinberg-heisenberg}):
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item $\cM_{\mathrm{vac}}(\cH_k) =
 T^*[-2]\bigl(\operatorname{Maps}(D^2, V)\bigr)$ with
 $\omega_{-2} = k \cdot \omega_{\mathrm{can}}$;
\item the Dirichlet zero section is Lagrangian;
\item the derived self-intersection recovers
 $\cH_k \simeq Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k)$.
\end{enumerate}
The clean intersection ($m_k = 0$ for $k \ge 3$,
Proposition~\ref{prop:rosetta-heisenberg-mk}) is the chiral
analogue of the abelian Steinberg variety degenerating to a point.
The excess intersection of the Virasoro fourth-order pole is the
chiral analogue of passing from torus to non-abelian Springer.
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[$E_N$ level reached by Heisenberg]
\label{rem:heisenberg-EN-level}
\index{Heisenberg algebra!$E_N$ level}
\index{E_N ladder@$E_N$ ladder!Heisenberg}
The Heisenberg algebra $\cA = \cH_k$ reaches the following
levels of the $E_N$ ladder:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $\Eone$-chiral
 (Definition~\ref{def:e1-chiral-algebra}): the OPE
 $J(z)\,J(w) \sim k/(z-w)^2$ defines $\cH_k$ as an
 $\Einf$-chiral algebra, hence \emph{a fortiori}
 $\Eone$-chiral. The $R$-matrix is
 $R(z) = \exp(k\hbar/z)$ with collision residue $k/z$
 and monodromy $\exp(-2\pi i k)$.

\item $\Etwo$-chiral on the derived center
 (Definition~\ref{def:E2-chiral-algebra}): the chiral
 Deligne conjecture equips
 $Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k)
 = C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k, \cH_k)$
 with an $\Etwo$-chiral algebra structure. This is
 automatic for every chiral algebra.

\item $\Etwo$-topological
 (Definition~\ref{def:E2-topological-algebra}):
 \textbf{not attained}. The Heisenberg algebra carries
 no conformal vector: it is not a conformal vertex algebra.
 Without a Sugawara-type stress tensor $T(z)$ satisfying
 $\{Q, G(z)\} = T(z)$, the complex-structure dependence
 on $\C$ cannot be trivialized in cohomology, and the
 topologization step
 (Construction~\ref{constr:topologization}) fails.

\item The pair
 $(Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k),\, \cH_k)$
 carries the $\SCchtop$ structure
 (bulk acting on boundary) as a first-class object.
 This is the generic situation described in
 \S\ref{subsec:ordered-three-tier}: $\SCchtop$ is
 the natural home of chiral algebras without conformal
 vector.
\end{enumerate}
Shadow class: $\mathbf{L}$ (simple poles in the $J$-$J$
OPE; the bar complex is formal and
$m_k = 0$ for $k \ge 3$ by
Proposition~\ref{prop:rosetta-heisenberg-mk}).
The obstruction to climbing higher is the absence of a
conformal vector, not any deficiency in the OPE.
\end{remark}

% ================================================================
\subsection{The three-tier $R$-matrix classification}
\label{subsec:ordered-three-tier}
\index{R-matrix!three-tier classification|textbf}
\index{three-tier classification|textbf}
% ================================================================

The Heisenberg computations reveal a complete package (operations, $R$-matrix, genus tower, PVA, Koszul dual) controlled
by a single scalar~$k$. The rest of this chapter asks: what
happens when the package is no longer controlled by a single scalar?
The answer organises all chiral algebras into three tiers by the
provenance of their spectral $R$-matrix, four depth classes by the
complexity of their Lagrangian self-intersection, and three
genus-$1$ regimes by the entanglement of curvature and braiding.
The Heisenberg sits at the simplest point of each classification;
the programme from this section onward systematically traces
what changes as the algebra grows more complex.

The Heisenberg belongs to the second of three tiers that
organise all chiral algebras by the provenance of their spectral
$R$-matrix. The three tiers are:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Pole-free commutative}:
 the OPE has no singularities, $R(z) = \tau$
 (the Koszul-signed flip), and the ordered bar complex
 descends to the symmetric bar by the na\"{\i}ve
 $\Sigma_n$-quotient.
 Examples: commutative chiral algebras in the sense of BD
 (D-schemes). None of the standard vertex algebra families
 belong to this tier, since all have OPE poles.

\item \emph{$\Einf$-chiral with OPE poles}:
 the algebra is a vertex algebra (local, $\Sigma_n$-equivariant),
 but the OPE has singularities and the spectral $R$-matrix is
 \emph{derived} from the local OPE via analytic continuation
 of the flat connection on configuration space.
 The descent $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}} \to \barBch$ is
 $R$-matrix twisted (Proposition~\ref{prop:r-matrix-descent}).
 Examples: all standard vertex algebras,
 including Heisenberg ($R = e^{k\hbar/z}$), affine Kac--Moody
 ($R = 1 + k\Omega/z + \cdots$), Virasoro, $\cW_3$, symplectic
 bosons, lattice VOAs, $\beta\gamma$, $bc_\lambda$,
 free fermions. For systems whose OPE on generators
 has only a simple pole ($\beta\gamma$, $bc_\lambda$, $\psi$),
 the $d\log$ kernel absorbs it to a constant and the
 generator-level $R$-matrix is $\tau$ or $\mathrm{Id}$;
 nevertheless these are tier~(ii), not tier~(i),
 because the OPE is singular.

\item \emph{Genuinely $\Eone$-chiral}:
 the $R$-matrix is \emph{independent input}, not derivable
 from a local OPE; the algebra is nonlocal (ordered configurations
 only, no underlying $\Sigma_n$-equivariance).
 Examples: Yangians $Y_\hbar(\fg)$, quantum vertex algebras
 in the sense of Etingof--Kazhdan.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
The tier determines three things:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*),nosep]
\item the \emph{$R$-matrix structure} ($\tau$, OPE-derived, or
 independent);
\item the \emph{ordered Koszul dual}
 ($\cA^!_{\mathrm{line}}$ carries a spectral parameter
 in tiers~(ii)--(iii), but in tier~(i) it agrees with
 the symmetric Koszul dual $\cA^!_{\mathrm{ch}}$);
\item the \emph{genus-$1$ regime} (decoupled when
 $c_0 = 0$, entangled when $c_0 \ne 0$; the decoupled
 case occurs only for $\cH_k$ among the standard
 families).
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
The examples below are organised by this classification:
$\S$\ref{subsec:cs-nonabelian-primitive-package}--\ref{subsec:symplectic-boson-ordered-bar}
treat the standard vertex algebra families (all tier~(ii));
$\S$\ref{sec:shadow-tower-atlas}--\ref{subsec:e1-ordered-bar-landscape}
assemble the complete landscape, recording the tier of each family
alongside its shadow depth class and genus-$1$ regime.
Tier~(iii) is treated in
Part~\ref{part:e1-core}\@.

The three tiers above refine to a five-term algebraic hierarchy
that organises chiral algebras by increasingly nonlocal structure.

\begin{definition}[Five-term algebraic hierarchy]
\label{def:v2-algebraic-hierarchy}
\index{algebraic hierarchy!five-term|textbf}
The algebraic hierarchy of chiral algebras, ordered by increasingly
nonlocal structure, is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:five-term-hierarchy}
 \chirCom
 \;\subset\;
 \PVA
 \;\subset\;
 \Einf\text{-chiral}
 \;\subset\;
 \Pinf\text{-chiral}
 \;\subset\;
 \Eone\text{-chiral}.
\end{equation}
Each inclusion is strict.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[The five levels]
\label{rem:v2-algebraic-hierarchy-levels}
\index{algebraic hierarchy!five levels}
The five levels are:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $\chirCom$: pole-free commutative chiral algebras.
 The OPE is trivial, the chiral product factors through
 a commutative D-module structure, and the bar complex
 descends to the symmetric bar by the na\"{\i}ve
 $\Sigma_n$-quotient.

\item $\PVA$: Poisson vertex algebras. A PVA carries a
 $\lambda$-bracket on cohomology (the classical shadow) but
 no quantum corrections; it is the semiclassical limit of a
 vertex algebra.

\item $\Einf$-chiral: all vertex algebras with local OPE.
 This is the standard setting of Beilinson--Drinfeld~\cite{BD04}
 and Frenkel--Ben-Zvi~\cite{FBZ04}. Every standard vertex
 algebra (Heisenberg, affine Kac--Moody, Virasoro,
 $\mathcal{W}$-algebras, lattice VOAs, $\beta\gamma$,
 $bc_\lambda$, free fermions) belongs to this level: the OPE
 is local and the algebra carries $\Sigma_n$-equivariance
 on configuration spaces.

\item $\Pinf$-chiral: homotopy-coherent intermediate algebras.
 A $\Pinf$-chiral algebra is homotopy-commutative but not
 strictly commutative; this level arises in the deformation
 quantisation of PVAs and in the homotopy transfer of
 $\Einf$-structures along quasi-isomorphisms.

\item $\Eone$-chiral: fully nonlocal chiral algebras.
 The $R$-matrix is independent input, not derivable from a
 local OPE. This is the natural home of Yangian $R$-matrices
 $Y_\hbar(\fg)$ and quantum vertex algebras in the sense of
 Etingof--Kazhdan. The ordered bar complex
 $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}$ lives here; it has no
 underlying $\Sigma_n$-equivariance.
\end{enumerate}
The hierarchy collapses under the forgetful functor: every
$\Eone$-chiral algebra has an underlying $\Einf$-chiral
algebra obtained by forgetting the nonlocal data, and every
$\Einf$-chiral algebra has an underlying PVA obtained by
passing to the classical limit.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Nonabelian Chern--Simons: the primitive package}
\label{subsec:cs-nonabelian-primitive-package}
\index{Chern--Simons!nonabelian!primitive package|textbf}
\index{affine Kac--Moody!as boundary chart}

The Heisenberg algebra is the boundary chart for abelian
Chern--Simons. The nonabelian case $G$ (complex algebraic,
Lie algebra~$\fg$, level~$k$) produces the same architecture
with the affine Kac--Moody vertex algebra $V_k(\fg)$ as boundary
chart.

\noindent\textbf{Boundary algebra (chart).}
The boundary chiral algebra is $A = V_k(\fg)$, the affine
vertex algebra at level~$k$
(Frenkel--Ben-Zvi \cite{FBZ04}).
Generators: currents $J^a(z)$, $a = 1, \ldots, \dim \fg$.
OPE relations:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:cs-km-ope}
J^a(z)\, J^b(w)
\;\sim\;
\frac{k\,\kappa^{ab}}{(z-w)^2}
\;+\;
\frac{f^{ab}{}_c\, J^c(w)}{z-w},
\end{equation}
where $\kappa^{ab}$ is the Killing form and $f^{ab}{}_c$
are the structure constants of~$\fg$. In modes:
$[J^a_m, J^b_n] = f^{ab}{}_c\, J^c_{m+n}
+ k\, m\, \kappa^{ab}\, \delta_{m+n,0}$.

\noindent\textbf{Open category (primitive).}
$\cC^{\mathrm{op}} = \cC_{\mathrm{CS}(G,k)}^{\mathrm{op}}$
is the factorization dg-category of boundary
line and junction operators on the holomorphic boundary
curve~$X$, with punctures at Wilson-line endpoints.
The local construction is a theorem
(Costello--Gwilliam \cite{CG17}); the global cosheaf
structure is part of the programme of
Section~\ref{subsec:modular-holography-programme}.
A vacuum boundary condition $b_{\mathrm{WZW}}$ gives the
local chart
$A = \mathrm{End}(b_{\mathrm{WZW}}) \simeq V_k(\fg)$.
At rational/integrable levels, the decategorified shadow
is the modular tensor category of
Chern--Simons/WZW Wilson lines.

\noindent\textbf{Bulk (derived center).}
$Z = C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(V_k(\fg), V_k(\fg))$,
the chiral derived center.
This is a distinct object from the bar complex:
$\bar{B}(V_k(\fg))$ classifies twisting morphisms
(couplings between $A$ and $A^!$),
while $Z$ classifies bulk observables acting on
the boundary
(Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:thqg-swiss-cheese}).

\noindent\textbf{Shadow archetype.}
Class~$\mathbf{L}$ (Lie/tree): shadow depth
$r_{\max} = 3$. The cubic shadow
$C_\fg = f^{ab}{}_c$ encodes the Lie bracket;
the quartic contact invariant vanishes
by the Jacobi identity
(Volume~I).

\noindent\textbf{Modular data.}
$\kappa(V_k(\fg)) = \dim(\fg) \cdot (k + h^\vee)/(2h^\vee)$,
where $h^\vee$ is the dual Coxeter number.
The Koszul dual
$V_k(\fg)^! = \mathrm{CE}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\fg_{-k-2h^\vee})$
has modular characteristic
$\kappa(V_k(\fg)^!) = -\kappa(V_k(\fg))$
by the level shift $k \mapsto -k - 2h^\vee$,
giving complementarity
$\kappa + \kappa' = 0$.
(The Koszul dual is the chiral CE algebra, not
$V_{-k-2h^\vee}(\fg)$ itself; these share the
same~$\kappa$ but are categorically distinct.)
The genus tower on the proved scalar lane is
$F_g = \kappa(V_k(\fg)) \cdot
\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ at all genera (Volume~I, Theorem~D).

\noindent\textbf{Koszul dual: explicit generators and relations.}
\label{par:cs-koszul-dual-explicit}%
\index{Chern--Simons!Koszul dual!explicit generators|textbf}%
\index{Yangian!dg-shifted!Chern--Simons}%
The Koszul dual $A^! = Y_\hbar^{\mathrm{dg}}(\fg)$ is the
dg-shifted Yangian constructed from the bar complex of
$V_k(\fg)$ (Volume~I,
Theorem~\ref*{thm:Koszul_dual_Yangian};
\cite{DNP25}). We give the
explicit presentation in modes and generating functions,
first for general~$\fg$ and then for $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_2$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{General $\fg$.}
The algebra $A^!$ is generated by modes
\begin{equation}\label{eq:cs-dual-generators}
B_n^a \;\;(\text{even, degree $0$}),
\qquad
c_n^a \;\;(\text{odd, degree $-1$}),
\qquad
n \ge 0,\quad a = 1, \ldots, \dim \fg,
\end{equation}
with algebraic relations
\begin{equation}\label{eq:cs-dual-BB}
[B_n^a,\, B_m^b] \;=\; f^{ab}{}_{c}\, B_{n+m}^c,
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:cs-dual-Bc}
[B_n^a,\, c_m^b] \;=\; f^{ab}{}_{c}\, c_{n+m}^c,
\end{equation}
and differential $Q$ (cohomological, $|Q| = +1$) given by
\begin{align}
Q(c_n^a)
&\;=\;
\tfrac{1}{2}\, f^{a}{}_{bc}
\sum_{\substack{r+s = n-1 \\ r,s \ge 0}} c_r^b\, c_s^c,
\label{eq:cs-Q-ghost}
\\[4pt]
Q(B_n^a)
&\;=\;
n\,(k - h^\vee)\,\kappa^{ab}\, c_{n-1}^b
\;+\;
f^{a}{}_{bc}
\sum_{\substack{r+s = n-1 \\ r,s \ge 0}}
B_s^c\, c_r^b,
\label{eq:cs-Q-current}
\end{align}
where $h^\vee$ is the dual Coxeter number and $\kappa^{ab}$
the Killing form, both evaluated in a Killing-orthonormal basis
for~$\fg$ simple.
The even generators~\eqref{eq:cs-dual-BB} form the
enveloping algebra $U(\fg[t])$ of the polynomial current
algebra; the full structure
$Q^2 = 0$ is the dg deformation at level~$k$.
In generating-function form, with
$B^a(u) := \sum_{n \ge 0} B_n^a\, u^{-n-1}$
and
$c^a(u) := \sum_{n \ge 0} c_n^a\, u^{-n-1}$,
\begin{align}
Q\, c^a(u)
&\;=\;
\tfrac{1}{2}\, f^{a}{}_{bc}\; c^b(u)\, c^c(u),
\label{eq:cs-Q-ghost-gf}
\\[4pt]
Q\, B^a(u)
&\;=\;
-(k + h^\vee)\,\kappa^{ab}\,\partial_u c^b(u)
