\;+\;
f^{a}{}_{bc}\; c^b(u)\, B^c(u),
\label{eq:cs-Q-current-gf}
\end{align}
where the sign and shift
$k - h^\vee \mapsto -(k + h^\vee)$ in passing to
generating functions absorbs the normal-ordering correction
$h^{ab} = h^\vee \kappa^{ab}$ from the
Casimir contraction
$h^{ab} := \tfrac{1}{2}\,
f^{a}{}_{Lc}\, f^{b\,c}{}_{L}$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Specialisation: $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_2$.}
The dual Coxeter number is $h^\vee = 2$.
In the Killing-orthonormal basis $\{t^a\}_{a=1}^3$
with $[t^a, t^b] = \epsilon^{abc}\, t^c$ and
$\kappa^{ab} = \delta^{ab}$,
the differential~\eqref{eq:cs-Q-ghost-gf}--\eqref{eq:cs-Q-current-gf}
reads
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-Q-orthonormal}
Q\, c^a(u)
\;=\;
\tfrac{1}{2}\,\epsilon^{a}{}_{bc}\, c^b(u)\, c^c(u),
\qquad
Q\, B^a(u)
\;=\;
-(k + 2)\,\partial_u c^a(u)
\;+\;
\epsilon^{a}{}_{bc}\, c^b(u)\, B^c(u).
\end{equation}
The even subalgebra generated by the $B^a_n$
satisfies $[B^a_n, B^b_m] = \epsilon^{ab}{}_{c}\, B^c_{n+m}$
and is isomorphic to $U(\mathfrak{sl}_2[t])$;
the differential $Q$ deforms it at level~$k$.

Pass to the Chevalley basis $\{e, f, h\}$
($[h,e] = 2e$, $[h,f] = -2f$, $[e,f] = h$,
Killing form $\kappa(h,h) = 2$,
$\kappa(e,f) = 1$).
Write $E_n := B_n^e$, $F_n := B_n^f$,
$H_n := B_n^h$ for the even modes, and
$\epsilon_n := c_n^e$, $\varphi_n := c_n^f$,
$\eta_n := c_n^h$ for the ghost modes.
The current-algebra relations are
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-yangian-modes}
\begin{aligned}
{[H_n,\, E_m]} &= 2\, E_{n+m},
&\qquad
{[H_n,\, F_m]} &= -2\, F_{n+m},
\\[3pt]
{[E_n,\, F_m]} &= H_{n+m},
&\qquad
{[H_n,\, H_m]} &= 0.
\end{aligned}
\end{equation}
The differential $Q$ acts on the even
generators by
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-Q-EFH}
\begin{aligned}
Q(E_n)
&\;=\;
n(k-2)\,\varphi_{n-1}
\;+\;
2\!\!\sum_{\substack{r+s=n-1\\r,s\ge 0}}
\bigl(
 E_s\, \eta_r
 \;-\;
 H_s\, \epsilon_r
\bigr),
\\[4pt]
Q(F_n)
&\;=\;
n(k-2)\,\epsilon_{n-1}
\;+\;
2\!\!\sum_{\substack{r+s=n-1\\r,s\ge 0}}
\bigl(
 H_s\, \varphi_r
 \;-\;
 F_s\, \eta_r
\bigr),
\\[4pt]
Q(H_n)
&\;=\;
\tfrac{n(k-2)}{2}\,\eta_{n-1}
\;+\;
\sum_{\substack{r+s=n-1\\r,s\ge 0}}
\bigl(
 F_s\, \epsilon_r
 \;-\;
 E_s\, \varphi_r
\bigr),
\end{aligned}
\end{equation}
where the off-diagonal Killing form
$\kappa^{ef} = 1$, $\kappa^{hh} = \tfrac{1}{2}$
accounts for the cross-pairing $E \leftrightarrow
\varphi$, $F \leftrightarrow \epsilon$ in the
linear term and the $\tfrac{1}{2}$ on the
Cartan line.
The coefficient $k - h^\vee = k - 2$ vanishes at the
critical level $k = -h^\vee = -2$ (equivalently
$k_{\mathrm{ren}} = k + h^\vee = 0$):
the linear term in $Q$ drops out, the differential reduces
to the Chevalley--Eilenberg differential of
$\mathfrak{sl}_2[t]$, and the Sugawara construction
degenerates.

The generating series of the even modes are
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-dual-generators}
E(u) := \sum_{n \ge 0} E_n\, u^{-n-1},
\quad
F(u) := \sum_{n \ge 0} F_n\, u^{-n-1},
\quad
H(u) := \sum_{n \ge 0} H_n\, u^{-n-1}.
\end{equation}
On cohomology, the even sector survives: the Yangian
$Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_2) = H^0(A^!, Q)$ is
generated by $E(u)$, $F(u)$, $H(u)$ with the
RTT relations
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-RTT}
R_{12}(u - v)\, T_1(u)\, T_2(v)
\;=\;
T_2(v)\, T_1(u)\, R_{12}(u - v),
\end{equation}
where $T(u) = \bigl(\begin{smallmatrix}
k_1(u) & F(u) \\ E(u) & k_2(u)
\end{smallmatrix}\bigr)$ is the Gauss-decomposed
transfer matrix, $R(u) = 1 + \hbar\, P/u$ the
Yang $R$-matrix ($P$ the permutation on
$\bC^2 \otimes \bC^2$), and
$H(u) = k_1(u)/k_2(u)$.
The FRT expansion of~\eqref{eq:sl2-RTT} gives, among
others, the Drinfeld relations
\begin{align}
(u - v - \hbar)\, E(u)\, E(v)
&\;=\;
(u - v + \hbar)\, E(v)\, E(u),
\label{eq:cs-drinfeld-EE}
\\[3pt]
[E(u),\, F(v)]
&\;=\;
\frac{\hbar}{u - v}
\bigl(k_1(u)\, k_2(v) - k_1(v)\, k_2(u)\bigr),
\label{eq:cs-drinfeld-EF}
\end{align}
which encode the spectral OPE of line operators
on the holomorphic boundary
(Section~\ref{subsec:spectral-ope-and-yangian}).
The passage from the dg presentation
\eqref{eq:sl2-yangian-modes}--\eqref{eq:sl2-Q-EFH}
to the RTT form~\eqref{eq:sl2-RTT} is the
content of the bar--cobar Quillen equivalence
(Volume~I, Theorem~B) applied to the affine
boundary chart: the twisting morphism extracted
from the bar complex of $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
yields the rational $r$-matrix
$r(z) = k\,\Omega/z$ (with $\Omega$ the Casimir
element of $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ and $k$ the level), whose quantisation
is the Yang $R$-matrix above.

\begin{computation}[The $\mathfrak{sl}_3$ Yangian: adjacent roots and the triangle coefficient; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:sl3-yangian-triangle}%
\index{Yangian!sl3 triangle@$\mathfrak{sl}_3$ triangle coefficient}%
\index{triangle sector!explicit for sl3@explicit for $\mathfrak{sl}_3$}%
The rank-$2$ case $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_3$ is the first where
composite roots, triangle sectors, and Serre relations become
visible. Simple roots $\alpha_1, \alpha_2$ with Cartan matrix
$\bigl(\begin{smallmatrix} 2 & -1 \\ -1 & 2
\end{smallmatrix}\bigr)$;
composite root $\alpha_{12} = \alpha_1 + \alpha_2$ with
generators $e_{12} = [e_1, e_2]$, $f_{12} = [f_2, f_1]$.
In the defining representation ($E_{ij}$ = matrix units of
$\mathfrak{gl}_3$): $e_1 = E_{12}$, $e_2 = E_{23}$,
$e_{12} = E_{13}$.

The \emph{triangle sectors} on three tensor factors are
\[
T^L_{12} = E_{13}^{(1)}\,E_{21}^{(2)}\,E_{32}^{(3)},
\qquad
T^L_{21} = E_{13}^{(1)}\,E_{32}^{(2)}\,E_{21}^{(3)},
\]
carrying weights $(\alpha_{12},\,-\alpha_1,\,-\alpha_2)$ and
$(\alpha_{12},\,-\alpha_2,\,-\alpha_1)$ respectively.
The triangle localization formula
(Theorem~\ref{thm:triangle-localization}), with
$S_{ab}(u) = \sum_\alpha \rho_\alpha(u)\,E_\alpha^{(a)}F_\alpha^{(b)}$
the two-body spectral kernel, computes
\[
\Pi_{\langle T^L_{12},\,T^L_{21}\rangle}
\tfrac12[S_{12}(w),\,S_{13}(w{+}z)]
\;=\;
\frac{1}{2}\,\rho_1(w)\,\rho_2(w{+}z)\,T^L_{12}
\;-\;
\frac{1}{2}\,\rho_2(w)\,\rho_1(w{+}z)\,T^L_{21},
\]
where $E_i^{(a)} := e_i$ acting on tensor factor~$a$, and the
commutators $[E_1^{(1)}F_1^{(2)},\,
E_2^{(1)}F_2^{(3)}] = E_{12}^{(1)}F_1^{(2)}F_2^{(3)}$
and $[E_2^{(1)}F_2^{(2)},\,E_1^{(1)}F_1^{(3)}]
= -E_{12}^{(1)}F_2^{(2)}F_1^{(3)}$ each contribute one
triangle vector. Under the normalised rational ansatz
$\rho_i(u) = 1/u$, adjacent-root rigidity
(Theorem~\ref{thm:adjacent-root-rigidity}) forces
\[
\lambda^L_{12} = \lambda^L_{21}
= \lambda^R_{12} = \lambda^R_{21}
= \frac{c_1 c_2}{2\,c_{12}}
\;=\;\frac12.
\]
This is the universal coefficient
$\frac1n\big|_{n=2} = \int_0^1(1-t)\,dt$
from the Dynkin--BCH beta integral
(Theorem~\ref{thm:dynkin-bch-path}).

The \emph{Serre relation} $[e_1,[e_1,e_2]] = 0$ has
a root-space origin: the weight $2\alpha_1 + \alpha_2$ is
\emph{not} a root of $\mathfrak{sl}_3$, so
$(\mathfrak{sl}_3)_{2\alpha_1 + \alpha_2} = 0$ and
every multilinear Lie monomial of that weight vanishes.
In the bar complex, the degree-$3$ element
$[s^{-1}e_1\,|\,s^{-1}e_1\,|\,s^{-1}e_2]$ vanishes in
bar homology: its boundary at $D_{1,2}$ vanishes
($[e_1,e_1] = 0$) and its boundary at $D_{2,3}$ produces
$[s^{-1}e_1\,|\,s^{-1}e_{12}]$, whose own boundary
$[e_1, e_{12}] = 0$ by the Serre relation; the weight
space $(\mathfrak{sl}_3)_{2\alpha_1+\alpha_2} = 0$
forces the entire sector to be acyclic. The Yangian Serre relation
$\mathrm{Sym}_{r_1,r_2}[x^+_{1,r_1},[x^+_{1,r_2},
x^+_{2,s}]] = 0$ follows by the same mechanism at all mode
levels.
\end{computation}

\begin{remark}[$E_N$ level reached by $V_k(\fg)$ at non-critical level]
\label{rem:km-EN-level}
\index{Kac--Moody!$E_N$ level}
\index{E_N ladder@$E_N$ ladder!Kac--Moody}
For $k \ne -h^\vee$ (non-critical level), the affine
Kac--Moody vertex algebra $\cA = V_k(\fg)$ reaches the
top of the $E_N$ ladder:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $\Eone$-chiral
 (Definition~\ref{def:e1-chiral-algebra}): the current
 OPE~\eqref{eq:cs-km-ope} gives $V_k(\fg)$ the
 structure of an $\Einf$-chiral algebra, hence
 \emph{a fortiori} $\Eone$-chiral.
 The $R$-matrix is $R(z) = 1 + \hbar\,\Omega/z + \cdots$
 with $\Omega$ the Casimir of~$\fg$.

\item $\Etwo$-chiral on the derived center
 (Definition~\ref{def:E2-chiral-algebra}): automatic from
 the chiral Deligne conjecture.

\item $\Etwo$-topological
 (Definition~\ref{def:E2-topological-algebra}): the
 Sugawara construction provides a conformal vector
 $T_{\mathrm{Sug}}(z)
 = \frac{1}{2(k + h^\vee)}
 \sum_a {:}\!J^a J^a\!{:}(z)$
 of central charge $c = k\dim\fg/(k + h^\vee)$.
 At $k \ne -h^\vee$ this is well-defined, and
 Construction~\ref{constr:topologization} trivializes the
 complex-structure dependence in cohomology.

\item $\Ethree$-chiral: the 3d holomorphic-topological
 theory is holomorphic Chern--Simons on $\C \times \R$,
 descended from the 6d holomorphic gauge theory
 (Costello--Li). The boundary of the 3d HT theory is
 $V_k(\fg)$.

\item $\Ethree$-topological
 (Definition~\ref{def:E3-topological-algebra}): both
 requirements are met---the 3d HT theory exists
 (holomorphic CS) and the conformal vector exists
 (Sugawara at $k \ne -h^\vee$). The derived chiral
 center $Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(V_k(\fg))$
 carries a genuine $\Ethree$-topological algebra
 structure, independent of the complex structure on
 $\C$. This is the Chern--Simons TQFT, and it is the
 example where Conjecture~\ref{conj:E3-topological-climax}
 is proved.
\end{enumerate}
Shadow class: $\mathbf{L}$ (double poles from the
Sugawara stress tensor; $m_k = 0$ for $k \ge 3$ by
Jacobi termination, \S\ref{subsec:affine-shadow}).
The affine Kac--Moody family at non-critical level is the
unique standard family that reaches $\Ethree$-topological
unconditionally.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[$E_N$ level at the critical level $k = -h^\vee$]
\label{rem:critical-level-EN}
\index{critical level!$E_N$ obstruction}
\index{Feigin--Frenkel center!$E_N$ level}
\index{E_N ladder@$E_N$ ladder!critical level}
At $k = -h^\vee$, the Sugawara denominator $k + h^\vee$
vanishes and the conformal vector is undefined. The
$E_N$ ladder for $V_{-h^\vee}(\fg)$ terminates at
$\Etwo$-chiral:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $\Eone$-chiral and $\Etwo$-chiral on the derived
 center: both automatic, as for any chiral algebra.
 At the critical level the center
 $Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(V_{-h^\vee}(\fg))$
 contains the Feigin--Frenkel center $\fz(\hat\fg)$,
 which is large (isomorphic to
 $\operatorname{Fun}\operatorname{Op}_{\fg^\vee}(D^\times)$).

\item $\Etwo$-topological: \textbf{not attained}.
 Without a conformal vector, the topologization step
 (Construction~\ref{constr:topologization}) fails.
 The holomorphic direction carries nontrivial
 cohomological information that cannot be trivialized.

\item $\Ethree$-chiral and $\Ethree$-topological:
 \textbf{not attained}. The jump of the center at
 $k = -h^\vee$ obstructs both the 3d HT construction
 and the topologization.
\end{enumerate}
The critical level is stuck at $\SCchtop$ with an
enlarged center---the geometric Langlands regime. Shadow
class: $\mathbf{L}$ (the OPE pole structure is
unchanged from non-critical level; the obstruction is
to the conformal vector, not to the shadow tower).
\end{remark}

\subsection{Wakimoto realisation: bar-cobar commutes with free-field embedding}%
\label{subsec:wakimoto-ordered-bar}%
\index{Wakimoto realisation!ordered bar complex|textbf}%
\index{free-field realisation!bar-cobar compatibility}

The Wakimoto realisation of $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ is the
free-field embedding
$\iota_W \colon V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2) \hookrightarrow
\cH_k \otimes \beta\gamma$
into a tensor product of a Heisenberg algebra and a
$\beta\gamma$ system. The compatibility of bar-cobar with
this embedding is a worked verification of the general
principle that bar-cobar commutes with free-field realisations.

\begin{computation}[Wakimoto bar-cobar compatibility;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:wakimoto-bar-cobar}%
\index{Wakimoto realisation!bar complex}%
\index{Wakimoto realisation!Koszul dual}%
\index{free-field realisation!bar complex}%
The Wakimoto realisation embeds the $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$
currents into a Heisenberg field $a(z)$ (level~$k$) and a
$\beta\gamma$ pair via
\begin{equation}\label{eq:wakimoto-embedding}
\begin{aligned}
J^+(z) &\;=\; \beta(z)\,, \\
J^0(z) &\;=\; {:}\beta(z)\gamma(z){:} + a(z)\,, \\
J^-(z) &\;=\; {:}\beta(z)\gamma(z)\gamma(z){:}
 + (k+2)\,\partial\gamma(z)
 + a(z)\gamma(z)\,.
\end{aligned}
\end{equation}
The three currents satisfy the $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$ OPE
at level~$k$ as a consequence of the free-field OPE relations
$a(z)\,a(w) \sim k/(z-w)^2$,\;
$\beta(z)\,\gamma(w) \sim 1/(z-w)$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Bar complex compatibility.}
The embedding $\iota_W$ induces a coalgebra map on bar
complexes:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:wakimoto-bar-map}
\barBch(\iota_W) \;\colon\;
\barBch(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2))
\;\longrightarrow\;
\barBch(\cH_k \otimes \beta\gamma)\,.
\end{equation}
The source is class~$\mathbf{L}$ (depth~$3$,
Computation~\ref{comp:lattice-voa-ordered-bar} at
$k = 1$, and the general affine case at arbitrary~$k$).
The target is the tensor product of two bar complexes:
$\barBch(\cH_k)$ (class~$\mathbf{G}$, depth~$2$)
and $\barBch(\beta\gamma)$ (class~$\mathbf{C}$,
depth~$4$ on composites).
The bar map preserves the coalgebra structure and
intertwines the bar differentials.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Cobar compatibility and Koszul dual.}
Applying $\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}$ to both sides of
\eqref{eq:wakimoto-bar-map}, the cobar functor commutes
with the embedding:
\[
\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}(\barBch(\iota_W))
\;\colon\;
V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)
\;\xrightarrow{\;\sim\;}
\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}\bigl(
\barBch(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2))\bigr)
\;\longrightarrow\;
\cH_k \otimes \beta\gamma\,.
\]
At the level of Koszul duals, the map induces
\begin{equation}\label{eq:wakimoto-koszul}
Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_2)
\;=\;
V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)^!
\;\longrightarrow\;
(\cH_k)^! \otimes (bc)
\;=\;
\mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*) \otimes bc\,,
\end{equation}
embedding the Yangian into a tensor product of the Heisenberg
Koszul dual and the $bc$ system. This is the Koszul-dual
shadow of the Wakimoto embedding: the Yangian inherits a
free-field presentation from the free-field realisation
of the original affine algebra.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{$R$-matrix compatibility.}
The Yang $R$-matrix
$R(z) = 1 + k\Omega/z$ of $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
decomposes under the Wakimoto embedding as a product:
$R_{\mathrm{Wak}}(z) = R_{\cH}(z) \cdot R_{\beta\gamma}$,
where $R_{\cH}(z) = e^{k\hbar/z}$ (the Heisenberg
exponential $R$-matrix) and
$R_{\beta\gamma} = \mathrm{Id}$ (trivial on generators).
The Lie-bracket contributions to the $\mathfrak{sl}_2$
Casimir $\Omega$ arise from the composite sector of
$\beta\gamma$ (the ghost current $J_{bc} = {:}\beta\gamma{:}$).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Depth analysis.}
The Wakimoto embedding witnesses the depth upgrade from
$\mathbf{G}$ (Heisenberg) and $\mathbf{C}$ ($\beta\gamma$)
to $\mathbf{L}$ ($V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$): the simple-pole
terms in $J^-(z)$ (specifically the $a(z)\gamma(z)$ coupling)
introduce a Lie-bracket interaction that is absent in either
free-field factor alone. The composition of two abelian
systems produces a non-abelian system: the Wakimoto realisation
is the mechanism by which class~$\mathbf{G}$ components
assemble into class~$\mathbf{L}$.
\end{computation}

\subsection{The lattice VOA $V_{\sqrt{2}\Z}$: class~L from vertex operators}%
\label{subsec:lattice-voa-ordered-bar}%
\index{lattice VOA!ordered bar complex|textbf}%
\index{Koszul duality!lattice VOA}

The shadow obstruction tower atlas
(Computation~\ref{comp:shadow-tower-atlas}) lists $V_\Lambda$
as class~$\mathbf{G}$ when restricted to the momentum
sublattice (the Heisenberg currents $J_\alpha$). The full
lattice VOA $V_\Lambda$ with its vertex operators
$e^\alpha$ ($\alpha \in \Lambda$) belongs to class~$\mathbf{L}$:
the OPE of vertex operators has a simple pole producing a
Lie-bracket term, and the Jacobi identity terminates the
shadow obstruction tower at depth~$3$.

We compute the case $\Lambda = \sqrt{2}\,\Z$, the
$A_1$ root lattice, where $V_\Lambda \cong L_1(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
(the integrable vacuum module of $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$
at level~$1$).

\begin{computation}[Lattice VOA ordered bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:lattice-voa-ordered-bar}%
\index{lattice VOA!A1 root lattice@$A_1$ root lattice!bar complex}%
\index{lattice VOA!depth spectrum}%
\index{Yangian!lattice VOA Koszul dual}%
The lattice $\Lambda = \sqrt{2}\,\Z$ has rank~$1$,
Gram matrix $(\alpha, \alpha) = 2$, and root system
$\Phi = \{\pm\alpha\}$ where $\alpha = \sqrt{2}$. The
lattice VOA $V_\Lambda$ has generators:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item the Heisenberg current $J(z)$ with
 $J(z)\,J(w) \sim 1/(z-w)^2$
 (level $k = 1$ normalisation);
\item vertex operators $e^{\pm\alpha}(z)$ of
 conformal weight~$1$, with OPE
 \begin{align}
 e^\alpha(z)\, e^{-\alpha}(w)
 &\;\sim\;
 \frac{1}{(z-w)^2}
 \;+\;
 \frac{\alpha \cdot J(w)}{z-w}\,,
 \label{eq:lattice-vertex-ope}
 \\[3pt]
 J(z)\, e^{\pm\alpha}(w)
 &\;\sim\;
 \frac{\pm\alpha\, e^{\pm\alpha}(w)}{z-w}\,,
 \label{eq:lattice-current-vertex-ope}
 \\[3pt]
 e^{\alpha}(z)\, e^{\alpha}(w)
 &\;\sim\; 0\,.
 \label{eq:lattice-vertex-vertex-vanishing}
 \end{align}
\end{itemize}
The isomorphism $V_\Lambda \cong L_1(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
sends $J \mapsto h/\sqrt{2}$,
$e^\alpha \mapsto e$, $e^{-\alpha} \mapsto f$,
recovering the $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$ OPE at $k = 1$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Depth spectrum: $\{1,2\}$.}
The OPE~\eqref{eq:lattice-vertex-ope} has both a double pole
(depth~$1$, the Killing form: $\kappa(e^\alpha, e^{-\alpha}) = 1$)
and a simple pole (depth~$2$, the Lie bracket:
$[e^\alpha, e^{-\alpha}] = \alpha \cdot J$). The depth spectrum
is $\{1, 2\}$, matching $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ at $k = 1$.
This is class~$\mathbf{L}$, not class~$\mathbf{G}$:
the vertex operators lift the momentum algebra from depth~$\{1\}$
to depth~$\{1,2\}$.
The Virasoro sub-sector is absent (no weight-$2$ generator), so the weight-depth identity (Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)) is vacuously satisfied; the depth spectrum is controlled by the Lie bracket truncation instead.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Operations: $m_3 \ne 0$, $m_4 = 0$.}
The binary operation decomposes as
$m_2(e^\alpha, e^{-\alpha};\, \lambda)
= \lambda + \alpha \cdot J$
(double pole $\leadsto \lambda$; simple pole $\leadsto$ Lie bracket).
The ternary operation $m_3$ is nonzero on the triple
$(e^\alpha, e^{-\alpha}, e^\alpha)$: the iterated OPE
produces a Lie-bracket composition
$[e^\alpha, [e^{-\alpha}, e^\alpha]] = [e^\alpha, -\alpha J]
= +\alpha^2\, e^\alpha = 2\, e^\alpha$.
The quartic operation $m_4 = 0$ by the Jacobi identity:
the weight $2\alpha$ is not a root
($e^{2\alpha}$ does not exist in the lattice VOA
since $(2\alpha, 2\alpha) = 8 > 2$), forcing the
obstruction to vanish. The tower terminates at depth~$3$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{$r$-matrix and Koszul dual.}
The collision residue is
$r(z) = k\,\Omega/z$ at $k = 1$, where
$\Omega = e^\alpha \otimes e^{-\alpha}
+ e^{-\alpha} \otimes e^{\alpha}
+ \tfrac{1}{2} J \otimes J$
is the $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ Casimir and $k = 1$ is the
lattice level (the $k = 0$ limit gives the abelian
Heisenberg r-matrix $r = 0$ on the Cartan, consistent
).
The quantisation of $r(z) = k\,\Omega/z$ is the
Yang $R$-matrix $R(z) = 1 + k\hbar\,\Omega/z$,
and the Koszul dual is the Yangian
$Y_{1/3}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
(the $k = 1$ specialisation of the general affine
Koszul dual
$A^! = Y_\hbar^{\mathrm{dg}}(\fg)$).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Serre relation = root-space vanishing.}
The Serre relation $[e^\alpha, [e^\alpha, e^{-\alpha}]] = 0$
has a root-space origin: $2\alpha - \alpha = \alpha$ is a root,
but $[e^\alpha, e^\alpha] = 0$
(equation~\eqref{eq:lattice-vertex-vertex-vanishing})
because $(\alpha, \alpha) = 2 > 0$ (same-sign vertex
operators have no singular OPE). In the bar complex,
this forces the degree-$3$ element
$[s^{-1}e^\alpha\,|\,s^{-1}e^\alpha\,|\,s^{-1}e^{-\alpha}]$
to be exact, by the same mechanism as the $\mathfrak{sl}_3$
Serre relation
(Computation~\ref{comp:sl3-yangian-triangle}).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Genus-$1$.}
Since $c_0 = \Omega \ne 0$ (the Lie bracket is
nonvanishing), the lattice VOA at level~$1$ is
propagator-entangled at genus~$1$: the $r$-matrix
becomes elliptic,
$r^{E_\tau}(z) = \Omega \cdot \zeta(z|\tau) + \kappa \cdot \wp(z|\tau)$,
with $B$-cycle monodromy $2\eta_\tau \cdot \Omega$.
The shadow Hessian is $S_2 = c/2 = 1/2$
(the $k = 1$, $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ value:
$S_2 = \dim(\mathfrak{sl}_2)\cdot k/(2(k+h^\vee)) = 3/(2 \cdot 3) = 1/2$;
the Volume~I modular characteristic is
$\kappa = \dim(\mathfrak{sl}_2)(k+h^\vee)/(2h^\vee) = 9/4$).
\end{computation}

\begin{remark}[Lattice atlas correction]%
\label{rem:lattice-atlas-correction}%
\index{lattice VOA!atlas classification}%
The shadow obstruction tower atlas entry for $V_\Lambda$ as
class~$\mathbf{G}$ (depth~$2$) applies to the
\emph{momentum sublattice} only: the Heisenberg
currents $J_i(z)$ ($i = 1, \ldots, \operatorname{rk}(\Lambda)$)
with $J_i(z)\, J_j(w) \sim (\alpha_i, \alpha_j)/(z-w)^2$
have scalar OPE residues and no simple pole. The
full lattice VOA with vertex operators $e^\alpha$
($\alpha \in \Lambda$) is class~$\mathbf{L}$ whenever
$\Lambda$ has roots: the simple-pole OPE
$e^\alpha(z)\,e^{-\alpha}(w) \sim \cdots + (\alpha \cdot J)/(z-w)$
introduces a Lie bracket. The atlas entry is refined
accordingly: $V_\Lambda(\mathrm{mom.})$ is
class~$\mathbf{G}$; $V_\Lambda(\mathrm{v.o.})$ is
class~$\mathbf{L}$.
\end{remark}

\begin{computation}[$A_2$ lattice VOA ordered bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:lattice-voa-A2-ordered-bar}%
\index{lattice VOA!A2 root lattice@$A_2$ root lattice!bar complex}%
\index{lattice VOA!rank 2}%
\index{Yangian!sl3@$\mathfrak{sl}_3$!from lattice VOA}%
The $A_2$ root lattice $\Lambda = \Z\alpha_1 \oplus \Z\alpha_2$
with Gram matrix
$\bigl(\begin{smallmatrix} 2 & -1 \\ -1 & 2
\end{smallmatrix}\bigr)$
has rank~$2$, root system $\Phi = \{\pm\alpha_1, \pm\alpha_2,
\pm(\alpha_1+\alpha_2)\}$ of type~$A_2$, and the lattice VOA
$V_\Lambda \cong L_1(\mathfrak{sl}_3)$ is the integrable vacuum
module of $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3$ at level~$1$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Generators.}
Two Heisenberg currents $J_1, J_2$ spanning the Cartan,
and six vertex operators $e^{\pm\alpha_1}, e^{\pm\alpha_2},
e^{\pm(\alpha_1+\alpha_2)}$ of conformal weight~$1$,
giving $\dim(\fg) = 8$ generators total.
The OPE structure:
\begin{align}
J_i(z)\,J_j(w) &\;\sim\; \frac{(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)}{(z-w)^2}\,,
\label{eq:A2-cartan-ope}
\\[3pt]
J_i(z)\,e^{\pm\alpha_j}(w) &\;\sim\;
\frac{\pm(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)\,e^{\pm\alpha_j}(w)}{z-w}\,,
\\[3pt]
e^{\alpha_i}(z)\,e^{-\alpha_j}(w)
&\;\sim\;
\delta_{ij}\biggl(
\frac{1}{(z-w)^2}
+ \frac{\alpha_i \cdot J(w)}{z-w}\biggr)
+ (1-\delta_{ij})\,
\frac{\epsilon_{ij}\,e^{\alpha_i-\alpha_j}(w)}{z-w}\,,
\label{eq:A2-vertex-ope}
\end{align}
where $\epsilon_{ij} = \pm 1$ is the cocycle sign
($\epsilon_{12} = 1$, $\epsilon_{21} = -1$). The composite
root vertex operator satisfies
$e^{\alpha_1+\alpha_2} = [e^{\alpha_1}, e^{\alpha_2}]$
(the Lie bracket).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Depth spectrum: $\{1,2\}$, class~$\mathbf{L}$, depth~$3$.}
As for $A_1$, the double poles between opposite-root vertex
operators give depth~$1$ (Killing form) and the simple poles
give depth~$2$ (Lie bracket). The quartic operation $m_4 = 0$
by the Jacobi identity:
the weight $2\alpha_1 + \alpha_2$ is a non-root weight of
$\mathfrak{sl}_3$ at height~$3$ (dimension count: $\dim(\fg_{2\alpha_1+\alpha_2}) = 0$),
so the iterated bracket vanishes by the same mechanism as
Computation~\ref{comp:sl3-yangian-triangle}.
The tower terminates at depth~$3$. This is class~$\mathbf{L}$.
As for the $A_1$ lattice, no Virasoro sub-sector exists on generators, so the weight-depth identity (Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)) is vacuously satisfied.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Operations: $m_2$ table.}
The nonvanishing $m_2$ operations on Chevalley generators:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\toprule
\textbf{Pair} & $m_2(a,b;\lambda)$ & \textbf{Source} \\
\midrule
$(e^{\alpha_i}, e^{-\alpha_i})$ & $\lambda + \alpha_i \cdot J$
 & double + simple pole \\
$(e^{\alpha_1}, e^{-\alpha_2})$ & $e^{\alpha_1-\alpha_2}$
 & simple pole \\
$(e^{\alpha_2}, e^{-\alpha_1})$ & $-e^{\alpha_2-\alpha_1}$
 & simple pole \\
$(J_i, J_j)$ & $(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)\,\lambda$
 & double pole \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
All $m_k = 0$ for $k \ge 4$. The ternary operation $m_3$ is
nonzero on triples involving the composite root, e.g.\
$m_3(e^{\alpha_1}, e^{-\alpha_1}, e^{\alpha_2})
= -(\alpha_1,\alpha_2)\,e^{\alpha_2} = e^{\alpha_2}$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{$R$-matrix and Koszul dual.}
The collision residue is the $\mathfrak{sl}_3$ classical
$r$-matrix:
$r(z) = k\,\Omega_{\mathfrak{sl}_3}/z$,
where $\Omega_{\mathfrak{sl}_3}$ is the quadratic Casimir
of~$\mathfrak{sl}_3$; at level~$k=1$ the collision residue is $\Omega_{\mathfrak{sl}_3}/z$. The spectral $R$-matrix is
the Yang $R$-matrix
\begin{equation}\label{eq:A2-lattice-R}
R(z) \;=\; 1 + \frac{\hbar\,\Omega_{\mathfrak{sl}_3}}{z}\,.
\end{equation}
The Koszul dual is the Yangian
$Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_3)$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Poincar\'{e} series and Euler characteristic.}
$P(t) = 1 + 8t$ (eight cogenerators in degree~$1$,
corresponding to the $\dim(\mathfrak{sl}_3) = 8$
desuspended generators). The shadow Hessian
$S_2 = 4k/(k+3)\big|_{k=1} = 1$, matching the
general affine formula
$S_2(V_k(\fg)) = c(\fg)/2 = \dim(\fg) \cdot k/(2(k+h^\vee))$
with $h^\vee = 3$. (As in the landscape table on
p.~\pageref{comp:e1-ordered-bar-landscape}, we record
$S_2 = c/2$ rather than the Volume~I modular characteristic
$\kappa = \dim(\fg)(k+h^\vee)/(2h^\vee)$, which for
$\mathfrak{sl}_3$ at $k = 1$ gives
$\kappa = 8 \cdot 4/6 = 16/3 \ne S_2$.)

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Genus-$1$.}
Since $c_0 = \Omega_{\mathfrak{sl}_3} \ne 0$ (the
Lie bracket is nonvanishing), the $A_2$ lattice VOA is
propagator-entangled at genus~$1$. The elliptic $r$-matrix is
$r^{E_\tau}(z) = \Omega_{\mathfrak{sl}_3}\cdot\zeta(z|\tau)
+ \kappa\cdot\wp(z|\tau)$,
with $B$-cycle monodromy $2\eta_\tau\cdot\Omega_{\mathfrak{sl}_3}$.
\end{computation}

\begin{computation}[$D_4$ lattice VOA: triality and ordered bar;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:lattice-voa-D4-ordered-bar}%
\index{lattice VOA!D4 root lattice@$D_4$ root lattice!bar complex}%
\index{lattice VOA!triality}%
\index{triality!lattice VOA bar complex}%
The $D_4$ root lattice $\Lambda_{D_4}$ has rank~$4$,
$|\Phi| = 24$ roots, and the lattice VOA
$V_{\Lambda_{D_4}} \cong L_1(\mathfrak{so}_8)$ is the
integrable vacuum module of $\widehat{\mathfrak{so}}_8$ at
level~$1$. This is the first lattice VOA where \emph{triality}
(the $S_3$ outer automorphism of $D_4$) is visible.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Generators.}
Four Heisenberg currents $J_1, \ldots, J_4$ spanning the Cartan,
and $24$ vertex operators $e^\alpha$ ($\alpha \in \Phi_{D_4}$) of
conformal weight~$1$, giving $\dim(\mathfrak{so}_8) = 28$ generators.
The OPE has the same structure as~\eqref{eq:A2-vertex-ope}
with the $D_4$ Killing form and structure constants.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Depth spectrum: $\{1,2\}$, class~$\mathbf{L}$, depth~$3$.}
As for all simply-laced root lattices at level~$1$, the double
poles (Killing form) give depth~$1$ and the simple poles
(Lie bracket) give depth~$2$. The quartic operation $m_4 = 0$
by the Jacobi identity. Class~$\mathbf{L}$, depth~$3$.
The weight-depth identity (Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)) is vacuously satisfied on the affine generators; the depth spectrum is controlled by the Jacobi termination mechanism.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{$R$-matrix and Koszul dual.}
The collision residue is $r(z) = k\,\Omega_{\mathfrak{so}_8}/z$.
The spectral $R$-matrix is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:D4-lattice-R}
R(z) \;=\; 1 + \frac{\hbar\,\Omega_{\mathfrak{so}_8}}{z}\,.
\end{equation}
The Koszul dual is $Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{so}_8)$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Triality.}
The outer automorphism group $\mathrm{Out}(D_4) \cong S_3$
permutes the three $8$-dimensional representations:
the vector $\mathbf{8}_v$, the spinor $\mathbf{8}_s$, and
the co-spinor $\mathbf{8}_c$. At the level of the bar complex:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item Triality permutes the vertex operators:
 $\sigma \colon e^{\alpha} \mapsto e^{\sigma(\alpha)}$
 for $\sigma \in S_3$.
\item The collision residue $r(z) = k\,\Omega/z$ is triality-invariant
 ($\Omega_{\mathfrak{so}_8}$ is the unique quadratic
 Casimir, hence $S_3$-invariant).
\item The Yangian $Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{so}_8)$ inherits triality:
 the evaluation representation $V(u)$ in the vector
 representation is isomorphic to $V_s(u)$ in the spinor
 representation and $V_c(u)$ in the co-spinor representation,
 as Yangian modules.
\end{enumerate}
Triality is a symmetry of the ordered bar complex that does
\emph{not} descend from an inner automorphism: it is the
bar-complex shadow of the exceptional Dynkin diagram symmetry.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Poincar\'{e} series.}
$P(t) = 1 + 28t$ ($\dim(\mathfrak{so}_8) = 28$ cogenerators).
Shadow Hessian
$S_2 = \dim(\fg)\cdot k/(2(k+h^\vee)) = 28/(2 \cdot 7) = 2$
(using $\dim(\mathfrak{so}_8) = 28$, $k = 1$, $h^\vee(D_4) = 6$);
equivalently $S_2 = c/2 = 4/2 = 2$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Genus-$1$.}
Propagator-entangled ($c_0 = \Omega_{\mathfrak{so}_8} \ne 0$).
The genus-$1$ partition function
$Z_1(V_{\Lambda_{D_4}}) = (\Theta_{D_4}(\tau)/\eta(\tau)^4)$,
where $\Theta_{D_4}$ is the $D_4$ theta function.
Triality permutes the three conjugacy classes of $D_4$
lattice cosets, corresponding to the three modular-invariant
partition functions (diagonal, spinor, co-spinor) of the
$\widehat{\mathfrak{so}}_8$ WZW model at level~$1$.
\end{computation}

\subsection{The $\beta\gamma$ system: class~C and statistics exchange}%
\label{subsec:betagamma-ordered-bar}%
\index{beta-gamma system@$\beta\gamma$ system!ordered bar complex|textbf}%
\index{Koszul duality!beta-gamma-bc@$\beta\gamma$--$bc$}

The $\beta\gamma$ system is the simplest chiral algebra of
class~$\mathbf{C}$: it has a non-scalar quartic contact
invariant but the tower terminates at depth~$4$ by
rank-$1$ abelian rigidity.

\begin{computation}[$\beta\gamma$ ordered bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:betagamma-ordered-bar}%
\index{beta-gamma system@$\beta\gamma$ system!R-matrix}%
\index{beta-gamma system@$\beta\gamma$ system!Koszul dual}%
\index{beta-gamma system@$\beta\gamma$ system!depth spectrum}%
The $\beta\gamma$ system has two generators:
$\beta$ of conformal weight~$\lambda$ and
$\gamma$ of conformal weight~$1-\lambda$, with OPE
\begin{equation}\label{eq:betagamma-ope}
\beta(z)\,\gamma(w)
\;\sim\;
\frac{1}{z-w}\,,
\qquad
\beta(z)\,\beta(w) \sim 0,
\qquad
\gamma(z)\,\gamma(w) \sim 0.
\end{equation}
Central charge $c(\beta\gamma) = 2(6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1)$.
At $\lambda = 1/2$: $c = -1$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Depth spectrum: $\{0\}$ on generators.}
The OPE~\eqref{eq:betagamma-ope} has a single simple pole.
the $d\log$ kernel absorbs one power: the
collision residue is $r^{\mathrm{coll}} = 1$ (a constant,
depth~$0$). On generators, all $m_k = 0$ for
$k \ge 3$: there are no iterated OPE singularities
because $\beta\beta$ and $\gamma\gamma$ are regular.
The depth spectrum on generators is $\{0\}$.

The shadow obstruction tower atlas records depth~$4$ for $\beta\gamma$
because the \emph{composite} quasi-primary
$\Lambda = {:}\beta\gamma{:}$ (the $U(1)$ ghost current)
mediates a quartic exchange at weight~$4$. On the
composite sector, the $\beta\gamma$ system behaves like
class~$\mathbf{C}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:pole-structure-dichotomy}(iii)).
On generators, $m_2(\beta,\gamma;\lambda) = 1$ is a depth-$0$ constant: the weight-depth identity (Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)) is trivially satisfied ($w = 0$, $d = 0$, consistent with degree~$2$ and the simple-pole absorption ).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{$R$-matrix: trivial.}
The collision residue is a constant ($r = 1$, depth~$0$):
the connection on $\Conf_2^{\mathrm{ord}}(\C)$ is
$\nabla = d$ (flat), and the $R$-matrix is the identity:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:betagamma-R}
R(z) \;=\; \mathrm{Id}.
\end{equation}
The $\beta\gamma$ OPE on generators has only a simple pole,
and the $d\log$ absorption reduces it to a constant:
the generator-level $R$-matrix is trivial. This is the
simple-pole sub-stratum within tier~(ii) of the three-tier
picture ($\S$\ref{subsec:ordered-three-tier}):
the algebra is $\Einf$-chiral (local, with OPE singularities),
but the simple-pole structure makes the generator-level
braiding trivial.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Koszul dual: $bc = \bigwedge^{\mathrm{ch}}(V)$.}
The chiral $\mathrm{Ext}/\mathrm{Sym}$ duality
(Remark~\ref{rem:rosetta-bc-betagamma-koszul})
exchanges statistics:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:betagamma-koszul-dual}
\beta\gamma_\lambda^!
\;=\;
bc_\lambda\,,
\qquad
bc_\lambda^!
\;=\;
\beta\gamma_\lambda\,.
\end{equation}
The $\beta\gamma$ system is the chiral symmetric algebra
$\mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V)$
on $V = \C\beta \oplus \C\gamma$ (bosonic); its
Koszul dual is the chiral exterior algebra
$\bigwedge^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$ (fermionic), which is the
$bc$ ghost system.
The Poincar\'{e} series is $P(t) = 1 + 2t$
(two cogenerators $s^{-1}\beta$ and $s^{-1}\gamma$
in degree~$1$).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Complementarity: $\kappa(\beta\gamma_\lambda) + \kappa(bc_\lambda) = 0$.}
The modular characteristics are
$\kappa(\beta\gamma_\lambda) = 6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1$ and
$\kappa(bc_\lambda) = -(6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1)$.
Their sum vanishes:
$K(\beta\gamma_\lambda) = \kappa(\beta\gamma_\lambda) + \kappa(bc_\lambda) = 0$.
This is the free-field instance of the affine-lineage
complementarity $K = 0$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:rosetta-complementarity}).
The central charges also satisfy
$c(\beta\gamma) + c(bc)
= 2(6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1) - 2(6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1) = 0$
for all~$\lambda$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Genus-$1$.}
Since the zeroth product
$\beta_{(0)}\gamma = 1 \ne 0$ (the simple-pole OPE
residue is nonvanishing), we have $c_0 \ne 0$: the
$\beta\gamma$ system is propagator-entangled at genus~$1$.
The symplectic Casimir $\Omega_{\mathrm{symp}}
= \beta \otimes \gamma - \gamma \otimes \beta$
replaces the Lie-algebra Casimir in the elliptic
$r$-matrix formula. The curvature is
$\kappa(\beta\gamma_\lambda) = 6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1$.
\end{computation}

\subsection{The free fermion $\psi$: class~G on generators, class~C full}%
\label{subsec:free-fermion-ordered-bar}%
\index{free fermion!ordered bar complex|textbf}%
\index{Koszul duality!free fermion}

The free fermion $\psi$ of conformal weight~$1/2$ is the
simplest fermionic chiral algebra. On generators it is
class~$\mathbf{G}$ (the OPE $\psi(z)\,\psi(w) \sim 1/(z-w)$
is a single simple pole, and the $d\log$ kernel absorbs it
to a constant). The full algebra, including the composite
$J = {:}\psi\psi{:}$ (a weight-$1$ boson), is class~$\mathbf{C}$
because $J$ mediates a quartic exchange.

\begin{computation}[Free fermion ordered bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:free-fermion-ordered-bar}%
\index{free fermion!R-matrix}%
\index{free fermion!Koszul dual}%
\index{free fermion!depth spectrum}%
The free fermion has a single generator $\psi$ of conformal
weight~$1/2$ (fermionic), with OPE
\begin{equation}\label{eq:free-fermion-ope}
\psi(z)\,\psi(w) \;\sim\; \frac{1}{z-w}\,.
\end{equation}
Central charge $c(\psi) = 1/2$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Operations.}
The single nonvanishing operation on generators is
$m_2(\psi,\psi;\,\lambda) = 1$
(the simple-pole residue is the identity pairing).
All $m_k = 0$ for $k \ge 3$ on generators: the OPE
$\psi(z)\,\psi(w)$ has only a simple pole, and the
iterated collision $\psi\,\psi\,\psi$ vanishes by
fermionic antisymmetry. On the composite sector
($J = {:}\psi\psi{:}$, $T = \tfrac{1}{2}{:}\partial\psi\,\psi{:}$),
the OPE $J(z)\,J(w) \sim 1/(z-w)^2$ introduces a
Heisenberg-type double pole, and $T(z)\,T(w)$ has the
Virasoro quartic pole at $c = 1/2$. The full algebra is
class~$\mathbf{C}$ with depth~$4$ on composites.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Depth spectrum: $\{0\}$ on generators.}
The $d\log$ kernel absorbs the simple pole:
$r^{\mathrm{coll}} = 1$ (constant, depth~$0$).
On generators the depth spectrum is $\{0\}$, matching
$\beta\gamma$ (Computation~\ref{comp:betagamma-ordered-bar}).
The full depth spectrum including composites is $\{0,1,4\}$.
On the composite Virasoro sector ($T = \tfrac{1}{2}{:}\partial\psi\,\psi{:}$, $c = 1/2$), the weight-depth identity $w + d = n - 1$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)) applies to the induced $\Ainf$ operations.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{$R$-matrix: trivial on generators.}
Since $r^{\mathrm{coll}} = 1$ (a scalar constant), the connection
on $\Conf_2^{\mathrm{ord}}(\C)$ is flat: $\nabla = d$.
The $R$-matrix on generators is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:free-fermion-R}
R(z) \;=\; \tau \qquad\text{(Koszul-signed flip)},
\end{equation}
where $\tau(a \otimes b) = (-1)^{|a||b|}\,b \otimes a$ is the
graded transposition. The minus sign in
$\psi \otimes \psi \mapsto -\psi \otimes \psi$
encodes the fermionic statistics. This is the simple-pole
sub-stratum within tier~(ii): the OPE has a singularity,
but $d\log$ absorption makes the generator-level
$R$-matrix the Koszul-signed flip.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Koszul dual: $\beta\gamma_{1/2}$.}
The free fermion is the chiral exterior algebra
$\bigwedge^{\mathrm{ch}}(\C\psi)$ (a single fermionic
generator). Its Koszul dual is the chiral symmetric
algebra on the dual:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:free-fermion-koszul}
\psi^! \;=\; \beta\gamma_{1/2}\,.
\end{equation}
The Koszul dual exchanges statistics
(fermionic~$\to$~bosonic) and preserves the
conformal weight~$1/2$. This is the single-generator
case of the $bc$--$\beta\gamma$ duality
(Remark~\ref{rem:rosetta-bc-betagamma-koszul}).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Bar cohomology.}
The bar complex $\barBch(\psi)$ on generators is the
cofree coalgebra on a single fermionic desuspended generator
$s^{-1}\psi$. Since $m_2(\psi,\psi) = 1$ is a nondegenerate
pairing, $H_1(\barBch) = 0$: the single generator is
exact. The bar cohomology in higher degrees is
$H_n(\barBch) \cong \C$ for $n = 0$ and
$H_n(\barBch) = 0$ for $n \ge 1$ on generators
(the pairing is perfect). Including composites, the
bar cohomology is large: $H_n \ne 0$ for $n \ge 3$
(the quartic exchanges on composites generate
nontrivial cohomology classes).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Poincar\'{e} series and Euler characteristic.}
$P(t) = 1 + t$ (single cogenerator in degree~$1$).
Modular characteristic $\kappa(\psi) = 1/4$
(from $c = 1/2$ and the free-fermion curvature formula).
Complementarity: $\kappa(\psi) + \kappa(\beta\gamma_{1/2})
= 1/4 + (-1/4) = 0$, matching the free-field pattern.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Genus-$1$.}
The zeroth product $\psi_{(0)}\psi = 1 \ne 0$
(the simple-pole residue), so $c_0 \ne 0$: the free fermion is
propagator-entangled at genus~$1$. The genus-$1$ partition function
$Z_1(\psi) = \sqrt{\theta_3(\tau)/\eta(\tau)}$
(the NS-sector character), encoding the
theta-function/eta-function ratio characteristic of
free fermions.
\end{computation}

\subsection{The $bc$ ghost system: class~G on generators, weight-$\lambda$ landscape}%
\label{subsec:bc-ordered-bar}%
\index{bc ghost system!ordered bar complex|textbf}%
\index{Koszul duality!bc ghost}

The $bc$ ghost system at general conformal weight~$\lambda$
is the fermionic partner of $\beta\gamma_\lambda$
(Remark~\ref{rem:rosetta-bc-betagamma-koszul}). The OPE
is the same for all~$\lambda$; the conformal weight affects
only the stress tensor.

\begin{computation}[$bc$ ghost system ordered bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:bc-ordered-bar}%
\index{bc ghost system!R-matrix}%
\index{bc ghost system!Koszul dual}%
\index{bc ghost system!depth spectrum}%
The $bc$ system has two generators: $b$ of conformal
weight~$\lambda$ and $c$ of conformal weight~$1-\lambda$
(both fermionic), with OPE
\begin{equation}\label{eq:bc-ope}
b(z)\,c(w)
\;\sim\;
\frac{1}{z-w}\,,
\qquad
b(z)\,b(w) \sim 0,
\qquad
c(z)\,c(w) \sim 0.
\end{equation}
Central charge $c(bc) = -2(6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1)$.
At $\lambda = 2$: $c = -26$ (reparametrisation ghosts).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Operations.}
The nonvanishing operation is
$m_2(b,c;\,\lambda) = 1$ (simple-pole residue).
All $m_k = 0$ for $k \ge 3$ on generators: the OPE has
only a simple pole, and $bb$, $cc$ are regular (vanish by
fermionic antisymmetry). On composites
($J_{bc} = {:}bc{:}$, $T = \lambda\,{:}\partial b\,c{:}
+ (1-\lambda)\,{:}b\,\partial c{:}$), the full algebra
is class~$\mathbf{C}$ with depth~$4$ (the ghost current
$J_{bc}$ mediates a quartic exchange).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Depth spectrum: $\{0\}$ on generators.}
The $d\log$ kernel absorbs the simple pole:
$r^{\mathrm{coll}} = 1$ (constant, depth~$0$).
On generators the depth spectrum is $\{0\}$; on the composite Virasoro sector, the weight-depth identity $w + d = n - 1$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)) applies.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{$R$-matrix: trivial on generators.}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:bc-R}
R(z) \;=\; \mathrm{Id}\,.
\end{equation}
As for $\beta\gamma$, the generators see only a simple pole
whose $d\log$ absorption gives a constant. On the composite
sector the $R$-matrix acquires nontrivial spectral
dependence.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Koszul dual: $\beta\gamma_\lambda$.}
The $bc$ system is the chiral exterior algebra
$\bigwedge^{\mathrm{ch}}(V)$ on
$V = \C b \oplus \C c$ (fermionic); its Koszul dual is
the chiral symmetric algebra
$\mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$ (bosonic):
\begin{equation}\label{eq:bc-koszul-dual}
bc_\lambda^! \;=\; \beta\gamma_\lambda\,,
\qquad
\beta\gamma_\lambda^! \;=\; bc_\lambda\,.
\end{equation}
This is independent of~$\lambda$: the Koszul duality
exchanges statistics, not conformal weights.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Weight-$\lambda$ landscape.}
The central charge
$c(\lambda) = -2(6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1)$ is a quadratic
in~$\lambda$ with roots at $\lambda = (3 \pm \sqrt{3})/6$.
Key specialisations:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{ccll}
\toprule
$\lambda$ & $c(bc)$ & \textbf{Physics} & \textbf{Koszul dual} \\
\midrule
$1/2$ & $1$ & Ising fermion ghost & $\beta\gamma_{1/2}$ \\
$1$ & $-2$ & scalar ghost & $\beta\gamma_1$ \\
$3/2$ & $-11$ & spin-$3/2$ ghost & $\beta\gamma_{3/2}$ \\
$2$ & $-26$ & reparametrisation ghost & $\beta\gamma_2$ (graviton) \\
$5/2$ & $-47$ & spin-$5/2$ ghost & $\beta\gamma_{5/2}$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
At $\lambda = 2$: the Koszul dual of the reparametrisation
ghost $bc_2$ ($c = -26$) is the bosonic spin-$2$ system
$\beta\gamma_2$ ($c = +26$). A spin-$2$ boson is a
symmetric tensor field, a graviton.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Complementarity.}
$\kappa(bc_\lambda) = -(6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1)$ and
$\kappa(\beta\gamma_\lambda) = 6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1$.
The complementarity sum
$K(bc_\lambda) = \kappa(bc_\lambda) + \kappa(\beta\gamma_\lambda) = 0$
vanishes universally. The central charges satisfy
$c(bc_\lambda) + c(\beta\gamma_\lambda) = 0$ for all~$\lambda$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Poincar\'{e} series.}
$P(t) = 1 + 2t$ (two cogenerators $s^{-1}b, s^{-1}c$).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Genus-$1$.}
$b_{(0)}c = 1 \ne 0$, so $c_0 \ne 0$: the $bc$ system is
propagator-entangled at genus~$1$. The curvature is
$\kappa(bc_\lambda) = -(6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1)$. The genus-$1$ partition function
$Z_1(bc_\lambda) = \eta(\tau)^{2(6\lambda^2-6\lambda+1)}$
(the eta function raised to the power $-c$).
\end{computation}

\subsection{Symplectic bosons: class~C and depth~$4$}%
\label{subsec:symplectic-boson-ordered-bar}%
\index{symplectic bosons!ordered bar complex|textbf}%
\index{Koszul duality!symplectic bosons}

The symplectic boson system (also called the $\beta\gamma$
system at half-integer weight in the physics literature,
or the bosonic ghost system) at weight~$1/2$ is
class~$\mathbf{C}$ with depth~$4$. It provides the
bosonic analogue of the free fermion
(Computation~\ref{comp:free-fermion-ordered-bar}).

\begin{computation}[Symplectic boson ordered bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:symplectic-boson-ordered-bar}%
\index{symplectic bosons!R-matrix}%
\index{symplectic bosons!Koszul dual}%
\index{symplectic bosons!depth spectrum}%
The symplectic boson system has two generators
$\chi^+, \chi^-$ of conformal weight~$1/2$ (bosonic),
with OPE
\begin{equation}\label{eq:symplectic-boson-ope}
\chi^+(z)\,\chi^-(w) \;\sim\; \frac{1}{z-w}\,,
\qquad
\chi^+(z)\,\chi^+(w) \sim 0,
\qquad
\chi^-(z)\,\chi^-(w) \sim 0.
\end{equation}
Central charge $c(\chi) = -1$:
$c = 2(6 \cdot (1/2)^2 - 6 \cdot (1/2) + 1) = 2(-1/2) = -1$,
the same as $\beta\gamma$ at $\lambda = 1/2$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Operations.}
$m_2(\chi^+, \chi^-;\,\lambda) = 1$ (simple-pole residue).
All $m_k = 0$ for $k \ge 3$ on generators. The OPE on
generators has only a simple pole, and $\chi^+\chi^+$,
$\chi^-\chi^-$ are regular. On composites
($J = {:}\chi^+\chi^-{:}$), the ghost current $J$ mediates
a quartic exchange at depth~$4$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Depth spectrum: $\{0\}$ on generators; depth~$4$ full.}
The collision residue is $r^{\mathrm{coll}} = 1$ (constant).
On generators, depth~$\{0\}$; the weight-depth identity (Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)) is trivially satisfied at degree~$2$. The composite sector has
depth~$4$ (class~$\mathbf{C}$), the same as
$\beta\gamma$, confirming that depth is controlled by
OPE structure, not statistics.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{$R$-matrix.}
On generators, the collision residue is constant
($r^{\mathrm{coll}} = 1$, depth~$0$), so the $R$-matrix is
the identity:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:symplectic-boson-R}
R(z) \;=\; \mathrm{Id}\,,
\end{equation}
the same as $\beta\gamma$ at $\lambda = 1/2$
(equation~\eqref{eq:betagamma-R}). The DK-0 Laplace
kernel $r(z) = 1/z$ (from the simple-pole OPE) is a
different object from the collision residue: the $d\log$
bar kernel absorbs the pole, reducing the generator-level
braiding to trivial.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Koszul dual.}
The symplectic bosons are the chiral symmetric algebra on a
symplectic vector space. The Koszul dual is the chiral
exterior algebra on the dual:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:symplectic-boson-koszul}
(\chi^+\chi^-)^! \;=\; \text{fermionic symplectic system}\,.
\end{equation}
The statistics exchange (bosonic $\leftrightarrow$ fermionic)
preserves the symplectic structure.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Complementarity.}
$\kappa(\chi) = -1/4$ (from the weight-$1/2$ curvature formula).
The complementarity sum with the dual vanishes:
$K = \kappa(\chi) + \kappa(\chi^!) = 0$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Poincar\'{e} series.}
$P(t) = 1 + 2t$ (two cogenerators $s^{-1}\chi^+, s^{-1}\chi^-$).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Genus-$1$.}
$\chi^+_{(0)}\chi^- = 1 \ne 0$, so $c_0 \ne 0$: symplectic bosons
are propagator-entangled at genus~$1$. The symplectic Casimir
$\Omega_{\mathrm{symp}} = \chi^+ \otimes \chi^- - \chi^- \otimes \chi^+$
enters the elliptic $r$-matrix. Curvature $\kappa = -1/4$.
\end{computation}

% ================================================================
\section{The shadow obstruction tower atlas}%
\label{sec:shadow-tower-atlas}%
\index{shadow tower!atlas|textbf}%
\index{Lagrangian self-intersection!atlas}

The Heisenberg Rosetta Stone establishes the principle:
the bar complex of a chiral algebra is the formal bar/Koszul model of
a Lagrangian self-intersection, and the shadow obstruction tower
$\{\operatorname{Sh}_r\}_{r\ge 2}$ measures the excess
intersection multiplicity at each codimension. For
$\cH_k$, the intersection is clean ($m_{k\ge 3}=0$) and the
tower terminates at degree~$2$: the single scalar~$k$ is the
only datum. What happens for algebras with singular
self-intersections?

This section answers by explicit computation for all
standard families. The results are summarised in the
\emph{shadow obstruction tower atlas}: a complete table of shadow
coefficients, depths, and termination degrees for seven
families covering all four depth classes.

\subsection{Excess intersection depth}%
\label{subsec:excess-intersection-depth}%
\index{shadow depth!excess intersection}

\begin{definition}[Shadow depth as excess intersection
codimension]%
\label{def:shadow-depth-intersection}%
\index{shadow depth!definition}%
The \emph{shadow depth} of a chiral algebra~$\cA$
is
\[
 d(\cA)
 \;:=\;
 \max\{r \ge 2 : \operatorname{Sh}_r(\cA) \ne 0\}
 \;\in\;
 \{2, 3, 4, \ldots\} \cup \{\infty\}\,.
\]
In the Chriss--Ginzburg picture, $d(\cA)$ is the codimension
of the \emph{excess intersection locus}: the deepest stratum
of the Lagrangian self-intersection
$\mathfrak{S}_b = L\times_X L$ at which the Borel--Moore
fundamental class carries nontrivial convolution data.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Four classes.}
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{cllll}
\toprule
\textbf{Class} & \textbf{Depth} & \textbf{Intersection} &
\textbf{Mechanism} & \textbf{Archetype} \\
\midrule
$\mathbf{G}$ & $2$ & Clean &
 Abelian OPE & Heisenberg \\
$\mathbf{L}$ & $3$ & Lie-transverse &
 Jacobi kills quartic & Affine $V_k(\fg)$ \\
$\mathbf{C}$ & $4$ & Contact &
 Rank-$1$ abelian rigidity & $\beta\gamma$ \\
$\mathbf{M}$ & $\infty$ & Excess tower &
 Composite-field exchange & Virasoro \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{definition}

\subsection{The atlas}%
\label{subsec:atlas}%
\index{shadow tower!atlas!master table}

\begin{computation}[Shadow obstruction tower atlas;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:shadow-tower-atlas}%
\index{shadow tower!atlas!computation}%
The shadow obstruction tower coefficients $S_r = \operatorname{Sh}_r / x^r$
for all standard families, with $P = H^{-1}$ the propagator
\textup{(}inverse Hessian\textup{)}:

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabular}{llccccl}
\toprule
\textbf{Family} & \textbf{Class}
& $S_2$ & $S_3$ & $S_4$
& \textbf{Depth} & \textbf{Terminates} \\
\midrule
$\cH_k$
 & $\mathbf{G}$
 & $k$
 & $0$
 & $0$
 & $2$
 & $\checkmark$ \\[2pt]
$V_\Lambda$ (mom.)
 & $\mathbf{G}$
 & $\operatorname{rk}(\Lambda)$
 & $0$
 & $0$
 & $2$
 & $\checkmark$ \\[2pt]
$V_\Lambda$ (v.o.)
 & $\mathbf{L}$
 & (see~\ref{comp:lattice-voa-ordered-bar})
 & $C_\Lambda \ne 0$
 & $0$
 & $3$
 & $\checkmark$ \\[2pt]
$V_k(\fg)$
 & $\mathbf{L}$
 & $\dfrac{dk}{2(k+h^\vee)}$
 & $C_{\fg}\ne 0$
 & $0$
 & $3$
 & $\checkmark$ \\[4pt]
$\beta\gamma$
 & $\mathbf{C}$
 & $-1$
 & $0$
 & $-\dfrac{5}{12}$
 & $4$
 & $\checkmark$ \\[4pt]
Virasoro
 & $\mathbf{M}$
 & $\dfrac{c}{2}$
 & $2$
 & $\dfrac{10}{c(5c{+}22)}$
 & $\infty$
 & \\[4pt]
$\cW_3$
 & $\mathbf{M}$
 & $\dfrac{5c}{6}$
 & $2$
 & $\dfrac{10}{c(5c{+}22)}$
 & $\infty$
 & \\[4pt]
$\cW_N$
 & $\mathbf{M}$
 & $c(H_N{-}1)$
 & $2$
 & $\dfrac{10}{c(5c{+}22)}$
 & $\infty$
 & \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Here $d = \dim\fg$, $h^\vee$ is the dual Coxeter number,
$H_N = \sum_{j=1}^N 1/j$ is the harmonic number,
$C_\fg$ is the Lie cubic shadow, and the $\cW_N$ entries
for $S_3$, $S_4$ restrict to the $T$-line. The
$\cW_3$ Hessian $\kappa = 5c/6$ is the composite
$\kappa_T + \kappa_W = c/2 + c/3$.
\end{computation}

\subsection{Virasoro: the infinite tower}%
\label{subsec:virasoro-shadow-tower}%
\index{shadow tower!Virasoro}

\begin{computation}[Virasoro shadow obstruction tower;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:virasoro-shadow-tower}%
\index{shadow tower!Virasoro!explicit}%
The Virasoro algebra has a single strong generator~$T$ of
weight~$2$, with curvature $\kappa = c/2$ and
propagator $P = 2/c$. The shadow obstruction tower is computed by
the obstruction recursion: $\operatorname{Sh}_r =
-o^{(r)}/(2r)$ where $o^{(r)} = \sum_{j+k=r+2}
\{\operatorname{Sh}_j, \operatorname{Sh}_k\}_H$ is the
Poisson bracket of lower shadows.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Explicit coefficients.}
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{clc}
\toprule
$r$ & $S_r$ & Sign \\
\midrule
$2$ & $c/2$ & $+$ \\
$3$ & $2$ & $+$ \\
$4$ & $10/\bigl[c(5c{+}22)\bigr]$ & $+$ \\
$5$ & $-48/\bigl[c^2(5c{+}22)\bigr]$ & $-$ \\
$6$ & $80(45c{+}193)/\bigl[3\,c^3(5c{+}22)^2\bigr]$ & $+$ \\
$7$ & $-2880(15c{+}61)/\bigl[7\,c^4(5c{+}22)^2\bigr]$ & $-$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\emph{Denominator structure} \textup{(}verified through
$r = 7$\textup{)}\emph{.}
$S_r$ has denominator $c^{r-2}(5c{+}22)^{\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor}$.
The factor $(5c{+}22)$ is the Kac determinant at level~$4$:
$\det M_4 \sim c^2(2c{-}1)(5c{+}22)(7c{+}68)$. The shadow obstruction tower
knows the Kac determinant.
Each entry verifies the weight-depth identity $w + d = n - 1$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)): the shadow $S_r$ at degree~$r$ has spectral degree $r - 1$ for the $T$-dependent sector and degree $r + 1$ for the scalar contact term.
\end{computation}

\begin{remark}[Kac--shadow singularity principle]%
\label{rem:kac-shadow-singularity}%
\index{Kac determinant!shadow tower}%
\index{shadow tower!Kac determinant}%
The denominator of~$S_r$ divides the product of Kac
determinants up to level~$r$. Concretely:
$(5c+22)$ appears in $S_4$ and in $\det M_4$;
$(c+24)$ from $\det M_6$ appears in the $\cW_3$ cubic
coupling $C_{333}^2 = 64(7c+68)(2c-1)/[5c(c+24)(5c+22)]$.
The shadow pole locus $\{S_r = \infty\}$ is contained in the
Kac degeneration locus $\{\det M_r = 0\}$: shadows diverge
where the chiral algebra degenerates.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Affine Kac--Moody: Jacobi termination}%
\label{subsec:affine-shadow}%
\index{shadow tower!affine}

\begin{computation}[Affine $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$:
depth~$3$ by Jacobi; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:affine-shadow-tower}%
\index{shadow tower!affine!termination}%
The affine algebra $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ has
$\dim\fg = 3$, $h^\vee = 2$,
$c = 3k/(k+2)$, and $\kappa = 3(k+2)/4$. On the Cartan
line $(\bC\cdot h)$:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{ccc}
\toprule
$r$ & Affine $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ & Virasoro \\
\midrule
$S_2$ & $k$ & $c/2$ \\
$S_3$ & $0$ (Cartan abelian) & $2$ \\
$S_4$ & $0$ (Jacobi) & $10/[c(5c{+}22)]$ \\
$\delta H^{(1)}$ & $0$ & $120/[c^2(5c{+}22)]$ \\
$\rho^{(1)}$ & $0$ & $240/[c^3(5c{+}22)]$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\emph{Termination mechanism.}
The Cartan subalgebra is abelian ($[h,h]=0$), so
$S_3|_{\mathrm{Cartan}} = 0$. The quartic
$Q^{\mathrm{contact}} = \{S_3, S_3\}_H/(8) = 0$
vanishes on the Cartan line because $S_3 = 0$ there.
On the full $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ basis $\{h,e,f\}$,
the cubic $C(h,e,f) = \kappa(h,[e,f]) = 2k$ is nonzero,
but the quartic contact term vanishes by the Jacobi
identity: $\{C, C\}_H = 0$. The genus-$1$ Hessian
correction $\delta H^{(1)}$ vanishes on the Cartan line by
sign cancellation between $e$- and $f$-loops.
The tower terminates at degree~$3$. The Virasoro column provides a reference for the weight-depth identity $w + d = n - 1$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)); the affine column terminates before the identity produces a nontrivial structural gap.
\end{computation}

\subsection{$\cW_3$: the first multivariable shadow}%
\label{subsec:w3-shadow}%
\index{shadow tower!$\cW_3$}

\begin{computation}[$\cW_3$ multivariable shadow;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:w3-shadow-tower}%
\index{shadow tower!$\cW_3$!quartic}%
The $\cW_3$ algebra has generators $T$ (weight~$2$)
and $W$ (weight~$3$), with Hessian
$\kappa = \operatorname{diag}(c/2,\, c/3)$. The
deformation space is two-dimensional: $(x_T, x_W)$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Weight-$4$ quasi-primary.} The unique quasi-primary
at weight~$4$ is
$\Lambda = {:}TT{:} - \tfrac{3}{10}\partial^2 T$,
with norm $N_\Lambda = c(5c{+}22)/10$. Its couplings:
$C_{TT,\Lambda} = 1$,
$C_{WW,\Lambda} = \alpha(c) := 32/(5c{+}22)$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Quartic shadow.}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-quartic}
 \operatorname{Sh}_4(x_T, x_W)
 \;=\;
 \frac{10}{c(5c{+}22)}\,x_T^4
 \;+\;
 \frac{6\cdot 320}{c(5c{+}22)^2}\,x_T^2 x_W^2
 \;+\;
 \frac{10240}{c(5c{+}22)^3}\,x_W^4\,.
\end{equation}
The $(5c{+}22)$ multiplicity increases with the number of
$W$-legs: $Q_{T^4}$ has $(5c{+}22)^1$,
$Q_{T^2W^2}$ has $(5c{+}22)^2$,
$Q_{W^4}$ has $(5c{+}22)^3$. Each pair of $W$-legs
contributes one factor of
$\alpha = C_{WW,\Lambda} = 32/(5c{+}22)$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{$W$-line parity.}
On the $W$-line ($x_T = 0$), the $\mathbb{Z}_2$ symmetry
$W\mapsto -W$ forces all odd-degree shadows to vanish:
$S_{2m+1}|_{x_T=0} = 0$ for all $m$. The even-degree
recursion gives integer normalised coefficients through
degree~$32$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{DS depth jump.}
The Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction
$V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_3) \to \cW_3$ sends a class~$\mathbf{L}$
algebra (depth~$3$) to a class~$\mathbf{M}$ algebra
(depth~$\infty$). The depth increase is caused by the
composite field $\Lambda = {:}TT{:} - \tfrac{3}{10}
\partial^2 T$, which does not exist in the affine algebra
but is generated by the reduction. DS reduction introduces
new self-intersection strata.
On the $T$-line ($x_W = 0$), each shadow $\operatorname{Sh}_r$ verifies the weight-depth identity $w + d = n - 1$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)); the gap migration formula $d_{\mathrm{gap}} = 2N + n - 4$ (part~(iv)) is verified in Computation~\ref{comp:w3-gap-migration-verification}.
\end{computation}

\subsection{$\cW_4$: two exchange channels}%
\label{subsec:w4-shadow}%
\index{shadow tower!$\cW_4$}

\begin{computation}[$\cW_4$ two-channel shadow;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:w4-shadow-tower}%
\index{shadow tower!$\cW_4$!two channels}%
The $\cW_4$ algebra has generators $T$ (weight~$2$),
$W_3$ (weight~$3$), $W_4$ (weight~$4$), with
$\kappa = \operatorname{diag}(c/2,\, c/3,\, c/4)$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Two quasi-primary exchange channels at weight~$4$.}
Unlike~$\cW_3$, the $\cW_4$ algebra has \emph{two}
independent quasi-primaries at weight~$4$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item The composite $\Lambda = {:}TT{:}
 - \tfrac{3}{10}\partial^2 T$, with
 $N_\Lambda = c(5c{+}22)/10$\textup{;}
\item The primary $W_4$ itself, with $N_{W_4} = c/4$.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
\emph{Critical coefficient.}
The $T$--$W_4$ exchange through the $W_4$~channel gives
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w4-critical}
 Q_{TW_4 TW_4}
 \;=\;
 \frac{C_{TW_4,W_4}^2}{N_{W_4}}
 \;=\;
 \frac{64}{c}\,,
\end{equation}
with \emph{no factor of $(5c{+}22)$}. This is the first
quartic coefficient in the atlas that does not carry the
Kac level-$4$ factor.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Lee--Yang decoupling.}
At the Lee--Yang critical point $c = -22/5$, the composite
$\Lambda$ decouples ($N_\Lambda = 0$), and all
$\Lambda$-mediated channels diverge. But
$Q_{TW_4 TW_4} = 64/c$ remains regular: the
$W_4$~exchange is insensitive to the Lee--Yang critical
point. The Kac degeneration locus $\{5c+22=0\}$ is visible
to the $\Lambda$~channel but invisible to the $W_4$~channel.
\end{computation}

\begin{remark}[Chriss--Ginzburg reading of the atlas]%
\label{rem:cg-atlas}%
\index{Chriss--Ginzburg!shadow tower atlas}%
\index{Lagrangian self-intersection!depth classification}%
The depth classification
(Definition~\ref{def:shadow-depth-intersection}) has a
Chriss--Ginzburg interpretation: the shadow depth measures
the complexity of the Lagrangian self-intersection
$\mathfrak{S}_b = L\times_X L$.
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item \emph{Class~$\mathbf{G}$} ($d=2$): $\mathfrak{S}_b$ is
 a clean correspondence (smooth intersection, no excess).
 The Borel--Moore fundamental class is concentrated in the
 top stratum. Archetype: $\cH_k$.
\item \emph{Class~$\mathbf{L}$} ($d=3$): the Lie bracket
 creates a transverse intersection defect at codimension~$1$,
 but the Jacobi identity kills all higher defects. The
 excess locus has dimension~$1$. Archetype: $V_k(\fg)$.
\item \emph{Class~$\mathbf{C}$} ($d=4$): a contact term
 from composite-field exchange creates an isolated
 codimension-$2$ defect; rank-$1$ abelian rigidity
 prevents further growth. Archetype: $\beta\gamma$.
\item \emph{Class~$\mathbf{M}$} ($d=\infty$): composite
 fields generate an infinite tower of excess intersection
 strata. The shadow obstruction tower does not terminate. The Kac
 determinant factors accumulate in the denominators:
 $(5c+22)^{\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor}$ grows without bound.
 Archetype: Virasoro.
\end{itemize}
The $\cW_4$ two-channel phenomenon
(Computation~\ref{comp:w4-shadow-tower}) shows that the
class~$\mathbf{M}$ tower can have \emph{multiple independent
excess-intersection directions}: the $\Lambda$~channel and the
$W_4$~channel probe different strata of~$\mathfrak{S}_b$, with
different pole loci. The Lee--Yang decoupling
($5c+22 = 0$ affects $\Lambda$ but not $W_4$) means the
self-intersection has at least two irreducible components
at codimension~$2$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Koszul conductor and Kac--shadow duality]%
\label{rem:koszul-conductor}%
\index{Koszul conductor}%
\index{Kac--shadow duality}%
The \emph{Koszul conductor}
$K_N := 2(N{-}1)(2N^2+2N+1)$ (with $K_2 = 26$ (Virasoro),
$K_3 = 100$ ($\cW_3$), $K_4 = 246$, $K_5 = 488$,
$K_6 = 850$) governs the Kac--shadow duality: the
$\sigma$-invariant
$\Delta^{(r)} := S_r(c) + S_r(K_N - c)$
is the shadow obstruction tower's image under the Koszul involution
$c \leftrightarrow K_N - c$.
For the Virasoro algebra ($K_2 = 26$),
$\Delta^{(r)} = S_r(c) + S_r(26 - c)$ recovers the
self-dual locus at $c = 13$
(by the depth decomposition theorem of Volume~I).
\end{remark}

% ================================================================
\section{The genus-1 endomorphism atlas}%
\label{sec:genus1-endomorphism-atlas}%
\index{endomorphism algebra!genus 1|textbf}%
\index{Lagrangian self-intersection!genus 1}%
\index{genus 1!endomorphism atlas}
% ================================================================

\providecommand{\Mvac}{\cM_{\mathrm{vac}}}
\providecommand{\Mbar}{\overline{\mathcal{M}}}
\providecommand{\HH}{\operatorname{HH}}
\providecommand{\End}{\operatorname{End}}

The shadow obstruction tower atlas
(Computation~\ref{comp:shadow-tower-atlas}) classifies the
standard families by the excess intersection codimension of
the genus-$0$ Lagrangian self-intersection
$\mathfrak{S}_b = L \times_X L$: clean for class~$\mathbf{G}$,
transverse for class~$\mathbf{L}$, contact for
class~$\mathbf{C}$, infinite excess for class~$\mathbf{M}$.
All of this is genus-$0$ data, visible already on~$\C$.

At genus~$1$, the Lagrangian deforms
(Theorem~\ref{thm:curved-swiss-cheese}), the $r$-matrix
becomes elliptic
(Theorem~\ref{thm:elliptic-spectral-dichotomy}), and the
five theorems of Volume~I acquire curvature. Two
independent invariants control the deformation: the modular
characteristic $\kappa(\cA)$ (the scalar curvature, from the
highest-pole OPE coefficient) and the Coisson bracket
$c_0 = \{a \,{}_0\, b\}$ (the Lie-bracket residue, from the
simple-pole coefficient). The characteristic controls the
closed colour; the Coisson bracket controls the spectral
braiding. The \emph{curvature-braiding dichotomy}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:elliptic-spectral-dichotomy}) partitions
genus-$1$ deformations: $c_0 = 0$ (Heisenberg, lattice VOAs)
gives decoupled curvature and braiding; $c_0 \ne 0$ (affine KM,
Virasoro, $\cW_N$) gives entangled curvature and braiding.
This dichotomy cuts \emph{orthogonally} to the pole-order
classification $\mathbf{G}/\mathbf{L}/\mathbf{C}/\mathbf{M}$:
Heisenberg and affine KM are both class~$\mathbf{L}$ but have
opposite genus-$1$ behaviour. This section computes the genus-$1$
endomorphism algebra for every atlas family.

\begin{theorem}[Pole-structure dichotomy; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:pole-structure-dichotomy}
\index{pole-structure dichotomy|textbf}
\index{shadow depth!pole-structure classification|textbf}
Let\/ $\cA$ be a chirally Koszul logarithmic
$\SCchtop$-algebra whose OPE has maximal pole order\/~$d$.
The pole structure determines the Swiss-cheese formality
class:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item If\/ $d = 2$ and the OPE residues are scalar
 \textup{(}class~$\mathbf{G}$\textup{)}: the bar complex is
 cogenerated in degree~$2$, all $\Ainf$ operations vanish
 for $k \ge 3$, shadow depth\/~$r_{\max} = 2$, and the
 genus-$1$ self-intersection is clean
 \textup{(}Heisenberg, lattice VOAs\textup{)}.
\item If\/ $d = 2$ and the OPE residues are non-scalar
 \textup{(}class~$\mathbf{L}$\textup{)}: the bar complex
 has an degree-$3$ obstruction from Lie-bracket terms,
 $m_3 \ne 0$ on generators but $m_k = 0$ for $k \ge 4$
 on cohomology, shadow depth\/~$r_{\max} = 3$
 \textup{(}affine Kac--Moody\textup{)}.
\item If\/ $d = 3$ \textup{(}class~$\mathbf{C}$\textup{)}:
 the third-order pole produces a quartic contact invariant,
 $m_4 \ne 0$ but terminates at
 shadow depth\/~$r_{\max} = 4$ by rank-one rigidity
 \textup{(}$\beta\gamma$ system\textup{)}.
\item If\/ $d \ge 4$ \textup{(}class~$\mathbf{M}$\textup{)}:
 the bar complex has non-vanishing $m_k$ for all $k \ge 3$,
 shadow depth is infinite, and the Swiss-cheese structure is
 non-formal. The fourth-order pole manufactures a
 propagating obstruction that prevents the tower from
 terminating
 \textup{(}Virasoro, $\cW_N$\textup{)}.
\item All four Koszul classes are chirally Koszul \textup{(}bar
 cohomology concentrated\textup{)}. Shadow depth classifies
 complexity \emph{within} the Koszul world. A fifth
 class~$\mathbf{W}$ \textup{(}wild: Kronecker $K_m$, $m \geq 3$\textup{)}
 lies outside the Koszul locus, where the bar spectral
 sequence does not collapse and the shadow depth is undefined
 \textup{(}Volume~I, Remark~\textup{\ref*{V1-rem:wild-quiver-boundary}}\textup{)}.
\item \label{item:bar-channel} Classes~$\mathbf{G}$, $\mathbf{L}$, $\mathbf{C}$ have
 formal Swiss-cheese structure at genus~$0$; class~$\mathbf{M}$
 has non-formal Swiss-cheese structure. At genus~$g \ge 1$, the
 curvature $\kappa \cdot \omega_g$ entangles the propagator
 channel for classes with $c_0 \ne 0$, while the bar-complex
 channel contributes additional genus corrections for
 class~$\mathbf{M}$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The pole order $d$ determines the maximal degree at which new
bar cogenerators appear. For $d = 2$ with scalar residues,
the bar differential is quadratic and the Koszul complex is
exact: no higher cogenerators arise, giving
$r_{\max} = 2$. For $d = 2$ with non-scalar (Lie-bracket)
residues, the bracket $[a, b]$ produces an degree-$3$ term
$m_3$, but the Jacobi identity closes the obstruction at
degree~$4$, giving $r_{\max} = 3$.
For $d = 3$, the third-order pole creates a quartic contact
invariant $\mu = \langle\eta, m_3(\eta, \eta, \eta)\rangle$
in the cyclic deformation complex; rank-one rigidity
(Volume~I, Corollary~\ref*{V1-cor:nms-betagamma-mu-vanishing})
forces the quintic obstruction to vanish on $\beta\gamma$,
giving $r_{\max} = 4$. For $d \ge 4$, the Sugawara pole
manufactures a genuine quartic propagating obstruction
(the single-line dichotomy of Volume~I,
Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:single-line-dichotomy}), forcing the tower
to be infinite. Part~(v) follows from PBW universality
(Volume~I).
\end{proof}

\subsection{The genus-1 atlas theorem}%
\label{subsec:genus1-atlas-theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Genus-$1$ endomorphism atlas;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{thm:genus1-endomorphism-atlas}%
\index{genus-1 endomorphism atlas|textbf}%
Let\/ $\cA$ be a chiral algebra from the shadow obstruction tower atlas
\textup{(}Computation~\textup{\ref{comp:shadow-tower-atlas}}\textup{)}
that is a logarithmic\/ $\SCchtop$-algebra.
The curved bar complex~$\barB^{(1)}(\cA)$
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:curved-swiss-cheese}}\textup{)}
is determined by three genus-$1$ invariants.
In the Lagrangian picture
\textup{(}the genus-$1$ deformation picture encoded by the curved bar
equation\textup{)},
$\barB^{(1)}(\cA)$ is the genus-$1$ formal endomorphism model
attached to the derived tensor product of
$\cL_\cA^{(1)} \times_{\Mvac}
\cL_\cA^{(1)}$:
the genus-$1$ bar/Koszul model of the Lagrangian
self-intersection. The three invariants are:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textbf{Curvature.}
 $\dfib^{\,2} = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \omega_1$, with period
 correction
 $F_1(\cA) = \kappa(\cA)/24$
 \textup{(}Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:genus1-curved-swiss-cheese}}\textup{)}.

\item \textbf{Spectral type.}
 The genus-$1$ classical $r$-matrix
 $r^{E_\tau}(z) = c_0 \cdot \zeta(z|\tau) + c_1 \cdot \wp(z|\tau)
 + \cdots$
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:elliptic-spectral-dichotomy}},
 equation~\eqref{eq:elliptic-r-matrix}\textup{)}
 is doubly periodic if\/ $c_0 = 0$ \textup{(}Cartan type\textup{)}
 and quasi-periodic with $B$-cycle monodromy
 $2\eta_\tau \cdot c_0$ if\/ $c_0 \ne 0$
 \textup{(}Yangian type\textup{)}.

\item \textbf{Five-theorem projection.}
 Each of Volume~I's five theorems specialises at genus~$1$
 as a deformation of the genus-$0$ data by the single
 parameter $\kappa(\cA) \cdot \omega_1$:
 \begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\Alph*$_1$)},leftmargin=2.5em]
 \item \emph{Bar-cobar:} curved dg coalgebra
 $(\barB^{(1)}(\cA), \dfib, \Delta)$ over $\Mbar_1$;
 \item \emph{Inversion:} curved quasi-isomorphism
 $\Omegach(\barB^{(1)}(\cA)) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA$
 in the coderived category;
 \item \emph{Complementarity:}
 $\kappa(\cA) + \kappa(\cA^!) = K(\cA)$ on the Koszul locus,
 where $K$ is a level-independent constant ($K = 0$ for the
 affine lineage; $K \neq 0$ for DS reductions);
 when $K = 0$, $\barB^{(1)}(\cA) \otimes \barB^{(1)}(\cA^!)$
 is uncurved;
 \item \emph{Leading coefficient:}
 $F_1 = \kappa(\cA)/24$ is the genus-$1$
 Faber--Pandharipande integral;
 \item \emph{Hochschild:}
 $\mathrm{CH}^\bullet(\cA)^{(1)}$ acquires a correction
 from the Hodge bundle
 $\mathbb{E} \to \Mbar_1$.
 \end{enumerate}
\end{enumerate}

All four atlas classes are chirally Koszul (bar cohomology
concentrated by PBW). Class~$\mathbf{G}$ has formal Swiss-cheese structure
($m_k^{\mathrm{SC}} = 0$ for all $k \ge 3$).
Classes~$\mathbf{L}$ and~$\mathbf{C}$ have finite but
nontrivial SC operations: class~$\mathbf{L}$ has
$m_3^{\mathrm{SC}} \ne 0$ with $m_k^{\mathrm{SC}} = 0$ for
$k \ge 4$ (depth~$3$); class~$\mathbf{C}$ has
$m_4^{\mathrm{SC}} \ne 0$ with $m_3^{\mathrm{SC}} = 0$ and
$m_k^{\mathrm{SC}} = 0$ for $k \ge 5$ (depth~$4$).
Class~$\mathbf{M}$ (Virasoro, $\cW_N$) has \emph{infinite
shadow depth} and fully non-formal Swiss-cheese structure
($m_k^{\mathrm{SC}} \ne 0$ for all $k \ge 3$), but still
possesses well-defined Koszul duals
(e.g.\ $\mathrm{Vir}_c^! = \mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$). The
five-theorem projection applies to all classes; for
class~$\mathbf{M}$, the bar-cobar adjunction holds but the
big Koszul dual carries higher $\Ainf$ operations.
Within the standard atlas families, the three
invariants $(\kappa, c_0, d)$ organise the atlas into three
genus-$1$ regimes, distinguished by their self-intersection
geometry and Coisson bracket:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{lllll}
\toprule
\textbf{Regime} & $c_0$ & \textbf{Intersection}
 & $R_1 \stackrel{?}{=} R_0$ & \textbf{Families} \\
\midrule
Decoupled & $= 0$ & clean
 & yes & $\cH_k,\; V_\Lambda$ \\
Propagator-entangled & $\ne 0$ & clean
 & no & $V_k(\fg),\; \beta\gamma$ \\
Doubly entangled & $\ne 0$ & excess
 & no & $\mathrm{Vir}_c,\; \cW_N$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Part~(i) is
Corollary~\ref{cor:genus1-curved-swiss-cheese}.
Part~(ii) is
Theorem~\ref{thm:elliptic-spectral-dichotomy}, items
(\ref{item:dichotomy-decoupling}) and
(\ref{item:dichotomy-entanglement}).
Part~(iii) packages the separately proved genus-$1$ analogues of the
five Volume~I theorems under the single deformation parameter
$\kappa \cdot \omega_1$. Specifically:
(A$_1$) is
Theorem~\ref{thm:curved-swiss-cheese}(i)--(ii);
(B$_1$) is Theorem~B of Volume~I applied to the
curved coalgebra via the Positselski framework
(Theorem~\ref{thm:curved-swiss-cheese}(ii) and
Volume~I, Theorem~B(b));
(C$_1$) is Theorem~\ref{thm:curved-swiss-cheese}(iii);
(D$_1$) is the $g = 1$ specialisation of Volume~I,
Theorem~D\textsubscript{scal};
(H$_1$) is the genus-$1$ chiral Hochschild
correction
(Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-bridge-genus0}
extended over $\Mbar_1$ via the corrected differential
$\Dg{1}$).

The three-regime classification follows from
Theorem~\ref{thm:pole-structure-dichotomy}.
Classes~$\mathbf{G}$, $\mathbf{L}$, $\mathbf{C}$ are
chirally Koszul: the bar cohomology is concentrated,
the bar complex is cogenerated in degree~$1$, and
$m_{k \ge 3} = 0$ on cohomology. For these,
the bar-complex
channel~(\ref{item:bar-channel}) is trivial, the curvature
$\kappa \cdot \omega_1$ is primitive, and the $\Eone$-coproduct
is genus-independent.
Class~$\mathbf{M}$ (Virasoro, $\cW_N$) \emph{is} chirally
Koszul (PBW degeneration holds for all members of the
standard landscape; see Volume~I,
PBW universality), but has
\emph{non-formal} Swiss-cheese structure: the higher
$\Ainf$ operations $m_{k \ge 3} \ne 0$ are non-trivial
on cohomology, the bar complex has higher-degree
cogenerators (from wheel diagrams), and the hypothesis of
bar-degree-$1$ cogeneration fails. Shadow depth is
infinite, reflecting the non-vanishing of the full
$\Ainf$ tower, but this is a measure of \emph{complexity}
within the Koszul world, not a failure of Koszulness itself
\textup{(}cf.\ the Koszulness programme discussion in Volume~I\textup{)}.
For these, the bar-complex
channel~(\ref{item:bar-channel}) can contribute genus
corrections.
The three regimes:
decoupled $\Leftrightarrow$ $c_0 = 0$ and $\Ainf$-formal
(conditions (ii)--(v) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:pole-structure-dichotomy});
propagator-entangled $\Leftrightarrow$ $c_0 \ne 0$ and
$\Ainf$-formal (bar-complex channel trivial by genus-zero
formality,
propagator channel non-trivial by
Theorem~\ref{thm:elliptic-spectral-dichotomy}(\ref{item:dichotomy-entanglement}));
doubly entangled $\Leftrightarrow$ $c_0 \ne 0$ and
$\Ainf$-non-formal (both channels can contribute, by
Theorem~\ref{thm:pole-structure-dichotomy}(vi)).
\end{proof}

\subsection{Heisenberg: all five theorems at genus~$1$}%
\label{subsec:heisenberg-genus1-endomorphism}

\begin{computation}[Heisenberg genus-$1$ endomorphism algebra;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:heisenberg-genus1-endomorphism}%
\index{Heisenberg algebra!genus-1 endomorphism}%
For $\cH_k$, the three invariants are
$\kappa = k$, $c_0 = 0$, $d = 2$
\textup{(}decoupled regime\textup{)}.
The genus-$1$ endomorphism algebra
$\End^{(1)}(\cL_{\cH_k})$ is the genus-$0$
endomorphism algebra tensored with a scalar from
the Hodge line.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(A$_1$) Curved bar-cobar.}
$\barB^{(1)}(\cH_k) = T^c(s^{-1}\overline{\cH}_k)$
with $\dfib^{\,2} = k \cdot \omega_1$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:rosetta-curved}).
The fiberwise differential on $E_\tau$ uses the
elliptic propagator $dG_\tau(z)$; the coproduct
$\Delta$ is unchanged.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(B$_1$) Curved inversion.}
The cobar $\Omegach(\barB^{(1)}(\cH_k))$ inverts the
curved bar complex in the coderived category of
Positselski: the augmentation
$\Omegach(\barB^{(1)}(\cH_k)) \to \cH_k$ is a
quasi-isomorphism after restricting to the coderived
category. This uses $m_{k \ge 3} = 0$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:rosetta-heisenberg-mk}): the
Koszulness of $\cH_k$ ensures that the bar-cobar
unit is an equivalence fiberwise.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(C$_1$) Complementarity.}
$\kappa(\cH_k) + \kappa(\cH_k^!) = k + (-k) = 0$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:rosetta-complementarity}).
The tensor product
$\barB^{(1)}(\cH_k) \otimes \barB^{(1)}(\cH_k^!)$
has flat differential: the curvatures cancel, and the
genus-$1$ complementary Lagrangians remain
complementary.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(D$_1$) Period correction.}
$F_1(\cH_k) = k/24$. This is the first
Faber--Pandharipande coefficient
(Corollary~\ref{cor:genus1-curved-swiss-cheese}):
$\dfib^{\,2} = k \cdot \omega_1$ is compensated by
$\delta_{\mathrm{per}}$ satisfying
$\Dg{1}^{\,2} = 0$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(H$_1$) Hochschild at genus~$1$.}
The chiral Hochschild cochains
$\mathrm{CH}^\bullet(\cH_k, \cH_k)$
at genus~$1$ acquire a correction from the Eisenstein
series $E_2(\tau)$: the propagator
$G_\tau(z) = \zeta(z|\tau) - \frac{\pi^2}{3}E_2(\tau) z$
(equation~\eqref{eq:rosetta-elliptic-propagator})
introduces quasi-modularity into the Hochschild
differential. The correction is proportional to $k$:
the Hochschild class $c_k \in H^2(\barB(\cH_k))$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:rosetta-bar-hochschild})
deforms by $k \cdot E_2(\tau)$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Spectral $r$-matrix.}
The $\lambda$-bracket $\{J_\lambda J\} = k\lambda$
has $c_0 = 0$ (no simple pole) and $c_1 = k$ (the
level). By
Theorem~\ref{thm:elliptic-spectral-dichotomy}(\ref{item:dichotomy-decoupling}):
\begin{equation}\label{eq:heisenberg-genus1-rmatrix}
r^{E_\tau}_{\cH_k}(z)
\;=\;
k \cdot \wp(z|\tau),
\end{equation}
which is doubly periodic on $E_\tau$. The spectral
$R$-matrix is unchanged from genus~$0$:
$R_1(z) = R_0(z) = e^{k\hbar/z}$
(Corollary~\ref{cor:rosetta-heisenberg-projections}(iii)).
The curvature $k \cdot \omega_1$ and the braiding
$k \cdot \wp(z|\tau)$ are decoupled: the former comes
from the $B$-cycle monodromy of $\zeta(z|\tau)$
acting on the bar differential, the latter from the
doubly periodic $\wp$-function which has no monodromy.
The $B$-cycle has no effect on $r$ because $c_0 = 0$
filters it out.
\end{computation}

\begin{computation}[Heisenberg line bundle; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{comp:heisenberg-line-bundle}
The line bundle $\cL_\kappa$ of Construction~\ref{constr:determinant-line-bundle} specialises for $\cA = \cH_k$ as follows. The modular characteristic is $\kappa(\cH_k) = k$, so:
\[
\cL_k \;=\; (\det \lambda)^{\otimes k},
\]
the $k$-th tensor power of the determinant of the Hodge bundle. Its first Chern class is $c_1(\cL_k) = k \cdot \omega_1 \in H^2(\overline{\cM}_1, \Z)$. The curvature of the Quillen connection on $\cL_k$ is $F_{\cL_k} = k \cdot F^Q = -2\pi i \cdot (k/12) \cdot \omega_{\mathrm{WP}}$. Sections of $\cL_k$ over $\overline{\cM}_1$ are modular forms of weight $k/2$; the genus-$1$ partition function $Z_1(\cH_k) = \eta(\tau)^{-k}$ is a section of $\cL_k^{-1}$.
\end{computation}

\begin{computation}[Heisenberg annular bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:heisenberg-annular-bar}%
\index{annular bar complex!Heisenberg|textbf}%
\index{Heisenberg algebra!annular bar complex|textbf}%
\index{Hochschild homology!Heisenberg annular model}%
The annular bar complex
$B^{\mathrm{ann}}_\bullet(\cH_k)$
(Construction~\ref{constr:annular-bar-vol2},
Definition~\ref{def:annular-bar}) is the first
explicit instantiation of the annular bar differential.
The Heisenberg algebra has $V = \bC \cdot J$,
OPE $J(z)J(w) \sim k/(z-w)^2$, and
ordered bar coalgebra $C = \Barchord(\cH_k) = T^c(s^{-1}\bC\cdot J)$
with bar differential
$d_{\barB}[s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J] = k$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:rosetta-e1-coalgebra}).
The diagonal bicomodule is $C_\Delta = C$ with left and
right coactions given by the deconcatenation coproduct.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(1) Degree $n=0$.}
The cyclic cotensor at degree~$0$ is
$\mathrm{cyc}^0(C,C_\Delta) = C_\Delta \widehat\otimes_C \bC
\cong \bC$,
the ground field (the ``empty annulus'':
no points on either boundary circle, no bulk insertions).
The differential acts trivially: $d^{\mathrm{ann}}|_{n=0} = 0$.
This contributes a single class to
$\HH^{\mathrm{ch}}_0(\cH_k)$: the vacuum
character of the annulus, the identity endomorphism of the
identity functor on $\cH_k\text{-mod}$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(2) Degree $n=1$.}
The cyclic cotensor at degree~$1$ is
$\mathrm{cyc}^1(C,C_\Delta) = C_\Delta \widehat\otimes_C C
\cong C$,
with underlying vector space
