$\bigoplus_{m \ge 0} (s^{-1}\bC\cdot J)^{\otimes m}$.
At tensor degree~$m$, an element is a cyclic word
$\langle s^{-1}J\,|\,\cdots\,|\,s^{-1}J\rangle$
of length~$m$ on a single boundary circle.
The four-component differential acts as follows:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item $d_{\mathrm{int}} = 0$:
 the internal differential of $\cH_k$ vanishes
 (no $Q$-operator).
\item $d_{\mathrm{res}}$: the OPE collision residue
 differential. On $\langle s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J\rangle$
 (cyclic degree~$2$), two adjacent points on the
 boundary circle can collide in the holomorphic
 direction, producing the residue $k$ from the
 double-pole OPE\@. The collision of two consecutive
 factors gives
 \[
  d_{\mathrm{res}}\langle s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J\rangle
  \;=\; k \cdot \langle\,\rangle,
 \]
 where $\langle\,\rangle$ is the empty cyclic word
 (degree~$0$). At cyclic degree $m \ge 3$, each adjacent
 pair contributes $k$; the contributions cancel pairwise
 by the Koszul sign rule for cyclic words of odd-degree
 elements.
\item $d_\Delta$: the non-wrapping coproduct face.
 On a cyclic word of length~$m$, this inserts a tensor
 splitting at each non-seam position. For
 $\langle s^{-1}J \rangle$ (cyclic degree~$1$), the
 deconcatenation coproduct gives
 $\Delta(s^{-1}J) = [] \otimes s^{-1}J + s^{-1}J \otimes []$,
 which is the coaugmentation and contributes no new terms
 to the cyclic cotensor.
\item $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$: the wrap-around differential
 at the seam of the boundary circle. On
 $\langle s^{-1}J \rangle$, the last factor wraps
 around and is re-inserted at the beginning,
 acquiring the $R$-matrix monodromy. For $\cH_k$,
 $R(z) = e^{k\hbar/z}$ and the monodromy around
 the generator of $\pi_1(S^1)$ is
 (Remark~\ref{rem:wraparound-monodromy})
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:heisenberg-wrap-monodromy}
  \mathrm{Mon}(R) \;=\; \exp(-2\pi i k).
 \end{equation}
 Since $R$ is scalar, the wrap-around on a cyclic word
 of length~$m$ produces an overall phase
 $\exp(-2\pi i k)^m = \exp(-2\pi i m k)$.
 On a single factor:
 $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}\langle s^{-1}J \rangle
 = \bigl(\exp(-2\pi i k) - 1\bigr)\langle s^{-1}J \rangle$,
 where the $-1$ accounts for the identity (unwrapped)
 term subtracted by the differential.
\end{enumerate}

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(3) Degree $n=2$.}
The cyclic cotensor at degree~$2$ is
$\mathrm{cyc}^2(C,C_\Delta) = C_\Delta \widehat\otimes_C C
\widehat\otimes_C C$,
with elements of the form
$\langle a_1\,|\,a_2\rangle$ (cyclic words of length~$2$).
The unique indecomposable element at tensor degree~$2$ is
$\langle s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J\rangle$.
The differential has:
\begin{itemize}
\item $d_{\mathrm{res}}\langle s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J\rangle
 = k \cdot \langle\,\rangle$
 (collision of the two adjacent factors, producing the
 OPE residue $k$; only one collision orbit by cyclic
 symmetry of a $2$-element cycle);
\item $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}\langle s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J\rangle
 = \exp(-2\pi i k)\langle s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J\rangle
 - \langle s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J\rangle$,
 the monodromy phase from wrapping the second factor past
 the seam. Since both factors are copies of the same
 generator $s^{-1}J$, the wrapped word
 $\langle s^{-1}J\,|\,s^{-1}J\rangle$ is the
 same element up to the monodromy scalar.
\end{itemize}
The identity $(d^{\mathrm{ann}})^2 = 0$ at degree~$2$
is the annular analogue of the Arnold relation: the
two boundary strata of the annular FM space
(collision and wrap-around) compose to zero.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(4) The four-component differential: summary.}
For $\cH_k$, three of the four components simplify
to closed-form scalars:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{@{}l@{\;\;}l@{\;\;}l@{}}
\textbf{Component} & \textbf{Source} &
 \textbf{Value for $\cH_k$} \\
\hline
$d_{\mathrm{int}}$
 & internal differential
 & $0$ (no $Q$-operator) \\[2pt]
$d_{\mathrm{res}}$
 & OPE collision on $\FM_2(\C)$
 & $k$ (from $J_{(1)}J = k$) \\[2pt]
$d_\Delta$
 & deconcatenation at non-seam faces
 & coaugmentation terms only \\[2pt]
$d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$
 & wrap-around at seam of $S^1$
 & phase $\exp(-2\pi i k)$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The total differential on a cyclic word of length~$m$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:heisenberg-annular-total}
d^{\mathrm{ann}}\langle s^{-1}J\,|\,\cdots\,|\,s^{-1}J\rangle
\;=\;
m\,k\cdot
\langle s^{-1}J\,|\,\cdots\,|\,s^{-1}J\rangle_{m-1}
\;+\;
\bigl(e^{-2\pi i m k} - 1\bigr)
\langle s^{-1}J\,|\,\cdots\,|\,s^{-1}J\rangle_{m},
\end{equation}
where the first term is the collision residue
(each of the $m$ adjacent pairs contributes $k$,
reduced to a single orbit by cyclic symmetry)
and the second is the wrap-around monodromy.
The factor $m$ in the collision term is the number
of cyclic-adjacent pairs on a circle with $m$ marked
points.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(5) Hochschild homology $\HH_0^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k)$:
the character space.}
The zeroth Hochschild homology is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:heisenberg-HH0}
\HH_0^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k)
\;=\;
H_0\bigl(B^{\mathrm{ann}}_\bullet(\cH_k)\bigr)
\;\cong\;
\cH_k / [\cH_k, \cH_k]_{\mathrm{ch}},
\end{equation}
the quotient of $\cH_k$ by chiral commutators.
For the Heisenberg algebra, the chiral commutator
$[J,J]_{\mathrm{ch}} = J_{(0)}J = 0$ vanishes
(no simple pole), so every element is a class:
\[
\HH_0^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k)
\;\cong\;
\bC[J, \partial J, \partial^2 J, \ldots]
\;=\;
\bC[\partial^n J : n \ge 0].
\]
This is the space of conformal characters:
each element $f(J, \partial J, \ldots)$
of the differential polynomial ring defines a
trace functional
$\cH_k \to \bC$
via insertion into the annulus
(the trace of $f$ on the torus).
The graded character is
\[
\chi\bigl(\HH_0^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k);\, q\bigr)
\;=\;
\prod_{n=0}^{\infty} \frac{1}{1-q^{n+1}}
\;=\;
\frac{1}{\prod_{n=1}^{\infty}(1-q^n)}
\;=\;
\frac{q^{1/24}}{\eta(q)},
\]
recovering the bosonic partition function
(Computation~\ref{comp:heisenberg-line-bundle}).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(6) Modulus dependence: chain vs homology.}
At the chain level, $B^{\mathrm{ann}}_\bullet(\cH_k)$
depends on the conformal modulus~$\tau$ of the annulus
$\mathrm{Ann}_\tau$
(Remark~\ref{rem:annular-modulus-dependence}).
For $\cH_k$, this dependence enters through
the collision residue differential $d_{\mathrm{res}}$:
the propagator on $\mathrm{Ann}_\tau$ is the elliptic
Green's function
$G_\tau(z) = \zeta(z|\tau) - \tfrac{\pi^2}{3}E_2(\tau)\cdot z$
(equation~\eqref{eq:rosetta-elliptic-propagator}),
which is a holomorphic function of~$\tau$. The
genus-$1$ correction to the binary operation is
$m_2^{(1)}(J,J;\lambda;\tau) = k\lambda
- (\pi^2 k/3)\, E_2(\tau)\, \lambda$
(equation~\eqref{eq:e1-shadow-genus1-m2}).

At the level of homology, the $\tau$-dependence disappears:
$\HH_\bullet^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k)$
is the factorisation homology $\int_{S^1}\cH_k$,
which depends only on the topological type of $S^1$
and not on the conformal modulus of the annulus
that models it. The chain-level $\tau$-dependence
is the Heisenberg instance of the general
principle (Remark~\ref{rem:annular-modulus-dependence}):
the $E_1$-chain model sees the holomorphic annulus
and its modulus~$\tau$; the homology sees only the
topological circle. The Hodge-to-de~Rham spectral
sequence degenerates at $E_1$ for $\cH_k$
(because $\cH_k$ is formal: $m_k = 0$ for $k \ge 3$),
and the degeneration is the mechanism by which the
Eisenstein correction $E_2(\tau)$ becomes invisible
in homology.

The physical interpretation:
the annulus of modulus~$\tau$ is the propagator of
the 2d CFT between two boundary circles. At the chain
level, the propagator depends on~$\tau$
(the Schwinger proper time). At the level of the
partition function, the integral over~$\tau$
(the modular integral $\int_{\mathfrak{h}/\mathrm{SL}(2,\Z)}
d^2\tau / (\mathrm{Im}\,\tau)^2$)
produces the $\tau$-independent answer: the modular
invariant $|\eta(\tau)|^{-2k}$ of the free boson.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(7) The wrap-around monodromy $\exp(-2\pi ik)$ and integrality.}
The monodromy $\exp(-2\pi ik)$
(equation~\eqref{eq:heisenberg-wrap-monodromy})
is trivial (equal to~$1$) if and only if $k \in \Z$.
At integer level, the wrap-around differential
$d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$ reduces to the standard cyclic
rotation: $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}\langle a_1|\cdots|a_n\rangle
= \langle a_n|a_1|\cdots|a_{n-1}\rangle
- \langle a_1|\cdots|a_n\rangle$
up to signs. This is the classical cyclic bar
complex of Connes. At non-integer level, the monodromy
is a nontrivial phase, and the annular bar complex
carries genuinely more information than the
classical cyclic complex: the phase
$\exp(-2\pi ik)$ records the conformal spin of the
boundary field $J$.

The three regimes:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $k \in \Z$: monodromy trivial,
 $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$ = cyclic rotation,
 $\HH_\bullet(\cH_k) = $ classical Hochschild;
\item $k \in \mathbb{Q} \setminus \Z$: monodromy a
 root of unity, finite-order periodicity of the
 wrap-around, $\HH_\bullet(\cH_k)$ periodic;
\item $k \notin \mathbb{Q}$: monodromy irrational,
 $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$ ergodic,
 $\HH_\bullet(\cH_k)$ concentrated in degree~$0$.
\end{enumerate}
This trichotomy is the Heisenberg instance of the
rationality/irrationality divide for chiral algebras:
the annular bar complex detects rationality through
the arithmetic of the wrap-around monodromy.
\end{computation}

\subsection{Affine $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$:
 the Yangian-to-elliptic passage}%
\label{subsec:affine-genus1-endomorphism}

\begin{computation}[Affine $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ genus-$1$
endomorphism algebra; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:affine-sl2-genus1-endomorphism}%
\index{affine Kac--Moody!genus-1 endomorphism}%
\index{elliptic quantum group!from genus-1 Lagrangian}%
\index{Yangian!elliptic deformation}%
For $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ with generators
$J^a$ ($a = 1,2,3$) and $\lambda$-bracket
$\{J^a_\lambda J^b\} = f^{ab}_c J^c + k\,\kappa^{ab}\lambda$,
the three invariants are:
$\kappa = 3(k+2)/4$,
$c_0 = \Omega := \sum_a t^a \otimes t_a$ \textup{(}the
quadratic Casimir, from the Lie bracket\textup{)},
$d = 3$ \textup{(}propagator-entangled regime\textup{)}.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Period correction.}
$F_1 = 3(k+2)/96 = (k+2)/32$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Genus-$1$ $r$-matrix.}
The Laurent coefficients are $c_0 = \Omega \ne 0$
and $c_1 = k\,\kappa$. By
Theorem~\ref{thm:elliptic-spectral-dichotomy}:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:affine-genus1-rmatrix}
r^{E_\tau}_{V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)}(z)
\;=\;
k\,\Omega \cdot \zeta(z|\tau)
\;+\;
k\,\kappa \cdot \wp(z|\tau),
\end{equation}
with $B$-cycle monodromy
$r^{E_\tau}(z + \tau) - r^{E_\tau}(z) = 2k\,\eta_\tau \cdot \Omega$
(equation~\eqref{eq:r-monodromy}). At $k = 0$ every
term vanishes, consistent with the abelian limit
. This is the
\emph{elliptic classical $r$-matrix}: the genus-$0$
rational $r$-matrix $r_0(z) = k\,\Omega/z + k\,\kappa/z^2$
deforms by replacing $1/z \leadsto \zeta(z|\tau)$ and
$1/z^2 \leadsto \wp(z|\tau)$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{The DK hierarchy and the genus tower.}
The genus expansion of the $r$-matrix parallels
the Drinfeld--Kohno hierarchy of quantum groups:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\toprule
\textbf{Genus} & \textbf{$r$-matrix} &
 \textbf{Quantum group} \\
\midrule
$g = 0$ & $r_0(z) = k\,\Omega/z + \cdots$
 & Yangian $Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ \\
$g = 1$ & $r_1(z,\tau) = k\,\Omega\cdot\zeta + \cdots$
 & Elliptic quantum group \\
$g \ge 2$ & $r_g(z,\Omega_{ij}) = k\,\Omega\cdot\omega_g + \cdots$
 & (conjectural) \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
At genus~$0$ and~$1$, this identification is a theorem:
the rational kernel $1/z$ is replaced by
$\zeta(z|\tau)$ via
Theorem~\ref{thm:elliptic-spectral-dichotomy},
and the resulting $r$-matrix is the classical
elliptic $r$-matrix of Belavin--Drinfeld.
At genus~$\ge 2$, the replacement of kernel functions
by their higher-genus counterparts (via the
period matrix $(\Omega_{ij})$ of $\Sigma_g$) produces a
candidate higher-genus quantum group structure,
but the identification is not proved.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Entanglement.}
The curvature $\kappa \cdot \omega_1$ extracts $c_1 = k\kappa$
(the highest pole, a scalar); the braiding monodromy
$2\eta_\tau \cdot \Omega$ extracts $c_0 = \Omega$
(the lowest pole, a tensor). Both arise from the
quasi-periodicity of $\zeta(z|\tau)$ (the $B$-cycle is
the common geometric source), but they probe different
OPE pole orders. The entanglement is one-directional:
the curvature is visible in the closed-colour
differential ($\dfib^{\,2} \ne 0$), the braiding monodromy is
visible in the mixed-colour $r$-matrix ($r_1 \ne r_0$),
but the open-colour coproduct $\Delta$ remains
flat at genus~$1$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:curved-swiss-cheese}(i)).
\end{computation}

\begin{computation}[Affine $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ annular bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:affine-sl2-annular-bar}%
\index{annular bar complex!affine sl2@affine $\mathfrak{sl}_2$|textbf}%
\index{affine Kac--Moody!annular bar complex|textbf}%
\index{Hochschild homology!affine annular model}%
The annular bar complex
$B^{\mathrm{ann}}_\bullet(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2))$
(Construction~\ref{constr:annular-bar-vol2},
Definition~\ref{def:annular-bar}) is the first
\emph{nonabelian} instantiation of the annular bar
differential. Generators: currents $J^a$ ($a=1,2,3$)
in the Killing-orthonormal basis with
$[t^a, t^b] = \epsilon^{abc}\, t^c$ and
$\kappa^{ab} = \delta^{ab}$. OPE:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-ann-ope}
J^a(z)\, J^b(w)
\;\sim\;
\frac{k\,\delta^{ab}}{(z-w)^2}
\;+\;
\frac{\epsilon^{ab}{}_c\, J^c(w)}{z-w}.
\end{equation}
The ordered bar coalgebra is $C = \Barchord(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2))
= T^c(s^{-1}V)$ with $V = \bC^3 = \mathrm{span}\{J^1,J^2,J^3\}$,
and the diagonal bicomodule is $C_\Delta = C$
with deconcatenation coactions.

Two structural features distinguish this from the
abelian case (Computation~\ref{comp:heisenberg-annular-bar}):
\begin{itemize}
\item The bar differential has a \emph{simple-pole component}:
 $d_{\barB}[s^{-1}J^a\,|\,s^{-1}J^b]
 = k\,\delta^{ab} + \epsilon^{ab}{}_c\, s^{-1}J^c$.
 The first term (double pole, scalar) is the Heisenberg
 contribution; the second (simple pole, valued in~$V$)
 is the Lie bracket. Heisenberg has only the first.
\item The $R$-matrix is \emph{matrix-valued}:
 $R(z) = 1 + k\,\Omega/z + \cdots$ with
 $\Omega = \sum_a t^a \otimes t_a \in
 \mathfrak{sl}_2 \otimes \mathfrak{sl}_2$,
 while Heisenberg has $R(z) = e^{k/z}$ (scalar).
 The KZ monodromy $\exp(-2\pi ik\,\Omega)$ is a
 genuine matrix acting on $V^{\otimes n}$, not a phase.
\end{itemize}

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(1) Degree $n=0$.}
As in the abelian case,
$\mathrm{cyc}^0(C,C_\Delta) \cong \bC$
with $d^{\mathrm{ann}}|_{n=0} = 0$. This contributes the
vacuum class to $\HH^{\mathrm{ch}}_0(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2))$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(2) Degree $n=1$.}
The cyclic cotensor at degree~$1$ is
$\mathrm{cyc}^1(C,C_\Delta) \cong C$,
with underlying space
$\bigoplus_{m \ge 0} (s^{-1}V)^{\otimes m}$.
A cyclic word of tensor degree~$m$ is
$\langle s^{-1}J^{a_1}\,|\,\cdots\,|\,s^{-1}J^{a_m}\rangle$.
The four components of $d^{\mathrm{ann}}$ act as follows.

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item $d_{\mathrm{int}} = 0$: no internal differential
 ($V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ has no $Q$-operator at the
 level of generators).

\item $d_{\mathrm{res}}$: the OPE collision residue.
 On a cyclic word of degree~$2$:
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-ann-dres-2}
 d_{\mathrm{res}}
 \langle s^{-1}J^a\,|\,s^{-1}J^b\rangle
 \;=\;
 k\,\delta^{ab}\cdot\langle\,\rangle
 \;+\;
 \epsilon^{ab}{}_c\cdot
 \langle s^{-1}J^c\rangle.
 \end{equation}
 The first term is the double-pole residue (the
 Heisenberg piece: collision contracts two generators
 to the scalar~$k\,\delta^{ab}$); the second is the
 simple-pole residue (the Lie-bracket piece: collision
 fuses $J^a$ and $J^b$ into $\epsilon^{ab}{}_c\, J^c$).
 At degree~$m \ge 3$, each cyclically adjacent pair
 $(a_i, a_{i+1})$ contributes both terms:
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-ann-dres-m}
 d_{\mathrm{res}}
 \langle s^{-1}J^{a_1}\,|\,\cdots\,|\,s^{-1}J^{a_m}\rangle
 \;=\;
 \sum_{i \in \Z/m\Z}
 \Bigl(
  k\,\delta^{a_i a_{i+1}}\cdot
  \langle\cdots\,
  \widehat{a_i}\,\widehat{a_{i+1}}
  \,\cdots\rangle
 \;+\;
  \epsilon^{a_i a_{i+1}}{}_c\cdot
  \langle\cdots\,
  s^{-1}J^c\,\cdots\rangle
 \Bigr),
 \end{equation}
 where $\widehat{a_i}\,\widehat{a_{i+1}}$ denotes
 omission of the colliding pair. The summation
 is over the $m$ cyclically adjacent pairs.
 In the abelian case ($\epsilon^{ab}{}_c = 0$), only the
 first term survives, recovering the Heisenberg formula.

\item $d_\Delta$: the deconcatenation coproduct at
 non-seam faces. Same structural form as the
 abelian case; no new features from the Lie bracket.

\item $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$: the wrap-around differential.
 This is the principal novelty. On a cyclic word
 of degree~$m$, the last factor wraps around the
 boundary circle and is re-inserted at the beginning,
 acquiring the KZ monodromy
 (Remark~\ref{rem:wraparound-monodromy}).

 For $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$, the $R$-matrix is
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-ann-Rmatrix}
 R(z) \;=\; 1 + \frac{k\,\Omega}{z}
 + \frac{k^2\,\Omega^2}{2z^2} + \cdots
 \;=\; \exp\!\Bigl(\frac{k\,\Omega}{z}\Bigr)
 + O(1/z^2),
 \end{equation}
 where $\Omega = \sum_a t^a \otimes t_a$
 is the quadratic Casimir tensor.
 The monodromy of the KZ connection around the
 generator of $\pi_1(S^1)$ is
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-ann-KZ-monodromy}
 \mathrm{Mon}_{\mathrm{KZ}}
 \;=\;
 \cP\exp\!\Bigl(
  -\frac{k}{2\pi i}
  \oint \Omega_{ij}\, d\log(z_i - z_j)
 \Bigr)
 \;=\;
 \exp(-2\pi ik\,\Omega_{(m)}),
 \end{equation}
 where $\Omega_{(m)} = \sum_{1 \le i < j \le m}
 \Omega_{ij}$ is the total Casimir acting on
 $V^{\otimes m}$, with $\Omega_{ij}$ placing
 $\Omega$ in the $i$-th and $j$-th tensor factors.

 On a single generator ($m=1$):
 \[
  d_{\mathrm{wrap}}\langle s^{-1}J^a \rangle
  \;=\;
  \bigl(\exp(-2\pi ik\cdot 0) - 1\bigr)
  \langle s^{-1}J^a \rangle
  \;=\; 0,
 \]
 since $\Omega_{(1)} = 0$ (no pair of factors for
 the Casimir to act on).

 On a pair ($m=2$): $\Omega_{(2)} = \Omega_{12}$
 acts on $s^{-1}J^a \otimes s^{-1}J^b$ as
 $\Omega_{12}(J^a \otimes J^b) = \sum_c
 (t^c \cdot J^a) \otimes (t_c \cdot J^b)
 = \sum_c \epsilon^{ca}{}_d\, \epsilon_{c}{}^{b}{}_e\,
 J^d \otimes J^e$.
 For $\mathfrak{sl}_2$, the Casimir eigenvalue on
 $V \otimes V = \mathrm{Sym}^2 V \oplus \bC$
 (the decomposition $\mathbf{3} \otimes \mathbf{3}
 = \mathbf{5} \oplus \mathbf{3} \oplus \mathbf{1}$
 of the adjoint representation) is:
 \begin{align}
 \Omega_{12}\big|_{\mathbf{5}} &= 1,
 &
 \Omega_{12}\big|_{\mathbf{3}} &= -1,
 &
 \Omega_{12}\big|_{\mathbf{1}} &= -2,
 \label{eq:sl2-casimir-eigenvalues}
 \end{align}
 using $\Omega_{12} = \tfrac{1}{2}(C_2^{\mathrm{total}}
 - C_2^{(1)} - C_2^{(2)})$ with $C_2^{\mathrm{adj}} = 2$
 on each factor.
 The wrap-around on a cyclic two-element word is:
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-ann-wrap-2}
 d_{\mathrm{wrap}}
 \langle s^{-1}J^a\,|\,s^{-1}J^b\rangle
 \;=\;
 \bigl(
  e^{-2\pi ik\,\Omega_{12}} - 1
 \bigr)
 \langle s^{-1}J^a\,|\,s^{-1}J^b\rangle,
 \end{equation}
 where $e^{-2\pi ik\,\Omega_{12}}$ acts as a
 matrix on the colour indices.
 Projecting onto the irreducible components:
 \begin{align}
 d_{\mathrm{wrap}}\big|_{\mathbf{5}}
 &= (e^{-2\pi ik} - 1) \cdot \id_{\mathbf{5}},
 \notag \\[3pt]
 d_{\mathrm{wrap}}\big|_{\mathbf{3}}
 &= (e^{2\pi ik} - 1) \cdot \id_{\mathbf{3}},
 \label{eq:sl2-ann-wrap-isotypic}\\[3pt]
 d_{\mathrm{wrap}}\big|_{\mathbf{1}}
 &= (e^{4\pi ik} - 1) \cdot \id_{\mathbf{1}}.
 \notag
 \end{align}
 The three isotypic components acquire \emph{different}
 monodromy phases. This is the fundamental
 non-abelian phenomenon: the Heisenberg annular bar
 has a single scalar phase $e^{-2\pi ik}$ at each
 degree, while $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ splits the
 wrap-around into representation-theoretic eigenspaces.

 The monodromy $\exp(-2\pi ik\,\Omega_{(m)})$ uses the
 \emph{unreduced} bar-complex collision residue
 $r(z) = k\,\Omega/z$, not the KZ-normalised coefficient
 $\Omega/(k+h^\vee)$.  The two differ by the Sugawara
 normalisation: reducing to conformal-block level
 (dividing by the level of the invariant form) replaces
 $k\,\Omega$ with $\Omega/(k+h^\vee)$, recovering
 the standard KZ monodromy
 $\exp\!\bigl({-}2\pi i\,\Omega/(k+h^\vee)\bigr)$
 of Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:affine-monodromy-identification}}.
\end{enumerate}

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(3) Degree $n=2$.}
At degree~$2$, the indecomposable elements are
$\langle s^{-1}J^a\,|\,s^{-1}J^b\rangle$
(the same underlying vector space as degree~$1$,
degree~$2$, but now the cyclic word has two marked
segments on the boundary circle).
The four-component differential combines:
\begin{itemize}
\item $d_{\mathrm{res}}
 \langle s^{-1}J^a\,|\,s^{-1}J^b\rangle
 = k\,\delta^{ab}\cdot\langle\,\rangle
 + \epsilon^{ab}{}_c\cdot\langle s^{-1}J^c\rangle$
 (identical to degree~$1$, degree~$2$:
 equation~\eqref{eq:sl2-ann-dres-2});
\item $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}
 \langle s^{-1}J^a\,|\,s^{-1}J^b\rangle
 = (e^{-2\pi ik\,\Omega_{12}} - 1)
 \langle s^{-1}J^a\,|\,s^{-1}J^b\rangle$
 (equation~\eqref{eq:sl2-ann-wrap-2}).
\end{itemize}
The identity $(d^{\mathrm{ann}})^2 = 0$ at degree~$2$
requires cancellation between
$d_{\mathrm{res}} \circ d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$ and
$d_{\mathrm{wrap}} \circ d_{\mathrm{res}}$.
This is the annular Arnold relation
(Theorem~\ref{thm:annular-bar-differential}): the
two boundary strata of $\overline{\FM}{}^{\mathrm{ann}}_{2}$
compose to zero. At the algebraic level, it is the
statement that the KZ monodromy
$e^{-2\pi ik\,\Omega_{12}}$ \emph{intertwines} the
OPE collision map: the Lie bracket $\epsilon^{ab}{}_c$
commutes with the Casimir action $\Omega_{12}$
(because $\Omega$ is $\fg$-invariant).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(4) The four-component differential: summary.}
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{@{}l@{\;\;}l@{\;\;}l@{}}
\textbf{Component} & \textbf{Source} &
 \textbf{Value for $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$} \\
\hline
$d_{\mathrm{int}}$
 & internal differential
 & $0$ (no $Q$-operator on generators) \\[2pt]
$d_{\mathrm{res}}$
 & OPE collision on $\FM_2(\C)$
 & $k\,\delta^{ab} + \epsilon^{ab}{}_c\, J^c$
  \;(double + simple pole) \\[2pt]
$d_\Delta$
 & deconcatenation at non-seam faces
 & coaugmentation terms only \\[2pt]
$d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$
 & wrap-around at seam of $S^1$
 & matrix $\exp(-2\pi ik\,\Omega_{(m)})$
 on $V^{\otimes m}$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Comparison with Heisenberg
(Computation~\ref{comp:heisenberg-annular-bar}):
the Heisenberg column has $d_{\mathrm{res}} = k$
(scalar) and $d_{\mathrm{wrap}} = e^{-2\pi ik}$ (phase).
The $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ column replaces both with
matrix-valued operations: $d_{\mathrm{res}}$ carries
the Lie bracket, and $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$ carries the
Casimir matrix exponential.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(5) $\HH_0^{\mathrm{ch}}(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2))$:
the character space.}
The zeroth chiral Hochschild homology is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-HH0}
\HH_0^{\mathrm{ch}}(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2))
\;\cong\;
V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)
\big/
[V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2),\,
 V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)]_{\mathrm{ch}},
\end{equation}
the quotient by chiral commutators.
The chiral commutator of the generators is
$J^a_{(0)} J^b = \epsilon^{ab}{}_c\, J^c$
(the simple-pole residue), which is the
\emph{adjoint action} of $\fg$ on $V_k(\fg)$.
The quotient~\eqref{eq:sl2-HH0} is therefore the
space of $\fg$-coinvariants:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-HH0-coinv}
\HH_0^{\mathrm{ch}}(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2))
\;\cong\;
V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)_{\mathfrak{sl}_2}
\;=\;
\bigl\{
 v \in V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)
 \,:\,
 J^a_{(0)} v = 0
 \;\text{for all } a
\bigr\}^*,
\end{equation}
i.e., the dual of the space of $\mathfrak{sl}_2$-singular
vectors. This is a strict quotient of the Heisenberg answer
$\bC[\partial^n J^a : n \ge 0,\, a=1,2,3]$: the Lie-bracket
piece of $d_{\mathrm{res}}$ imposes the additional
$\fg$-coinvariance condition that is absent for $\cH_k$.

At \emph{integrable} level $k \in \Z_{\ge 0}$,
the algebra $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ has finitely many
irreducible modules $L_0, L_1, \ldots, L_k$
(with $L_j$ of spin~$j/2$), and the character
space has dimension $k+1$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-HH0-integrable}
\dim\, \HH_0^{\mathrm{ch}}(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2))
\;=\; k+1
\qquad (k \in \Z_{\ge 0}).
\end{equation}
The basis consists of the characters
$\chi_j(\tau) = \mathrm{tr}_{L_j}(q^{L_0 - c/24})$,
$j = 0, 1, \ldots, k$, with
$c = 3k/(k+2)$. These are the conformal blocks of
the WZW model on the torus: each character is a
trace functional obtained by inserting an element
of $\HH_0^{\mathrm{ch}}$ into the annulus.

At generic (non-integrable) level, the $\fg$-coinvariant
space is infinite-dimensional, generated by
$\mathfrak{sl}_2$-singular vectors at each conformal
weight. The graded character is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sl2-HH0-generic-char}
\chi\bigl(\HH_0^{\mathrm{ch}}(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2));\, q\bigr)
\;=\;
\frac{1}{\prod_{n=1}^{\infty}(1-q^n)^3}
\;\cdot\;
P_{\mathfrak{sl}_2\text{-}\mathrm{sing}}(q),
\end{equation}
where $\prod(1-q^n)^{-3}$ is the free-boson
factor ($\dim\fg = 3$ copies) and
$P_{\mathfrak{sl}_2\text{-}\mathrm{sing}}(q)$
is the Poincar\'e polynomial of the singular
vector quotient, which depends on the level~$k$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{(6) The non-abelian features: structure-constant
collision and matrix monodromy.}
Two phenomena distinguish the nonabelian annular bar
from the abelian case.

\emph{(6a) The Lie-bracket collision.}
The simple-pole term
$\epsilon^{ab}{}_c\, J^c$ in
$d_{\mathrm{res}}$ means that two generators on the
boundary circle can \emph{fuse} into a third generator,
not merely annihilate to a scalar. On a cyclic word
of degree~$3$:
\begin{multline}\label{eq:sl2-ann-dres-3}
d_{\mathrm{res}}
\langle s^{-1}J^a\,|\,s^{-1}J^b\,|\,s^{-1}J^c\rangle
\;=\;
k\,\delta^{ab}\cdot
\langle s^{-1}J^c\rangle
\;+\;
k\,\delta^{bc}\cdot
\langle s^{-1}J^a\rangle
\;+\;
k\,\delta^{ca}\cdot
\langle s^{-1}J^b\rangle \\
\;+\;
\epsilon^{ab}{}_d\cdot
\langle s^{-1}J^d\,|\,s^{-1}J^c\rangle
\;+\;
\epsilon^{bc}{}_d\cdot
\langle s^{-1}J^a\,|\,s^{-1}J^d\rangle
\;+\;
\epsilon^{ca}{}_d\cdot
\langle s^{-1}J^d\,|\,s^{-1}J^b\rangle.
\end{multline}
The first line is the Heisenberg contribution
(double-pole contractions of each adjacent pair);
the second line is the Lie-bracket contribution
(simple-pole fusions). The Jacobi identity
$\epsilon^{ab}{}_d\,\epsilon^{dc}{}_e
+ \epsilon^{bc}{}_d\,\epsilon^{da}{}_e
+ \epsilon^{ca}{}_d\,\epsilon^{db}{}_e = 0$
ensures that applying $d_{\mathrm{res}}$ twice to the
second line yields zero: this is the chain-level
statement that the $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ Jacobi identity
controls $(d^{\mathrm{ann}})^2 = 0$.

\emph{(6b) The matrix KZ monodromy.}
The wrap-around $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$ on
$V^{\otimes m}$ is the matrix exponential
$\exp(-2\pi ik\,\Omega_{(m)})$, which does not reduce
to a scalar. The eigenvalues of $\Omega_{(m)}$ on an
irreducible $\mathfrak{sl}_2$-representation of
spin~$\ell$ inside $V^{\otimes m}$ are
$\tfrac{1}{2}(\ell(\ell+1) - m \cdot 2)$
(from $\Omega_{(m)} = \tfrac{1}{2}
(C_2^{\mathrm{total}} - \sum_i C_2^{(i)})$
with $C_2^{\mathrm{adj}} = 2$).
The wrap-around differential thus
\emph{decomposes the annular bar complex
into isotypic components}, each acquiring a
different monodromy eigenvalue
$\exp(-\pi ik(\ell(\ell+1) - 2m))$.
The isotypic decomposition of
$B^{\mathrm{ann}}_\bullet(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2))$
by the total-spin quantum number~$\ell$ is the
chain-level avatar of the decomposition of
$\HH^{\mathrm{ch}}_\bullet(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2))$
into sectors labelled by integrable representations.

The three regimes of the wrap-around, by analogy with
Computation~\ref{comp:heisenberg-annular-bar}(7):
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $k \in \Z_{\ge 0}$ (integrable):
 $\exp(-2\pi ik\,\Omega_{(m)})$ is a matrix
 whose eigenvalues are roots of unity.
 The annular bar complex decomposes into $k+1$
 sectors, one per integrable highest-weight
 module~$L_j$. Each sector is periodic.
\item $k \in \bQ \setminus \Z$ (rational,
 non-integrable): eigenvalues are roots of unity of
 varying orders; the annular bar complex is
 quasi-periodic with the common period determined
 by the denominator of~$k$.
\item $k \notin \bQ$ (irrational): the eigenvalues
 $\exp(-\pi ik\,\ell(\ell+1))$ for distinct spins~$\ell$
 are rationally independent. The wrap-around acts
 ergodically on each isotypic component,
 and $\HH^{\mathrm{ch}}_\bullet(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2))$
 is concentrated in degree~$0$.
\end{enumerate}

At integrable level, the finite-dimensionality
$\dim\,\HH_0^{\mathrm{ch}} = k+1$
(equation~\eqref{eq:sl2-HH0-integrable}) is the
statement that the wrap-around monodromy, together with
the Lie-bracket collision, selects exactly the $k+1$
conformal characters from the infinite-dimensional
space of $\fg$-coinvariants. The annular bar complex
is the chain-level mechanism behind the Verlinde formula.
\end{computation}


\subsection{The genus-1 atlas and the modular programme}%
\label{subsec:genus1-atlas-table}

\begin{computation}[Genus-$1$ atlas; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:genus1-atlas}%
\index{genus-1 atlas|textbf}%
\index{modular programme!genus-1 coefficients}%
For all standard families, the genus-$1$ invariants:

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabular}{llcccccc}
\toprule
\textbf{Family} & \textbf{Class}
& $\kappa$ & $F_1 = \kappa/24$
& $c_0$ & \textbf{$r_1$ type}
& $R_1 {=} R_0$? \\
\midrule
$\cH_k$ & $\mathbf{G}$
 & $k$ & $k/24$
 & $0$ & periodic
 & $\checkmark$ \\[2pt]
$V_\Lambda$ (mom.) & $\mathbf{G}$
 & $\operatorname{rk}(\Lambda)$
 & $\operatorname{rk}(\Lambda)/24$
 & $0$ & periodic
 & $\checkmark$ \\[2pt]
$V_\Lambda$ (v.o.) & $\mathbf{L}$
 & $\dfrac{(1{+}h^\vee_\Lambda)\operatorname{rk}(\Lambda)}{2h^\vee_\Lambda}$
 & (as $V_k(\fg)$)
 & $\Omega_\Lambda \ne 0$ & quasi-per.\
 & \\[4pt]
$V_k(\fg)$ & $\mathbf{L}$
 & $\dfrac{(k{+}h^\vee)\dim\fg}{2h^\vee}$
 & $\dfrac{(k{+}h^\vee)\dim\fg}{48h^\vee}$
 & $\Omega_\fg \ne 0$ & quasi-per.\
 & \\[4pt]
$\beta\gamma$ & $\mathbf{C}$
 & $-1$
 & $-1/24$
 & $\Omega_{\mathrm{symp}} \ne 0$ & quasi-per.\
 & \\[2pt]
$\mathrm{Vir}_c$ & $\mathbf{M}$
 & $c/2$
 & $c/48$
 & $\partial T \ne 0$ & quasi-per.\
 & \\[2pt]
$\cW_3$ & $\mathbf{M}$
 & $5c/6$
 & $5c/144$
 & $\ne 0$ & quasi-per.\
 & \\[2pt]
$\cW_N$ & $\mathbf{M}$
 & $c(H_N{-}1)$
 & $c(H_N{-}1)/24$
 & $\ne 0$ & quasi-per.\
 & \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Here $\Omega_\fg = \sum_a t^a \otimes t_a$ is the
quadratic Casimir,
$\Omega_{\mathrm{symp}}$ is the symplectic pairing
from $\{\beta \,{}_0\, \gamma\} = 1$
\textup{(}the simple-pole OPE\textup{)},
and $\partial T = T_{(0)}T$ is the translation
derivation of the Virasoro PVA\@. The $R_1 = R_0$
column is blank when $R_1 \ne R_0$.
\end{computation}

\begin{remark}[The genus-$1$ dichotomy refines the depth
classification]%
\label{rem:genus1-dichotomy}%
\index{genus-1 dichotomy}%
\index{Coisson bracket!genus-1 classification}%
The shadow obstruction tower atlas
(Computation~\ref{comp:shadow-tower-atlas}) classifies by
the genus-$0$ shadow depth $d \in \{2,3,4,\infty\}$.
The genus-$1$ Coisson invariant $c_0$ provides an
orthogonal classification: among the seven atlas families,
$c_0 = 0$ picks out exactly the abelian algebras
($\cH_k$ and $V_\Lambda$), while $c_0 \ne 0$ picks
out everything with a Lie bracket or symplectic pairing.
The combined invariant $(d, c_0)$ produces the
three-regime classification of
Theorem~\ref{thm:genus1-endomorphism-atlas}:
the genus-$0$ depth controls the bar-complex channel
(clean for $d < \infty$, excess for $d = \infty$),
and $c_0$ controls the propagator channel.
All four classes $\mathbf{G}$, $\mathbf{L}$,
$\mathbf{C}$, $\mathbf{M}$ are chirally Koszul (PBW
degeneration holds throughout the standard landscape).
What distinguishes class~$\mathbf{M}$ is
\emph{non-formality}: the higher $\Ainf$ operations
$m_{k \ge 3}$ are non-trivial on cohomology,
the bar-complex channel is activated by the excess
self-intersection, and shadow depth is infinite.
This is a measure of structural complexity within the
Koszul world, not a failure of Koszulness.
The two invariants are complementary: the genus-$0$ depth~$d$
determines the shadow obstruction tower architecture (how many $\Ainf$
operations are non-vanishing); the genus-$1$ Coisson bracket~$c_0$
determines whether that architecture is ``decoupled''
($c_0 = 0$: modular and spectral data independent) or
``entangled'' ($c_0 \ne 0$: modular and spectral data share
common algebraic sources, as in the Verlinde formula for
affine KM or the BTZ entropy for Virasoro).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The first modular coefficient and
question~\textup{(iii)} of the modular programme]%
\label{rem:modular-programme-genus1}%
\index{modular programme!first coefficient}%
\index{modular holography programme!genus 1}%
The period correction $F_1 = \kappa(\cA)/24$ is the
first genuinely modular coefficient requested in
question~(iii) of the modular holography programme
(Section~\ref{subsec:modular-holography-programme}).
In the Lagrangian picture, $F_1$ is the leading term
of the genus-$1$ self-intersection invariant
\[
R^{(1)}_\cA(z)
\;=\;
\chi\!\bigl(
 \cL_\cA^{(1)} \times_{\Mvac} \cL_\cA^{(1)}
\bigr)
\]
(Section~\ref{subsec:modular-holography-programme},
question~(iii$'$)). The three regimes of
Theorem~\ref{thm:genus1-endomorphism-atlas}
answer this question as follows:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},nosep]
\item \emph{Decoupled} ($c_0 = 0$):
 $R^{(1)}(z) = R^{(0)}(z)$. The genus-$1$
 Lagrangian self-intersection is trivially deformed;
 the Euler characteristic is unchanged. The only
 genus-$1$ effect is the scalar period correction
 $F_1 = \kappa/24$.

\item \emph{Propagator-entangled} ($c_0 \ne 0$, clean
 intersection):
 $R^{(1)}(z,\tau) = r^{E_\tau}(z)$ is the elliptic
 $r$-matrix~\eqref{eq:elliptic-r-matrix}, computed
 explicitly for all affine algebras and the
 $\beta\gamma$ system. The genus-$1$
 self-intersection carries additional monodromy
 $2\eta_\tau \cdot c_0$ from the $B$-cycle of
 $E_\tau$. The bar-complex channel is trivial in the
 genus-zero formal cases.

\item \emph{Doubly entangled} ($c_0 \ne 0$, excess
 intersection):
 $R^{(1)}(z,\tau)$ receives corrections from both
 channels. The propagator channel contributes the
 elliptic deformation; the bar-complex channel
 contributes corrections from the higher Swiss-cheese
 operations $m_{k \ge 3}$ (the wheel diagrams that
 source the infinite shadow obstruction tower). The algebra
 has non-formal Swiss-cheese structure (the transferred
 boundary operations $m_k^{\mathrm{SC}} \ne 0$ for all
 $k \ge 3$), though it is chirally Koszul and retains a
 well-defined Koszul dual ($\mathrm{Vir}_c^! = \mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$)
 carrying higher $\Ainf$ operations. Computing
 $R^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}(z,\tau)$ explicitly is
 the concrete test case for question~(iii) of the
 modular programme.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

\subsection{The complete E$_1$ ordered bar landscape}%
\label{subsec:e1-ordered-bar-landscape}%
\index{ordered bar complex!landscape table|textbf}%
\index{E1 landscape@$E_1$ landscape|textbf}

The preceding atlas tables
(Computations~\ref{comp:shadow-tower-atlas}
and~\ref{comp:genus1-atlas}) classify the standard
families by shadow depth and genus-$1$ invariants
separately. The following table assembles the
complete ordered bar landscape: all invariants of the
$\Eone$-coloured bar complex for every standard family,
in a single comparison.

\begin{computation}[Complete $\Eone$ ordered bar landscape;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:e1-ordered-bar-landscape}%
\index{ordered bar complex!landscape!master table}%
\index{depth spectrum!landscape}%
\index{R-matrix!landscape}%
\index{Koszul dual!landscape}%

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.5}
\setlength{\tabcolsep}{4pt}
\begin{tabular}{llccccccl}

 & $\ne 0$
 & (Part~\ref{part:e1-core}) \\

\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Reading the table.}
``Class'' is the shadow obstruction tower depth classification
(Definition~\ref{def:shadow-depth-intersection}).
``Depth'' is the set of cogenerator degrees minus one
(the depth spectrum of the ordered bar complex).
$R(z)$ is the spectral $R$-matrix on the fundamental
module (``non-closed'' means the $R$-matrix is
meromorphic but not closed-form as a single exponential).
$P(t)$ is the Poincar\'{e} series of the bar
cogenerators (counting bar cohomology generators by
desuspended degree).
$S_2^\dagger$ is the shadow Hessian
normalised as half the Virasoro central charge $c/2$
when the family has a Virasoro subalgebra or an
affine sub-sector (Heisenberg, lattice VOAs, affine KM,
Virasoro, $\cW_N$); for simple-pole families
($\psi$, $bc_\lambda$, $\beta\gamma$, symplectic bosons)
whose generator-level $S_2$ is the modular characteristic
$\kappa$, the table records $\kappa$. The dagger
distinguishes $S_2^\dagger$ from the Volume~I modular
characteristic $\kappa = \dim(\fg)(k{+}h^\vee)/(2h^\vee)$,
which differs for non-abelian families; e.g.\ for
$V_1(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$, $S_2^\dagger = 1/2$ but
$\kappa = 9/4$.
$c_0$ is the zeroth-product Coisson bracket
(the simple-pole OPE residue that controls genus-$1$
entanglement).

The table is organised by the three-tier $R$-matrix
classification
($\S$\ref{subsec:ordered-three-tier}).
All standard vertex algebra families are $\Einf$-chiral
(tier~(ii)): their $R$-matrices are derived from the
local OPE\@. Within tier~(ii), simple-pole families
($\psi$, $bc_\lambda$, $\beta\gamma$) have
generator-level $R = \tau$ or $\mathrm{Id}$
(the $d\log$ kernel absorbs the simple OPE pole to
a constant), while higher-pole families have genuinely
$z$-dependent $R(z)$. Wakimoto appears as a separate
row: the same algebra as $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ but
exhibiting the $R$-matrix product decomposition
$R_\cH \cdot R_{\beta\gamma}$ from the free-field
embedding. Tier~(iii) (genuinely $\Eone$-chiral)
is represented by the quantum vertex algebra $V_q(\fg)$;
the full treatment is in Part~\ref{part:e1-core}\@.
Within each tier, the shadow depth class
($\mathbf{G}$/$\mathbf{L}$/$\mathbf{C}$/$\mathbf{M}$)
and the genus-$1$ regime provide orthogonal cuts:

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item \emph{Finite formal} ($\mathbf{G}$, $\mathbf{L}$,
 $\mathbf{C}$): the bar complex is finitely cogenerated,
 the Swiss-cheese structure is formal at genus~$0$, and
 the Koszul dual has finitely many generators.
\item \emph{Infinite non-formal} ($\mathbf{M}$): the bar
 complex has infinitely many cogenerators
 (from composite-field exchange), the Swiss-cheese
 structure is non-formal, and the Koszul dual carries
 the full $\Ainf$ tower.
\item \emph{Genus-$1$ orthogonal cut}: within each class,
 $c_0 = 0$ gives decoupled genus-$1$ behaviour (only
 $\cH_k$ among the standard families), while $c_0 \ne 0$
 gives entangled behaviour (all other families).
\end{enumerate}
The Virasoro depth column $\{0,\ldots,n{-}1,n{+}1\}$ encodes the weight-depth identity $w + d = n - 1$ and the structural gap at $d = n$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)--(ii)); the $\cW_3$ depth column $\{0,\ldots,3,5\}$ reflects the gap migration $d_{\mathrm{gap}} = 2N + n - 4 = 4$ at degree~$2$ (part~(iv)).
\end{computation}

\subsection{Coset and orbifold bar complexes}%
\label{subsec:coset-orbifold-bar}%
\index{coset!ordered bar complex|textbf}%
\index{orbifold!ordered bar complex|textbf}%
\index{GKO coset!bar complex|textbf}%
\index{permutation orbifold!bar complex|textbf}

The standard families in the landscape table
(Computation~\ref{comp:e1-ordered-bar-landscape})
are all \emph{primitive}: each is a single vertex algebra, not
constructed from other vertex algebras by algebraic operations.
Two fundamental constructions produce new vertex algebras from
old: the \emph{coset} (commutant) and the \emph{orbifold}
(invariant subalgebra under a finite group).
Both are $\Einf$-chiral (they are vertex algebras, hence local),
and both have ordered bar complexes that are determined by, but
differ from, the bar complexes of their parent algebras.
This section computes the ordered bar complexes for the three
canonical constructions: the GKO coset, the $\Z_2$ lattice
orbifold, and the permutation orbifold.

\subsubsection{The GKO coset: bar complex of a commutant}%
\label{subsubsec:gko-coset-bar}%
\index{GKO coset!ordered bar complex|textbf}%
\index{coset!commutant!bar complex}%
\index{unitary minimal models!bar complex}

The Goddard--Kent--Olive coset construction starts from the
tensor product
$\cA := V_1(\mathfrak{sl}_2) \otimes V_{k-1}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$,
which carries the diagonal subalgebra
$V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2) \hookrightarrow \cA$
at the combined level $k = 1 + (k{-}1)$. The coset is the
commutant
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gko-coset-def}
\cC(k)
\;:=\;
\mathrm{Com}\bigl(
 V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2),\;
 V_1(\mathfrak{sl}_2) \otimes V_{k-1}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)
\bigr)\,,
\end{equation}
the subalgebra of~$\cA$ commuting with the diagonal currents.
For $k \ge 1$ integer, $\cC(k)$ is the unitary minimal model
$\cM(k+1, k+2)$ with central charge
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gko-central-charge}
c(k) \;=\; 1 - \frac{6}{(k+1)(k+2)}\,.
\end{equation}

\begin{computation}[GKO coset ordered bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:gko-coset-ordered-bar}%
\index{GKO coset!depth spectrum}%
\index{GKO coset!R-matrix}%
\index{unitary minimal models!Koszul dual}%
\index{GKO coset!genus 1}%
The commutant $\cC(k)$ is a Virasoro minimal model:
it is generated by the Virasoro field~$T$ (weight~$2$)
alone, with finitely many irreducible modules.
At $k = 1$: $\cC(1) \cong \C$ (trivial, $c = 0$).
At $k = 2$: $\cC(2) \cong \cM(3,4)$, the Ising model
($c = 1/2$, three irreducible modules).
At $k = 3$: $\cC(3) \cong \cM(4,5)$, the tricritical
Ising model ($c = 7/10$). The higher unitary minimal
models $\cM(k{+}1, k{+}2)$ for $k \ge 4$ are all
Virasoro algebras at irrational central charge
$c(k) < 1$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Depth spectrum and class.}
Since $\cC(k)$ is a Virasoro algebra at central charge
$c(k)$, the OPE is
$T(z)\,T(w) \sim (c/2)/(z-w)^4
+ 2T(w)/(z-w)^2 + \partial T(w)/(z-w)$,
with the characteristic fourth-order pole.
The bar complex inherits the Virasoro shadow obstruction tower:
class~$\mathbf{M}$, infinite shadow depth,
non-formal Swiss-cheese structure.
The shadow coefficients $S_r(\cC(k))$ are exactly the
Virasoro shadow coefficients
(Computation~\ref{comp:virasoro-shadow-tower})
evaluated at $c = c(k) = 1 - 6/((k{+}1)(k{+}2))$.
The denominators involve $c(k) \cdot (5c(k) + 22)^{\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor}$,
which is nonzero for all $k \ge 2$: the
Ising value $c = 1/2$ and Lee--Yang value $c = -22/5$
are the only potential poles, and $5c(k) + 22 \ne 0$
for $k \ge 2$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Operations: inherited from the tensor product.}
The embedding $\cC(k) \hookrightarrow \cA$ is a
morphism of vertex algebras, hence induces a chain map
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gko-bar-inclusion}
\iota_*\colon
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(\cC(k))
\;\longrightarrow\;
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(\cA)\,,
\end{equation}
and the image of $\iota_*$ consists of those bar elements
that commute with the diagonal $V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$-action.
Concretely, for bar degree~$n$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gko-bar-invariant}
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}_n(\cC(k))
\;\cong\;
\bigl\{
\xi \in \bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}_n(\cA)
\;\bigm|\;
J^a_{\mathrm{diag}} \cdot \xi = 0\;\;
\text{for all $a$}
\bigr\}\,,
\end{equation}
where $J^a_{\mathrm{diag}} = J^a_{(1)} + J^a_{(k-1)}$ are
the diagonal affine currents and the action is by the
coderivation extending the $V_k$-module structure on~$\cA$.
The bar differential $d_{\barBch}$ preserves this invariant
subspace (it is built from OPE residues of $\cC(k)$-fields,
which commute with~$J^a_{\mathrm{diag}}$). The coproduct
$\Delta$ also preserves invariance (it is a tensor
coalgebra operation on the ordering, not on the $\fg$-action).
Therefore $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(\cC(k))$ inherits the full
$E_1$ dg coalgebra structure from~$\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(\cA)$ by restriction to
invariants.

The bar complex of $\cC(k)$ is \emph{not} the quotient of
$\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(\cA)$ by the ideal generated by the
diagonal currents. Rather, it is the \emph{invariant
subcomplex}: the commutant is a subalgebra, not a quotient
algebra, and bar of a subalgebra is a sub-coalgebra.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Binary operation.}
At $k = 2$ (Ising model, $c = 1/2$), the single generator
is $T$ and the binary operation is
$m_2(T, T;\, \lambda) = (1/4)\lambda^3 + 2T\lambda
+ \partial T$.
This is the standard Virasoro $m_2$ at $c = 1/2$.
For $k = 2$, the GKO bar complex is isomorphic to
$\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(\mathrm{Vir}_{1/2})$, already
in the landscape as a specialisation of the Virasoro
row at $c = 1/2$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{$r$-matrix.}
The coset $r$-matrix is the restriction of the tensor
product $r$-matrix to the $V_k$-singlet sector.
For $\cA = V_1(\mathfrak{sl}_2) \otimes V_{k-1}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$,
the collision residue of the tensor product is
\[
r_\cA(z)
\;=\;
\frac{\Omega^{(1)}}{z}
\;+\;
\frac{\Omega^{(2)}}{z}\,,
\]
where $\Omega^{(1)}$ and $\Omega^{(2)}$ are the
$\mathfrak{sl}_2$ Casimirs acting on the first and
second tensor factors respectively (the levels $k = 1$
and $k - 1$ enter through the collision residues of the
individual factors). The coset $r$-matrix is the
projection to the diagonal $V_k$-singlet sector:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gko-r-matrix}
r_{\cC(k)}(z)
\;=\;
\mathrm{pr}_{\mathrm{sing}}
\circ\; r_\cA(z)
\;\circ\; \mathrm{incl}_{\mathrm{sing}}\,,
\end{equation}
where $\mathrm{pr}_{\mathrm{sing}}$ projects to
$\{v : J^a_{\mathrm{diag},0}\, v = 0\}$.
On minimal-model modules $L_{r,s}^{(k)}$ (classified
by the Kac table of $\cM(k{+}1, k{+}2)$), the $R$-matrix
is non-closed-form: it inherits the non-formal Virasoro
structure of the shadow obstruction tower at $c = c(k)$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Koszul dual.}
Since $\cC(k)$ is a Virasoro algebra at central
charge~$c(k)$, the Koszul dual is
$\cC(k)^! = \mathrm{Vir}_{26 - c(k)}$.
The complementarity constant is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gko-complementarity}
K(\cC(k))
\;=\;
\kappa(\cC(k)) + \kappa(\cC(k)^!)
\;=\;
\frac{c(k)}{2} + \frac{26 - c(k)}{2}
\;=\; 13\,,
\end{equation}
matching the universal Virasoro complementarity constant
$K = 13$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Modular characteristic.}
$\kappa(\cC(k)) = c(k)/2$
(the Virasoro value at central charge $c(k)$).
The genus-$1$ regime is entangled ($c_0 = \partial T \ne 0$).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Landscape entry.}
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabular}{llccccccl}
\toprule
\textbf{Family}
 & \textbf{Class}
 & \textbf{Depth}
 & $R(z)$
 & \textbf{Koszul dual}
 & $P(t)$
 & $\kappa$
 & $c_0$
 & \textbf{Genus-$1$} \\
\midrule
$\cC(2)$ (Ising)
 & $\mathbf{M}$
 & as Vir
 & non-closed
 & $\mathrm{Vir}_{25.5}$
 & $1{+}t$
 & $1/4$
 & $\ne 0$
 & entangled \\[3pt]
$\cC(k)$ ($k \ge 3$)
 & $\mathbf{M}$
 & as Vir
 & non-closed
 & $\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c(k)}$
 & $1{+}t$
 & $\frac{c(k)}{2}$
 & $\ne 0$
 & entangled \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{computation}

\begin{remark}[The coset bar complex as a relative construction]%
\label{rem:coset-relative-bar}%
\index{coset!relative bar complex}%
\index{relative bar complex!coset}%
The coset bar complex admits a relative interpretation.
The tensor product $\cA = V_1 \otimes V_{k-1}$ has bar
complex $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(\cA) \cong
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V_1) \otimes
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V_{k-1})$ (the K\"{u}nneth
isomorphism for ordered bar complexes of mutually
regular tensor products). The diagonal embedding
$V_k \hookrightarrow \cA$ defines a $V_k$-coaction
on $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(\cA)$, and the coset bar
complex is the \emph{relative cotensor}:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:coset-relative-cotensor}
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(\cC(k))
\;\simeq\;
\C \;\square_{\barBch(V_k)}^{\mathbf{R}}\;
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(\cA)\,,
\end{equation}
where the left factor $\C$ denotes the trivial
$\barBch(V_k)$-comodule (the coaugmentation) and the
derived cotensor $\square^{\mathbf{R}}$ is computed in
the coderived category. This is the bar-side avatar of
the commutant: the commutant algebra is the
$V_k$-invariant subalgebra; the commutant bar complex is
the $\barBch(V_k)$-coinvariant sub-coalgebra.

This relative presentation makes the GKO coset construction
functorial at the level of bar complexes: the coset map
$V_k \hookrightarrow \cA \twoheadleftarrow \cC(k)$ lifts
to a fiber sequence
$\barBch(\cC(k)) \to \barBch(\cA)
\to \barBch(V_k)$
in the category of conilpotent dg coalgebras.
\end{remark}


\subsubsection{The $\Z_2$ orbifold: bar complex of invariants}%
\label{subsubsec:z2-orbifold-bar}%
\index{orbifold!Z2@$\Z_2$!bar complex|textbf}%
\index{lattice VOA!orbifold|textbf}%
\index{orbifold!c=1 theory}

For a lattice VOA $V_\Lambda$ with an automorphism
$\sigma\colon V_\Lambda \to V_\Lambda$ of finite order,
the orbifold (or invariant) subalgebra $V_\Lambda^\sigma$ is
the fixed-point vertex algebra. The canonical example is the
$\Z_2$~orbifold of the $A_1$ lattice VOA.

\begin{computation}[$\Z_2$ orbifold ordered bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:z2-orbifold-ordered-bar}%
\index{orbifold!Z2@$\Z_2$!depth spectrum}%
\index{orbifold!Z2@$\Z_2$!R-matrix}%
\index{orbifold!Z2@$\Z_2$!Koszul dual}%
\index{orbifold!c=1 theory!bar complex}%
The lattice $\Lambda = \sqrt{2}\,\Z$ has lattice VOA
$V_\Lambda \cong L_1(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
(Computation~\ref{comp:lattice-voa-ordered-bar}).
The $\Z_2$ automorphism is the Cartan involution
$\sigma\colon J \mapsto -J$,
$e^\alpha \mapsto e^{-\alpha}$,
$e^{-\alpha} \mapsto e^{\alpha}$.
The fixed-point algebra is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:z2-orbifold-def}
V_\Lambda^{\Z_2}
\;=\;
\bigl\{v \in V_\Lambda \;\bigm|\; \sigma(v) = v\bigr\}\,.
\end{equation}
This is the $c = 1$ orbifold theory at the self-dual radius.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Generators.}
The $\Z_2$-invariant generators are:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item the Virasoro field
 $T = \tfrac{1}{2}\,{:}JJ{:}$
 (conformal weight~$2$, invariant since $\sigma(J^2) = (-J)^2 = J^2$);
\item the even vertex operator combinations
 $X^+ = e^\alpha + e^{-\alpha}$
 (weight~$1$, $\sigma(X^+) = e^{-\alpha} + e^\alpha = X^+$);
\item the bilinear $Y = {:}(e^\alpha)(e^{-\alpha}){:}$
 (weight~$2$, invariant).
\end{itemize}
The odd combination $X^- = e^\alpha - e^{-\alpha}$ has
$\sigma(X^-) = -X^-$ and is \emph{not} in $V_\Lambda^{\Z_2}$;
it generates the unique nontrivial twisted module.
The Heisenberg current $J$ itself satisfies $\sigma(J) = -J$,
so $J \notin V_\Lambda^{\Z_2}$. The orbifold algebra
does not contain the Heisenberg subalgebra; it is generated
by the Virasoro field, the invariant vertex operators, and
their composites.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Bar complex as invariant sub-coalgebra.}
The $\Z_2$-action on $V_\Lambda$ induces a $\Z_2$-action on
the ordered bar complex $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V_\Lambda)$
by the diagonal action on tensor factors:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:z2-bar-action}
\sigma\bigl[a_1 \,|\, \cdots \,|\, a_n\bigr]
\;=\;
[\sigma(a_1) \,|\, \cdots \,|\, \sigma(a_n)]\,.
\end{equation}
Since $\sigma$ is an automorphism of $V_\Lambda$, it
commutes with both the bar differential $d_{\barBch}$
(which is built from the OPE, preserved by automorphisms)
and the deconcatenation coproduct~$\Delta$ (which depends
only on the tensor ordering). Therefore:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:z2-orbifold-bar}
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V_\Lambda^{\Z_2})
\;\cong\;
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V_\Lambda)^{\Z_2}\,,
\end{equation}
the $\Z_2$-invariant sub-coalgebra of the lattice bar complex.
Both the bar differential and the deconcatenation coproduct restrict to
the invariant subspace.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Depth spectrum: $\{1, 2, \ldots\}$, class~$\mathbf{M}$.}
The orbifold algebra $V_\Lambda^{\Z_2}$ contains the
Virasoro field~$T$ of conformal weight~$2$ with the
fourth-order OPE at $c = 1$. The Virasoro subalgebra
forces class~$\mathbf{M}$, infinite shadow depth, and
non-formal Swiss-cheese structure, the same mechanism
as for any algebra containing a Virasoro sub-sector.
This represents a depth \emph{increase} relative to the
parent: $V_\Lambda \cong L_1(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ is
class~$\mathbf{L}$ (depth~$3$), but $V_\Lambda^{\Z_2}$
is class~$\mathbf{M}$ because the Sugawara construction
$T = \tfrac{1}{2}\,{:}JJ{:}$ introduces the fourth-order
pole.

The mechanism is: the orbifold removes the
simple-pole generator~$J$ (which is odd under $\sigma$)
but retains its quadratic composite $T = \tfrac{1}{2}{:}JJ{:}$,
which has a fourth-order self-OPE. The orbifold
trades a class-$\mathbf{L}$ generating set
$\{J, e^\alpha, e^{-\alpha}\}$ for a class-$\mathbf{M}$
generating set $\{T, X^+, Y\}$. The DS
depth-jump mechanism
(Computation~\ref{comp:w3-shadow-tower})
is at work here in a different guise: passing from
$V_\Lambda$ to $V_\Lambda^{\Z_2}$ replaces generators
by composites, just as the DS reduction
$V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_3) \to \cW_3$ replaces currents
by the Sugawara field and its partners.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Operations: $m_2$ on invariant generators.}
On the generator $X^+ = e^\alpha + e^{-\alpha}$:
\begin{align}
m_2(X^+, X^+;\, \lambda)
&\;=\;
m_2(e^\alpha{+}e^{-\alpha},\, e^\alpha{+}e^{-\alpha};\, \lambda)
\notag
\\[4pt]
&\;=\;
\underbrace{m_2(e^\alpha, e^{-\alpha};\, \lambda)
+ m_2(e^{-\alpha}, e^\alpha;\, \lambda)}_{\text{cross terms}}
\;+\;
\underbrace{m_2(e^\alpha, e^\alpha;\, \lambda)
+ m_2(e^{-\alpha}, e^{-\alpha};\, \lambda)}_{ = 0}
\notag
\\[4pt]
&\;=\;
(\lambda + \alpha \cdot J)
+ (\lambda - \alpha \cdot J)
\;=\;
2\lambda\,,
\label{eq:z2-orbifold-m2-xplus}
\end{align}
using the lattice OPE~\eqref{eq:lattice-vertex-ope}
and the vanishing~\eqref{eq:lattice-vertex-vertex-vanishing}.
The Lie-bracket terms $\pm\alpha \cdot J$ cancel in
the invariant sector because $J$ is $\sigma$-odd.
On the Virasoro field $T$, the binary operation is
the standard Virasoro $m_2$ at $c = 1$:
$m_2(T, T;\, \lambda) = \tfrac{1}{2}\lambda^3
+ 2T\lambda + \partial T$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{$r$-matrix.}
The orbifold $r$-matrix is the restriction of the parent
$r$-matrix to the $\sigma$-invariant sector:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:z2-orbifold-r-matrix}
r_{V^{\Z_2}}(z)
\;=\;
\mathrm{pr}_{\sigma = +1}\;\circ\;
r_{V_\Lambda}(z)
\;\circ\;
\mathrm{incl}_{\sigma = +1}\,.
\end{equation}
On the $\sigma$-invariant modules of $V_\Lambda^{\Z_2}$, the
Casimir $\Omega_{\mathfrak{sl}_2}$ projects to the
$\sigma$-invariant part. The off-diagonal components
$(e^\alpha \otimes e^{-\alpha} + e^{-\alpha} \otimes e^\alpha)$
contribute; the Cartan component $\tfrac{1}{2} J \otimes J$
does not (it is odd--odd $= $ even, so it contributes).
The restricted $r$-matrix is non-closed form:
$r_{V^{\Z_2}}(z)$ is a meromorphic function of~$z$
with poles, but the projection to the $\Z_2$-invariant
subspace of $\End(M_1 \otimes M_2)$ produces a truncated
Casimir.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Koszul dual.}
The Koszul dual $(V_\Lambda^{\Z_2})^!$ is not the
$\Z_2$-invariant part of $Y_{1/3}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
(the Koszul dual of the parent). Rather, it is a distinct
object: the orbifold Koszul dual, determined by the bar
complex $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V_\Lambda^{\Z_2})
= \bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V_\Lambda)^{\Z_2}$.
Since the orbifold is class~$\mathbf{M}$, the Koszul dual
carries the full infinite $\Ainf$ tower.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Genus-$1$.}
The orbifold partition function is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:z2-orbifold-partition}
Z_1(V_\Lambda^{\Z_2})
\;=\;
\frac{1}{2}\biggl(
\frac{|\Theta_\Lambda(\tau)|^2}{|\eta(\tau)|^2}
\;+\;
\biggl|\frac{\eta(\tau)}{\theta_2(\tau)}\biggr|
\;+\;
\biggl|\frac{\eta(\tau)}{\theta_4(\tau)}\biggr|
\;+\;
\biggl|\frac{\eta(\tau)}{\theta_3(\tau)}\biggr|
\biggr)\,,
\end{equation}
the standard orbifold modular-invariant partition function
(the $D_4$ modular invariant of $\widehat{\mathfrak{su}}(2)_1$,
not to be confused with the $D_4$ lattice VOA of
Computation~\ref{comp:lattice-voa-D4-ordered-bar}).
The genus-$1$ regime is entangled
($c_0 \ne 0$ from the Virasoro subalgebra).
The shadow Hessian is $S_2 = c/2 = 1/2$.
\end{computation}


\begin{remark}[Orbifold depth jump: L $\to$ M by composite generation]%
\label{rem:orbifold-depth-jump}%
\index{orbifold!depth jump}%
\index{depth jump!orbifold}%
\index{shadow depth!orbifold increase}%
The $\Z_2$ orbifold of $V_{\sqrt{2}\Z}$ exhibits a
\emph{depth jump}: the parent algebra is class~$\mathbf{L}$
(depth~$3$) but the orbifold is class~$\mathbf{M}$
(depth~$\infty$). The mechanism is the same as the
DS reduction depth jump
(Computation~\ref{comp:w3-shadow-tower}):
passing to invariants removes simple-pole generators
and replaces them with their quadratic composites,
which carry fourth-order poles. The DS reduction
$V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_3) \to \cW_3$ removes currents and
introduces $T = T_{\mathrm{Sug}}$; the $\Z_2$ orbifold
removes $J$ and retains $T = \tfrac{1}{2}\,{:}JJ{:}$.
Both are instances of a general principle: \emph{passing to
invariants under a reductive group action can only
increase shadow depth, never decrease it}, because the
invariant algebra is generated by composites whose
pole orders are bounded below by the pole orders of the
parent generators, and composite fields generically have
higher pole orders.
\end{remark}


\subsubsection{The permutation orbifold: bar complex of the symmetric product}%
\label{subsubsec:permutation-orbifold-bar}%
\index{permutation orbifold!bar complex|textbf}%
\index{symmetric product!bar complex|textbf}%
\index{orbifold!permutation!bar complex}

Given a vertex algebra~$V$ and a positive integer~$n$,
the permutation orbifold is the $S_n$-invariant subalgebra
\begin{equation}\label{eq:perm-orbifold-def}
V^{(n)}
\;:=\;
(V^{\otimes n})^{S_n}\,,
\end{equation}
where $S_n$ acts by permuting the tensor factors.
The permutation orbifold is an $\Einf$-chiral algebra
(a vertex algebra) for any choice of~$V$.

\begin{computation}[Permutation orbifold ordered bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{comp:permutation-orbifold-bar}%
\index{permutation orbifold!depth spectrum}%
\index{permutation orbifold!symmetric product formula}%
\index{permutation orbifold!Koszul dual}%
\index{symmetric product!bar complex!explicit}%

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Tensor product bar complex.}
For mutually regular vertex algebras $V_1, \ldots, V_n$
(no singular cross-OPE), the ordered bar complex of the
tensor product satisfies the K\"{u}nneth isomorphism:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:tensor-product-bar}
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V_1 \otimes \cdots \otimes V_n)
\;\cong\;
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V_1)
\otimes \cdots \otimes
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V_n)\,,
\end{equation}
with the bar differential acting as the sum of
individual bar differentials and the coproduct as
the product of individual coproducts. For $n$~copies
of the same algebra $V$:
$\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V^{\otimes n})
\cong \bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V)^{\otimes n}$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Permutation action.}
The $S_n$-action on $V^{\otimes n}$ permutes the tensor
factors: $\sigma(v_1 \otimes \cdots \otimes v_n)
= v_{\sigma^{-1}(1)} \otimes \cdots \otimes v_{\sigma^{-1}(n)}$.
This induces an $S_n$-action on the bar complex:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:perm-bar-action}
\sigma\bigl[a_1^{(i_1)} \,|\, \cdots \,|\, a_m^{(i_m)}\bigr]
\;=\;
[a_1^{(\sigma(i_1))} \,|\, \cdots \,|\, a_m^{(\sigma(i_m))}]\,,
\end{equation}
where the superscript $(i)$ records which tensor factor
the generator belongs to. The bar differential and
coproduct commute with this action (the OPE of
$V^{\otimes n}$ permutes with the tensor factor labels,
and the deconcatenation coproduct depends only on the
bar ordering, not on the tensor factor labels).
Therefore:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:perm-orbifold-bar}
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V^{(n)})
\;\cong\;
\bigl(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch,ord}}(V)^{\otimes n}\bigr)^{S_n}\,,
\end{equation}
the $S_n$-invariant sub-coalgebra of the $n$-fold tensor
product of bar complexes. This is the ordered bar complex
analogue of the symmetric product.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Structure of the invariant sub-coalgebra.}
The invariant bar complex~\eqref{eq:perm-orbifold-bar}
is \emph{not} the symmetric tensor product
$\mathrm{Sym}^n(\barBch(V))$ (which would be the
$S_n$-coinvariants, a quotient). It is the
$S_n$-\emph{invariants}, a subcoalgebra. In
characteristic~$0$, the norm map
$N = \sum_{\sigma \in S_n} \sigma$ provides a splitting
$(\barBch(V)^{\otimes n})^{S_n}
\hookrightarrow \barBch(V)^{\otimes n}
\twoheadrightarrow (\barBch(V)^{\otimes n})_{S_n}$,
and the invariants and coinvariants are isomorphic. The
permutation orbifold bar complex is therefore isomorphic
to the symmetric product of bar complexes.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Generators of the invariant bar complex.}
The invariant generators are the symmetrised
bar elements:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:perm-bar-generators}
[a]_{\mathrm{sym}}^{(n)}
\;:=\;
\frac{1}{n!}\sum_{\sigma \in S_n}
\sigma\bigl[a^{(1)}\bigr]
\;=\;
\frac{1}{n!}\sum_{i=1}^{n}
[a^{(i)}]\,,
\end{equation}
for each generator~$a$ of~$V$.
The bar complex of $V^{(n)}$ also contains
\emph{multi-factor} invariants, i.e.\ bar elements
involving generators from distinct tensor factors
$[a^{(i)} \,|\, b^{(j)}]$ with $i \ne j$, symmetrised
over~$S_n$.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Depth spectrum and class.}
The shadow depth of $V^{(n)}$ depends on $V$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item If $V$ is class~$\mathbf{G}$ (e.g.\ $\cH_k$):
 each copy contributes only $m_2$, and the tensor
 product remains class~$\mathbf{G}$. Since
 $S_n$-invariants preserve the class (no new composites
 arise from symmetrisation of abelian generators),
 $V^{(n)}$ is class~$\mathbf{G}$.

\item If $V$ is class~$\mathbf{L}$ (e.g.\ $V_k(\fg)$):
 the single-factor bar differential has $m_3 \ne 0$.
 Symmetrised multi-factor elements
 $[a^{(i)} \,|\, b^{(j)} \,|\, c^{(i)}]$ with
 $i \ne j$ give new cross-factor $m_3$ terms, but
 the Jacobi identity still kills $m_4$ (the Jacobi
 mechanism operates within each factor and the cross-factor
 terms cannot generate fourth-order poles).
 $V^{(n)}$ remains class~$\mathbf{L}$.

\item If $V$ is class~$\mathbf{M}$
 (e.g.\ $\mathrm{Vir}_c$):
 the full infinite shadow obstruction tower of each copy is
 inherited by the tensor product and hence by the
 invariants. $V^{(n)}$ is class~$\mathbf{M}$.
 The Sugawara-like field
 $T_{\mathrm{tot}} = T^{(1)} + \cdots + T^{(n)}$
 at central charge~$nc$ provides the class-$\mathbf{M}$
 generator for the permutation orbifold.
\end{enumerate}

In every case, the permutation orbifold preserves or
inherits the shadow depth class of the parent. There
is no depth jump, because the $S_n$-invariant subalgebra
of a tensor product does not create new composite fields
that were absent in the parent: the composites within each
factor are already present, and the cross-factor composites
are products (not genuinely new composites in the OPE
sense).

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Modular characteristic.}
The modular characteristic is additive on tensor products:
$\kappa(V^{\otimes n}) = n\,\kappa(V)$. The orbifold
does not change the modular characteristic
(it is a subalgebra at the same central charge):
\begin{equation}\label{eq:perm-kappa}
\kappa(V^{(n)}) \;=\; n\,\kappa(V)\,.
\end{equation}

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{$r$-matrix.}
The $r$-matrix of the tensor product is the sum of the
individual $r$-matrices:
$r_{V^{\otimes n}}(z) = \sum_{i=1}^{n} r_V^{(i)}(z)$,
where $r_V^{(i)}$ acts on the $i$-th tensor factor.
The orbifold $r$-matrix is the $S_n$-symmetrisation:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:perm-r-matrix}
r_{V^{(n)}}(z)
\;=\;
\mathrm{pr}_{S_n}\;\circ\;
\biggl(\sum_{i=1}^{n} r_V^{(i)}(z)\biggr)
\;\circ\; \mathrm{incl}_{S_n}\,,
\end{equation}
projected to the $S_n$-invariant sector.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Koszul dual.}
For mutually regular tensor products, the Koszul dual
distributes: $(V_1 \otimes V_2)^! \simeq V_1^! \otimes V_2^!$.
For the permutation orbifold:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:perm-koszul-dual}
(V^{(n)})^!
\;\simeq\;
\bigl((V^!)^{\otimes n}\bigr)^{S_n}
\;=\;
(V^!)^{(n)}\,.
\end{equation}
Koszul duality commutes with the permutation orbifold:
the Koszul dual of the orbifold is the orbifold of
the Koszul dual. For $V = \cH_k$:
$((\cH_k)^{(n)})^! \simeq
(\mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*))^{(n)}$.
For $V = V_1(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$:
$((V_1(\mathfrak{sl}_2))^{(n)})^! \simeq
(Y_{1/3}(\mathfrak{sl}_2))^{(n)}$, the $S_n$-invariant
subalgebra of the $n$-fold Yangian tensor product.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Genus-$1$ partition function.}
The genus-$1$ partition function of the permutation orbifold
is related to the parent by the DMVV formula:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:dmvv}
\sum_{n \ge 0} p^n\, Z_1(V^{(n)};\, \tau)
\;=\;
\prod_{m > 0,\, \ell \in \Z}
\bigl(1 - p^m\, q^\ell\bigr)^{-c_{m\ell}}\,,
\end{equation}
where $q = e^{2\pi i\tau}$ and $c_{m\ell}$ are the
Fourier coefficients of $Z_1(V;\, \tau)$. This is the
generating function for symmetric orbifolds, first
established by Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde.
In the bar-complex language, the DMVV formula is the
statement that the generating function of Euler
characteristics of the symmetric product of bar
complexes reproduces the infinite-product side
of~\eqref{eq:dmvv}.

\smallskip
\noindent
\emph{Landscape entries.}
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabular}{llccccccl}
\toprule
\textbf{Family}
 & \textbf{Class}
 & \textbf{Depth}
 & $R(z)$
 & \textbf{Koszul dual}
 & $P(t)$
 & $S_2^\dagger$
 & $c_0$
 & \textbf{Genus-$1$} \\
\midrule
$\cH_k^{(n)}$
 & $\mathbf{G}$
 & $\{1\}$
 & $e^{nk\hbar/z}$
 & $(\mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}})^{(n)}$
 & $1{+}nt$
 & $n/2$
 & $0$
 & decoupled \\[3pt]
$V_k(\fg)^{(n)}$
 & $\mathbf{L}$
 & $\{1,2\}$
 & $\mathrm{pr}_{S_n}\circ R_{\fg}^{\oplus n}$
 & $(Y_\hbar(\fg))^{(n)}$
 & $1{+}n\dim(\fg)\,t$
 & $\frac{n\dim(\fg)k}{2(k{+}h^\vee)}$
 & $\ne 0$
 & entangled \\[3pt]
$\mathrm{Vir}_c^{(n)}$
 & $\mathbf{M}$
 & $\infty$
 & non-closed
 & Vir-Yangian${}^{(n)}$
 & $1{+}nt$
 & $nc/2$
 & $\ne 0$
 & entangled \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{computation}

\begin{remark}[The three constructions compared]%
\label{rem:coset-orbifold-comparison}%
\index{coset!comparison with orbifold}%
\index{orbifold!comparison with coset}%
\index{permutation orbifold!comparison}%
The three constructions (coset, $\Z_2$ orbifold,
permutation orbifold) exhibit contrasting effects on the
ordered bar complex:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item \emph{Coset} (commutant of a subalgebra):
 the bar complex is a \emph{relative cotensor}, a
 sub-coalgebra of the parent bar complex cut out by
 the diagonal action. The depth class depends on the
 structure of the commutant: the GKO coset produces
 class~$\mathbf{M}$ (Virasoro-like) from a
 class-$\mathbf{L}$ tensor product.

\item \emph{Finite-group orbifold} ($G$-invariants):
 the bar complex is the $G$-invariant sub-coalgebra.
 The depth class can \emph{jump upward}: the $\Z_2$
 orbifold of the $A_1$ lattice VOA jumps from
 class~$\mathbf{L}$ to class~$\mathbf{M}$, because
 the invariant subalgebra is generated by composites
 (the Sugawara field) that carry higher pole orders
 than the original generators.

\item \emph{Permutation orbifold} ($S_n$-invariants of
 tensor product): the bar complex is the $S_n$-invariant
 sub-coalgebra of the $n$-fold bar tensor product.
 The depth class is \emph{preserved}: no new composite
 fields arise from the symmetrisation. The Koszul dual
 commutes with the construction:
 $(V^{(n)})^! \simeq (V^!)^{(n)}$.
\end{enumerate}
The common thread: all three produce the bar complex of
the new algebra as a sub-coalgebra (invariants or
relative cotensor) of a parent bar complex, not as a
quotient. The bar functor, being a coalgebra functor,
sends subalgebras to sub-coalgebras. The depth class
can increase (when invariants force generation by
higher-pole composites) but cannot decrease (the
invariant sub-coalgebra inherits all obstructions of
the parent).
\end{remark}


\subsection{The all-genera generating function}%
\label{subsec:all-genera-generating}%
\index{genus tower!generating function|textbf}%
\index{A-hat genus@$\hat{A}$-genus!as Lagrangian expansion|textbf}

The genus-$1$ atlas is the first page of an
all-genera story. The scalar period corrections
$F_g(\cA) = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ (Volume~I, Theorem~D\textsubscript{scal})
extend the genus-$1$ datum $F_1 = \kappa/24$ to
all genera via the Faber--Pandharipande intersection
numbers
\begin{equation}\label{eq:faber-pandharipande}
\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}
\;=\;
\frac{2^{2g-1} - 1}{2^{2g-1}}
\;\cdot\;
\frac{|B_{2g}|}{(2g)!}\,,
\qquad g \ge 1,
\end{equation}
where $B_{2g}$ are the Bernoulli numbers. The
first five values:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{cccccc}
\toprule
$g$ & $1$ & $2$ & $3$ & $4$ & $5$ \\
\midrule
$\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ &
 $\dfrac{1}{24}$ &
 $\dfrac{7}{5{,}760}$ &
 $\dfrac{31}{967{,}680}$ &
 $\dfrac{127}{154{,}828{,}800}$ &
 $\dfrac{73}{3{,}503{,}554{,}560}$ \\[6pt]
$F_g(\cH_1)$ &
 $\dfrac{1}{24}$ &
 $\dfrac{7}{5{,}760}$ &
 $\dfrac{31}{967{,}680}$ &
 $\dfrac{127}{154{,}828{,}800}$ &
 $\dfrac{73}{3{,}503{,}554{,}560}$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\begin{theorem}[The genus tower as $\hat{A}$-genus;
\ClaimStatusProvedElsewhere]%
\label{thm:ahat-lagrangian}%
\index{A-hat genus@$\hat{A}$-genus!generating function}% On the scalar lane, the total scalar free energy of the endomorphism algebra
$\End(\cL_\cA)$ expanded over $\coprod_g \Mbar_g$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:total-free-energy}
\boxed{
F^{\mathrm{tot}}(\cA;\, \hbar)
\;=\;
\frac{\kappa(\cA)}{\hbar^2}
\;\cdot\;
\frac{\hbar/2}{\sin(\hbar/2)}\,,
}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ahat-series}
\frac{x/2}{\sin(x/2)}
\;=\;
1 + \frac{x^2}{24} + \frac{7\, x^4}{5760}
 + \frac{31\, x^6}{967680} + \cdots
\;=\;
\sum_{g \ge 0}
 \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}\, x^{2g}
\end{equation}
is the generating function for the unsigned
Faber--Pandharipande numbers
\textup{(}Volume~I,
Theorem~D\textsubscript{scal}\textup{)},
related to the Hirzebruch $\hat{A}$-class by
$\hat{A}(ix) = (x/2)/\sin(x/2)$, the Wick rotation
that turns the alternating-sign $\hat{A}$-series into
the all-positive genus expansion.
The scalar genus-$g$ contribution is
$F_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}} \cdot
\hbar^{2g-2}$ ,
with $\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}} > 0$
for all $g \ge 1$. For arbitrary modular Koszul algebras, the
unconditional scalar statement is the genus-$1$ identity
$F_1 = \kappa/24$ (all-weight at $g = 1$; the
cross-channel correction starts at $g \ge 2$).
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[The platonic content]%
\label{rem:ahat-platonic}%
\index{platonic ideal!A-hat genus@$\hat{A}$-genus}%
Equation~\eqref{eq:total-free-energy} is the platonic
content of the genus tower. The Lagrangian
$\cL_\cA \hookrightarrow \Mvac$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:holographic-reconstruction-conclusion})
is a point in the derived symplectic category. Its formal
neighborhood over $\coprod_g \Mbar_g$ is the
$\hbar$-expansion of the endomorphism algebra. The
generating function of this expansion is
$(x/2)/\sin(x/2) = \hat{A}(ix)$, the Wick-rotated
$\hat{A}$-class, the same generating function that,
after rotation back, governs the index theorem for
Dirac operators. The single scalar $\kappa(\cA)$ (the
modular characteristic) plays the role of the curvature;
$\hbar$ plays the role of the genus parameter.

On the scalar lane, the coefficients of
$(\hbar/2)/\sin(\hbar/2)$ describe the scalar genus tower.
The genus-$0$ constant term produces the flat $E_1$
coalgebra; the genus-$1$ correction ($+\hbar^2/24$) produces
the curved $E_1$ coalgebra scalar term with curvature
$\kappa \cdot \omega_1$; the genus-$2$ correction
($+7\hbar^4/5760$) gives the next scalar coefficient over
$\Mbar_2$; and so on. Outside that scalar lane, the
monograph also carries genus dependence through
higher-degree shadow data and other non-scalar structures,
so the full genus content is not exhausted by a single
coefficient $F_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ .
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The Witten genus]%
\label{rem:ahat-witten-genus}%
\index{Witten genus!relation to genus tower}%
The Witten genus characteristic series is
\[
 \varphi_W(x)
 \;=\;
 \frac{x/2}{\sinh(x/2)}
 \;\prod_{n \ge 1}
 \frac{(1 - q^n e^x)(1 - q^n e^{-x})}{(1 - q^n)^2}\,,
\]
where $q = e^{2\pi i\tau}$. At $q = 0$ the product
is~$1$ and $\varphi_W(x)|_{q=0} = (x/2)/\sinh(x/2)
= \hat{A}(x)$.
Under the Wick rotation $x \mapsto ix$ that converts
the alternating-sign $\hat{A}$-series into the
all-positive genus expansion
(Theorem~\ref{thm:ahat-lagrangian}), this becomes
$\hat{A}(ix) = (x/2)/\sin(x/2)$, so the
generating function~\eqref{eq:ahat-series} is the
$q^0$~term of $\varphi_W(ix)$.

The higher $q$-powers are supplied by
the Eisenstein-weighted genus-$1$ corrections of
Remark~\ref{rem:eisenstein-weighted-genus1}:
on an elliptic curve~$E_\tau$, each pole of
order~$2k$ in the OPE generates a correction weighted
by the Eisenstein series~$E_{2k}(\tau)$
(equation~\eqref{eq:modular-propagator-coeffs}).
The Witten genus $\Phi_W \colon
\Omega^{\mathrm{String}}_\ast \to \mathrm{MF}_\ast$
factors through topological modular forms via the
Ando--Hopkins--Rezk string orientation
$\sigma \colon M\mathrm{String} \to \mathit{tmf}$,
and $\mathit{tmf}$ is assembled from
elliptic cohomology theories
of chromatic height~${\le}\, 2$.
The scalar genus tower~\eqref{eq:total-free-energy}
is the rational shadow of this height-$2$ invariant.

The rational truncation to $q^0$ breaks $S$-invariance:
$(x/2)/\sin(x/2)$ transforms with anomalous weight
$-\kappa/2$ under $\tau \mapsto -1/\tau$
(\S\ref{obs:genus-tower-wick-anomaly}).
The higher $q$-powers (the Eisenstein-weighted
corrections of the preceding paragraph) are
precisely the elliptic completion that restores it,
promoting the genus tower from a rational shadow
into the modular Witten genus.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Shadow corrections and the departure from
$\hat{A}$]%
\label{rem:shadow-corrections-ahat}%
\index{shadow corrections!departure from $\hat{A}$}%
The free energy~\eqref{eq:total-free-energy} is the
\emph{scalar} part of the Lagrangian expansion: it
captures the scalar period corrections on the proved
scalar lane. For class~$\mathbf{G}$ algebras,
this scalar term is the complete answer: the shadow obstruction tower
terminates at degree~$2$. For classes~$\mathbf{L}$ and
$\mathbf{C}$, the scalar term is accompanied by finitely
many non-scalar shadow corrections, reflecting
$r_{\max}=3$ and $r_{\max}=4$ respectively.

For algebras with excess self-intersection
(class~$\mathbf{M}$: Virasoro, $\cW_N$), the full
genus-$g$ endomorphism algebra carries an infinite tower
of higher-degree shadow corrections
(Computation~\ref{comp:virasoro-shadow-tower}). These
shadow corrections are the \emph{dispersive}
corrections to the genus tower, the same corrections
that appear in the Dubrovin--Zhang hierarchy as
higher-order terms beyond the dispersionless limit.
The $\hat{A}$-genus is the dispersionless approximation;
the shadow obstruction tower provides the higher-degree dispersive
completion.

For class~$\mathbf{M}$, the denominators of the shadow
coefficients $S_r$
(Computation~\ref{comp:virasoro-shadow-tower}) involve the
Kac determinants $\det M_r$: the self-intersection
degenerates where the algebra degenerates. These
are the poles of the Lagrangian deformation over the
moduli of curves, the locus where the endomorphism
algebra fails to be a flat deformation.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[From one page to the book]%
\label{rem:atlas-continuation}%
\index{genus tower!atlas continuation}%
The genus-$1$ atlas
(Theorem~\ref{thm:genus1-endomorphism-atlas}) classifies
the first-order deformation by the triple
$(\kappa, c_0, d)$. At genus~$g \ge 2$, the period
correction on the scalar lane,
$F_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ (equation~\eqref{eq:faber-pandharipande}),
extends the scalar atlas on that lane. Beyond it, new
genus-$g$ information also enters through higher-degree
shadow data. The geometric genus-$g$ data
enters through the period matrix $\Omega_{ij}$ of
$\Sigma_g$, which replaces the single modular parameter
$\tau$ of $E_\tau$: the elliptic $r$-matrix of
Section~\ref{subsec:affine-genus1-endomorphism} becomes
a function on the Jacobian of $\Sigma_g$, and the
$B$-cycle monodromy $2\eta_\tau \cdot c_0$ becomes a
$g \times g$ matrix of quasi-periods.

The genus-$0$ atlas classifies the point;
the genus-$1$ atlas classifies the first-order
deformation; on the scalar lane the
$\hat{A}$-genus generates the all-genera scalar
expansion; and the shadow obstruction tower
provides the dispersive corrections. The modular
programme
(Section~\ref{subsec:modular-holography-programme})
is the problem of computing the complete dispersive
expansion at all genera for all standard families.
\end{remark}
